=== page 4 ===
N
Nulb is a haven for Brigands and cultists
ulb is a haven for outlaws, cultists, and
criminals, located at the eastern edge of
the Viscounty of Verbobonc, bordered by
the Gnarley Forest and the Fens of Tor.
It’s a place where law is loosely enforced
and commerce thrives on illegal activity.
Despite its squalor and danger, the
village serves as a key stop along the High/Forest Road.
Arrival at the Bridge of Nulb
The Low Road winds through the southern reaches of the
Fens of Tor, where fetid marshlands form a natural barrier
between the fertile fields of Verbobonc and the shadowy
expanse of the Gnarley Forest. The road narrows as it nears
a dilapidated stone bridge spanning the sluggish waters of
the Imeryds Run. The air is heavy with the stench of stagnant
water, decaying vegetation, and woodsmoke curling from the
distant hovels of Nulb.
At the foot of the bridge, a leaning guardhouse stands
sentinel, its rotting timbers defying both time and tide.
Faded and tattered banners dangle limply in the humid air,
their once-proud sigils obscured by grime. The guardhouse
emits faint sounds—muted laughter, gruff voices, and the
occasional clink of metal—suggesting the men posted here
are less vigilant watchmen and more opportunistic rogues.
Two figures in mismatched armor linger at the
guardhouse entrance, their eyes sharp and unwelcoming.
One spits into the mud as the other rests a hand on the hilt
of a rusted blade. A third figure leans against the bridge
railing, chewing on a stalk of swamp grass and eyeing
travelers with the casual menace of someone unafraid of
conflict.
Across the river, the heart of Nulb spreads out in grim
disarray. The market square lies just beyond the bridge, a
cluster of crooked, uneven buildings huddled together like
scavengers around a fresh kill. To the left, the river bay
cradles a collection of decrepit docks where shadowy figures
and ramshackle boats move about under the watchful eye of
looming pirate ships. To the right, the Imeryds Run snakes
northward, its dark waters skirting the edge of town and
vanishing into the gloom of the Gnarley Forest.
The village itself seems shrouded in a pall of smoke and
decay. Its sagging rooftops and leaning chimneys speak of
neglect, while the ominous air of lawlessness emanates from
every shadow. Even from this distance, Nulb exudes an aura
of menace, a place where survival hinges on strength,
cunning, and the willingness to do what others will not.
“This is Nulb, stranger. Where the strong take, the
cunning thrive, and the foolish vanish into the swamp.”
– Grizzled dockworker at the River Docks.
Demographics of Nulb (576 CY)
Population: ~350-400
Humans: 65% (~230) Predominantly Oeridian and
Suel backgrounds, with some Flan. Includes
outlaws, laborers, pirates, and smugglers.
Half-Orcs: 15% (~60) Often serving as enforcers,
bodyguards, or mercenaries. Strong presence among
the pirate and bandit factions.
Elves and Half-Elves: 5% (~20) Drifters, exiles, and
opportunists, often mistrusted by others.
Halflings: 3% (~10) Merchants or spies who use their
unassuming nature to gather intelligence.
Occupational Breakdown
Pirates and Riverfolk: 90 (~25%)
Centered around the docks and ships like The Iron
Dagger.
Bandits and Outlaws: 80 (~20%)
Operate from hidden camps in nearby woods or
blend into Nulb’s population.
Cultists and Agents: 50 (~12%)
Loyal to the Temple of Elemental Evil, serving
various elemental factions.
Commoners: 60 (~15%)
Laborers, farmers, and tradespeople eking out a
living in the harsh conditions.
Adventurers and Freelancers: 20 (~5%)
Drift through Nulb seeking profit or information.
Merchants and Smugglers: 40 (~10%)
Handle trade and black-market goods, often under
the shadow of pirate crews or the Temple.
Enforcers and Guards: 30 (~8%)
Madame Selentis and her Temple-appointed guards.
Well-armed and disciplined, they are seen patrolling
near the Old Mayor’s Manor, Nulb docks and bridge.
Key Observations
Transient Population: Many inhabitants view Nulb
as a temporary refuge or staging ground for illicit
activities.
Lack of Unity: Factions constantly vie for dominance,
ensuring a volatile and dangerous environment.
Strategic Location: Proximity to the Imeryds Run
and the Fens of Tor makes Nulb an important hub
for smuggling, piracy, and covert operations. {{}}

=== page 5 ===
DM Spotlight: Campaign
Lawlessness and Power Struggles
Nulb remains a nest of anarchy and violence, its law
determined only by shifting alliances of pirates,
brigands, and smugglers. Beneath this surface,
however, Madame Selentis (the alias of Lady Nysera
Krivaltis) quietly directs operations on behalf of the
Temple of Elemental Evil. Her Temple-appointed
guards, a band of hardened men once loyal to Smigmal
Redhand, now hold the ruined Mayor’s Manor as their
base. From there, Selentis oversees the movement of
supplies, loot, prisoners, and recruits through Nulb into
the Gnarley Forest. Yet her dominance is not public. To
the average brigand, the pirates under Captain Tolub or
the Crimson Trader crew appear far more powerful.
This illusion of fragmented control is intentional,
keeping outside eyes blind to the Temple’s hand.
Cult Intrigue and Influence
The Temple’s resurgence makes Nulb a silent
battleground. Each Prophet seeks to undermine the
others while Hedrack pulls strings from the shadows.
Romag, Prefect of the Earth Temple, uses Dick Rentsch
and the Waterside Hostel to funnel coin and whispers
into his faction’s coffers. Belsornig of the Water Temple
manipulates Captain Tolub and Marad Vesrek,
leveraging piracy and slaving to secure wealth and
influence. Alrrem of the Fire Temple backs Wat, stirring
chaos with firebrand zealots. Each faction would gladly
use adventurers against their rivals, all while concealing
the true scale of the Temple’s second rising.
Persistent Evil Alignment
Nulb is steeped in opportunism, treachery, and cruelty.
Most villagers lean neutral or chaotic evil, surviving by
cutting deals and betraying neighbors. A few neutral
opportunists exist, but true good is almost unheard of.
This moral landscape makes Nulb ideal as both a den of
thieves and a logistics hub for the Temple’s operations.
A Dangerous Refuge
For pirates, cutthroats, and wandering mercenaries,
Nulb offers safe harbor from the authorities of
Verbobonc, Furyondy, and Veluna. Yet the stability of
this refuge is carefully curated. Madame Selentis
enforces secrecy on behalf of Hedrack, ensuring that no
rumor of the Temple’s resurgence escapes. The pirates
squabble, the bandits raid, and the brothels overflow,
but beneath the chaos lies quiet discipline: every wagon,
every hostage, every coin flows ultimately toward the
Temple’s cause.
Conclusion
Nulb teeters on the edge of chaos by design. The
factions appear to vie for dominance — pirates, bandits,
tavern lords — but their infighting masks the Temple’s
true hand. Madame Selentis’s work is not to rule, but to
hide the hand that feeds. For DM’s, this makes Nulb
both a deadly trap and a stage for political intrigue.
Dungeon Master’s Introduction
The Role of Nulb in T1-4 Temple of Elemental Evil
The Village of Nulb serves as an essential setting for
Dungeon Masters running the classic T1-4 Temple of
Elemental Evil by Gary Gygax and Frank Mentzer.
Originally, the module offered only a brief glimpse into
Nulb, leaving much of its intrigue, inhabitants, and
locations open to interpretation. This publication aims
to expand and reimagine Nulb, providing Dungeon
Masters with a fully fleshed-out village to enhance their
campaigns while staying true to Gygax’s vision.
The Original Vision of Nulb
In the T1-4 Temple of Elemental Evil, Nulb is presented
as a den of scum and villainy, a place where adventurers
encounter danger at every turn. However, Gygax only
keyed four specific locations and introduced a small
roster of non-player characters (NPCs). Nulb was meant
to be a haven for pirates, brigands, and cultists loyal to
the Temple, but its potential as a campaign hub was left
largely untapped.
Gygax later mentioned in interviews that there were
plans for additional Temple outposts and expanded
content for Nulb, which had to be omitted to keep the
module from ballooning to an unwieldy size. As it
stands, T1-4 Temple of Elemental Evil is already one of
the most detailed and sprawling modules of its time. A
fully developed Nulb would have added hundreds of
pages to the adventure, impractical for publication.
Expanding the Vision
Nulb as a Dynamic Setting
This reimagined version of Nulb provides Dungeon
Masters with the tools to immerse their players in a
village rife with intrigue, danger, and opportunity.
Lawlessness and Power Struggles: With no formal
government, control rests in the hands of factions.
Madame Selentis enforces Hedrack’s will from the
ruined Mayor’s Manor, pirates choke river trade, and
bandit gangs fight for scraps. Even the constable is a
hollow figure, a reminder that law is little more than
a rumor here.
The Temple’s Shadow: After Emridy Meadows, the
Temple rebuilt in secrecy. Nulb became its staging
ground—Romag runs schemes from the Waterside
Hostel, Belsornig manipulates pirates, and Alrrem
rallies zealots in hidden strongholds. Their rivalries
spill into the streets, but all serve Hedrack’s greater
plan to keep the uprising hidden.
A Living, Breathing Village: Nulb is more than a
backdrop. Every tavern, stable, or alley offers
intrigue, where a careless word can spark betrayal or
opportunity. The village changes with each visit—its
people shifting loyalties, its factions playing games of
survival, and its dangers waiting for heroes bold
enough to wade in.

=== page 6 ===
Politics in Nulb
A Web of Intrigue and Power Struggles
Nulb is a hornet’s nest of criminals, pirates, and cultists,
each pulling in different directions while pretending the
village is nothing more than a haven for brigands. At the
heart of this chaos stands Madame Selentis, Hedrack’s
appointed overseer. From the ruined Mayor’s Manor,
she manages the Temple’s covert supply chain while
disguising her work in a lawless border town.
Madame Selentis’s Political Strategy
Selentis plays the role of organizer without ever
revealing her true allegiance. She cultivates the illusion
of neutrality, allowing pirates, bandits, and smugglers to
believe they act independently—while quietly ensuring
their work feeds the Temple’s growing power.
Balancing Factions: Selentis manipulates rivalries
between Romag, Belsornig, and Alrrem, encouraging
each to undercut the others. Their petty squabbles
keep attention away from Hedrack’s larger designs.
Controlling Logistics: Through bandit crews and
Valegrave’s Farmstead, she secures food and grain;
through the stables, warehouses, and taverns, she
directs smuggling and prisoner transfers. Everything
eventually flows to the Hunting Cabin and into the
Temple’s secret tunnel.
Public Posture: To the common folk, she is no more
than another outlaw “matron” making her cut from
the chaos. Her quiet efficiency ensures most
outsiders never guess her true purpose.
Tensions with the Viscount of
Verbobonc
Though technically part of the Viscounty, Nulb has long
slipped beyond its grasp. Patrols avoid the village, and
the Constable is a drunk husk, tolerated as a symbol of
order while powerless in practice.
Non-Confrontational Stance: Selentis avoids
drawing the Viscount’s eye. She encourages the
appearance of pirate feuds, bandit raids, and
smuggling as the “real problem,” distracting from the
Temple’s hand.
Undermining Authority: By quietly feeding resources
into the Temple while keeping Nulb’s chaos
contained, Selentis ensures Hedrack’s uprising
remains hidden until the time is right to strike.
Criminal Alliances: Bandits and Pirates
Bandits are the lifeblood of Nulb’s roads, raiding
caravans in the Kron Hills and funneling loot back into
the village. Rather than imposing authority, Madame
Selentis quietly balances rival crews, making sure no
single gang grows strong enough to threaten her
position. She directs their plunder through the
Wainwright Depot and the Old Mayor’s Manor,
ensuring everything useful finds its way into the
Temple’s hidden supply chain.
Pirate Smugglers
Pirates on the Imeryds Run and Velverdyva River
remain Nulb’s most dangerous free agents. Captain
Tolub and Marad Vesrek command their own
followings, allied loosely with the Water Temple
through Belsornig. Smuggling, slavery, and extortion at
the docks provide coin and captives that pass through
Selentis’s hands before reaching the Cabin and Temple.
Hidden Economy: Though these dealings appear as
simple piracy, they are the backbone of the Temple’s
covert wealth.
Fragile Alliances: Tolub, Vesrek, and their crews
resist Selentis’s authority, but Hedrack ensures their
usefulness by funneling support through Belsornig.
The Temple of Elemental Evil’s Shadow
The true purpose of Nulb lies in its service to the
Temple’s second rising. Each elemental faction uses the
village to its advantage, though their competition fuels
constant instability.
Earth Temple: Romag manipulates Dick Rentsch at
the Waterside Hostel, keeping the tavern as his front.
Water Temple: Belsornig, through Tolub and Vesrek,
uses piracy to destabilize rivals.
Fire Temple: Alrrem leans on Wat and bandits, his
presence felt most in raids beyond the village.
Air Temple: Kelno operates in the shadows, quietly
recruiting mercenaries and spies while avoiding the
notice of stronger rivals.
Recent Political Developments
Mounted Borderer Withdrawal: The Viscount’s
retreat from the Kron Hills leaves the region
vulnerable, emboldening bandits and pirates to
strike deeper into Verbobonc’s lands.
Temple Influence Rising: Selentis exploits factional
feuds, often “encouraging” adventurers to harass one
faction at the behest of another.
Increased Bandit Raids: Hedrack insists Nulb
remain a den of outlaws in the eyes of outsiders,
using banditry and piracy as a cover for the Temple’s
swelling logistics machine.
“Let the Temple believe they hold the reins. Their
whispers echo here, but it is I who guide the storm that
brews in Nulb.” - Madame Selentis

=== page 7 ===
Notable People of Nulb
The village of Nulb is home to an eclectic array of
powerful and dangerous figures. Each wields influence
in their own way, contributing to the chaos and intrigue
that define the settlement. Below is a summary of the
key individuals whose actions shape the fate of Nulb.
Madame Selentis (alias Lady Nysera
Krivaltis) Click here
Once thought dead after her family’s disgrace, Nysera
reemerges in Nulb under the alias Madame Selentis.
Installed by Hedrack himself, she commands a band of
hardened Temple-backed enforcers from the Old
Mayor’s Manor, overseeing smuggling and logistics in
service of the Temple of Elemental Evil.
Role: Temple Agent and Logistics Overseer
Motivation: To rebuild her power through loyalty to
the Temple and tighten her hold on Nulb.
True Allegiance: The Scarlet Brotherhood seeded
Elvanna in Nulb’s brothel years ago.
Sir Torvel Hawkes Click here
A scarred veteran of the Battle of Emridy Meadows,
Torvel abandoned his noble path to become Selentis’s
sworn protector, serving as both her shield and sword.
Role: Loyal Knight and protector of Selentis.
Motivation: To redeem Nysera’s honor through
devotion and military strength.
Selentis’s Bandits Click here
Assigned by Smigmal Redhand, these hardened
brigands patrol Nulb’s key sites and guard Selentis’s
operations. Their allegiance is less about loyalty to her
and more about Temple backing—but their presence
marks Selentis as a force to be reckoned with.
Role: Selentis’s Enforcers
Motivation: To enforce Selentis’s will and ensure
Temple operations in Nulb.
Romag, Prophet of Earth
Operating through Dick Rentsch and the Waterside
Hostel, Romag manipulates Nulb’s factions to advance
the Earth Temple. His quiet strength is subtle but
pervasive, undermining Selentis.
Role: Earth Temple Leader and Manipulator
Motivation: Expand the Earth Temple’s power.
Belsornig, Prophet of Water
Belsornig’s alliance with Captain Tolub strengthens the
Water Temple’s grip on piracy and trade. His network
destabilizes Selentis’s authority.
Role: Water Temple Leader and Pirate Patron
Motivation: Control Nulb’s waterways and
outmaneuver rival prophets.
Captain Tolub Click here
Master of the Iron Dagger, Tolub is equal parts pirate
and politician. His partnership with Belsornig funds his
ventures, but his growing ambitions put him into
frequent conflict with Selentis and her Temple masters.
Role: Pirate Captain of the Iron Dagger
Motivation: Dominate Nulb’s river trade and amass
wealth while strengthening the Water Temple.
Grud Squinteye Click here
Tolub’s ruthless right hand, Grud relishes bloodshed
and intimidation. His cruel reputation cements the
pirates’ stranglehold on Nulb’s docks.
Role: Lieutenant of the Iron Dagger
Motivation: Prove himself as the deadliest enforcer.
Dick Rentsch Click here
Owner of the Waterside Hostel, Dick poses as a genial
innkeeper while secretly serving the Earth Temple. He
uses his position to collect intelligence and funnel
resources for Romag, always scheming to undercut
Selentis’s growing power.
Role: Hostelier and Earth Temple Agent
Motivation: Expand Earth Temple influence.
Wat Click here
The Waterside Hostel’s bartender hides a more
dangerous role—an informer for the Fire Temple and
Prefect Alrrem. By feeding intelligence across factions,
Wat stirs the pot in Nulb’s deadly rivalries.
Role: Bartender and Fire Temple Spy
Motivation: Aid the Fire Temple by sabotaging its
rivals through espionage.
Skole Click here
The Boatman’s Tavern is Skole’s domain. Outwardly
neutral, he covertly collaborates with the Water Temple,
serving as their eyes and ears in the taverns while
profiting from smuggling.
Role: Proprietor of the Boatman’s Tavern, Water
Temple Collaborator
Motivation: Gain wealth and influence by balancing
neutrality and Temple ties.Nulb’s chaos while
keeping pirates and bandits appeased.
Lodriss Click here
The hidden power behind the Boatman’s Tavern,
Lodriss cultivates ties with Captain Tolub while
carefully preserving her independence. Her sharp
instincts make her a dangerous rival—or ally—
depending on who crosses her path.
Role: Tavern Power Broker and Pirate Ally
Motivation: Leverage her ties with Tolub to remain
influential while avoiding Temple domination.

=== page 8 ===
Jereader Zomawyn Click here
The spiritual head of the Gilded Shackle, Jereader
cloaks cruelty in ceremony. A devout priest of bondage,
he conducts dark rites that sanctify Nulb’s thriving slave
trade. In his mind, slavery is not merely profit but divine
order. He and Lorveth “The Broker” maintain a
symbiotic partnership, blending faith and commerce.
Primary Goal: Expand the reach of the Gilded
Shackle through religious authority.
Secondary Goals: Undermine rival cult factions
while quietly strengthening ties to Hedrack and the
Greater Temple.
Krael Vortash, Captain Click here
Greater Temple Captain placed by Smigmal of the
Broken Tower to assist Hedrick’s agent in Nulb,
Madame Selentis.
Captain Marad Vesrek Click here
A calculating and ruthless pirate captain, he commands
the slaver ship The Crimson Trader . Operating under
the guise of a simple merchant along the rivers.
Primary Goal: Expand the Slave Lords’ operations.
Secondary Goals: Usurping rival Slave Lords.
Rom Khavernus Click here
Zelt (faction leader in Dyvers) right-hand enchanter, a
battle-mage with a sharp tongue and sharper mind. A
product of Dyvers’ New Gentry, he was born to privilege
but now thrives in the underworld.
Felix Fahnor Click here
Head of the Crimson Reaper hit squad in Nulb, operates
with ruthless efficiency, eliminating those in the way.
Edrick Malvaar, Constable Click here
A once-proud figure of authority, now a broken man
clinging to a title that has long since lost its meaning.
Malvaar is a former soldier who served in Verbobonc’s
military but was appointed to the position of Constable
of Nulb when his career faltered. He arrived in Nulb
years ago, eager to restore order to the chaotic village,
but instead found himself drowning in corruption.
Captain Dren Halveth Click here
Mercenary Captain of the Broken Blades—a hard
company of ex-soldiers, caravan guards, and sellswords.
Dren runs contracts out of the Waterside and
Boatman’s, playing Nulb’s factions off each other while
keeping his outfit independent. He’ll take coin from
pirates, bandits, or “merchants,” but avoids being
owned by any Temple prophet.
Primary Goal: Secure steady, well-paid contracts.
Secondary Goals: Build leverage and reputation
across the Viscounty; quietly position the Blades as
indispensable muscle to every major player.
Maldrith Click here
Second-in-command of The Crimson Reapers, Maldrith
plays a pivotal role in the gang’s operations. His
ultimate ambition to support the Crimson Reapers and
to transform Nulb into a necropolis
Otis, Master Smith Click here
Otis is a humble blacksmith of Nulb by trade, but in
truth, he is one of the Viscounty’s most loyal rangers
and a covert agent of the Gnarley Rangers. Scarred by
war and tempered by decades of hardship, Otis walks a
careful line between his quiet life and his sacred duty to
monitor the growing evil around the the village of Nulb.
Primary Goal: Monitor and report the resurgence of
the Temple of Elemental Evil to the Gnarley Rangers
and trusted allies in Hommlet and Verbobonc.
Secondary Goals: Train and evaluate potential
adventurers who might aid in the coming storm.
Canoness Y’dey Click here
An influential cleric of St. Cuthbert, operates under the
guise of Mother Screng in the sinister village of Nulb.
Primary Goal: Sent by the Church of St Cuthbert,
Y’dey in Nulb under the guise of Mother Screng.
Secondary Goals: Y’dey harbors doubts about the
true origins of the Temple of Elemental Evil. Her
mission involves uncovering the forces behind it and
preventing their resurgence.
Murfles (a.k.a. Hruda) Click here
Murfles, posing as Hruda a sharp-tongued daughter of
Mother Screng—is an undercover agent of Good
stationed in Nulb. Despite her rough, unappealing
demeanor, Murfles is a highly capable adventurer, bard,
and an ally of Otis and Canoness Y’dey.
Primary Goal: Protect and assist Canoness Y’dey in
her mission to monitor the Temple.
Secondary Goals: Strike covertly on behalf of Veluna
and Furyondy.
Elvanna Thorne Click here
Oversees the Nulb Brothel with cruel efficiency,
entertain important guests and negotiate deals.
Lorveth “The Broker” Click here
Slave factor of Nulb operating from a private office
upstairs at the Boatman’s Tavern. Lorveth coordinates
directly with Elvanna Thorne (brothel) and river crews
(Captain Tolub, Marad Vesrek), arranging discreet
auctions, keeping the ledgers, and laundering coin
through the tavern market and warehouse.
Master Aldren Valegrave Click here
Master of Valegrave Manor agricultural operations
providing Nulb with provides resources, grain, and
livestock. Fields worked by indentured serfs little better
than slaves to exploitation and cruelty. {{}}

=== page 9 ===
DM Nulb Notes: Lawful Good in
the Hornet’s Nest
A Guide to Running a Paladin or Cleric in Nulb without
Breaking Temple Secrecy
Core Premise
A paladin or cleric entering Nulb is like a flare in the
dark—every faction notices at once. Normally, such holy
figures would be swiftly killed, but Hedrack’s orders
forbid unnecessary provocations:
“No martyrs. No crusades. Nulb must remain a den of bandits,
not a holy battlefield.”
Thus begins a dangerous game of shadow politics. The
Paladin is both a threat and a tool.
Faction Reactions
Hedrack (via Madame Selentis): Spies track the
party, feeding false leads about pirate feuds and
splinter cults. Goal: waste their time.
Romag & Waterside Hostel: Friendly outlaw
innkeeper through Dick Rentsch. Wat spreads
stories of “bogus cults in the swamps.”
Belsornig & Boatman’s Tavern: Pirates pick staged
fights; false intel about smugglers and fire-cults.
Alrrem’s Agents: Deflect inquiries with fiery zeal, but
always redirect zealots toward Earth’s Shattered
Monastery or Water’s River Fort, promising
“heretics” ripe for cleansing.
Smigmal Redhand: Prefers ambushes outside town
to discredit the Paladin.
Feldrin & Gefreid Patris: Delay shipments through
the Hunting Cabin; avoid exposure.
Running the Stay at the Hostel
Day 1: Quiet observation. Locals grow silent, Dick
plays genial host.
Day 2–3: Staged brawls, gossip of splinter cults,
minor thefts.
Day 4+: Coordinated effort to frame or discredit the
Paladin, forcing them to leave.
DM Note: Stress the tension. NPCs always seem to
know more than they say. Conversations hush when the
Paladin enters. Shadowy figures linger at the edges.
Constable Edrick Malvaar
The Paladin may seek out the Constable for law and
order. Instead they find a broken man:
“Law in Nulb? Friend, I’m a scarecrow in a storm. The badge
shines, but the wind blows me where the pirates tell me.”
Malvaar quietly deflects the Paladin toward “safe”
targets—rivals of the faction currently keeping him alive.
Reactions:
If pressed for justice: He warns the Paladin of
“splinter cults” in the hills, parroting the faction that
currently owns his leash.
If threatened: Malvaar folds instantly, begging for his
life. He has no real power and knows it.
DM Use: Malvaar is a narrative mirror—showing the
cost of compromise, the collapse of law, and the futility
of one honest badge in a den of knives.
DM Guidance
Every NPC Has a Script: Locals are briefed on how
to handle outsiders.
False Leads with Just Enough Truth: Outposts exist,
but they’re rival strongholds.
Social Pressure: Prices rise, rooms vanish, allies
disappear. Subtle hostility escalates.
Optional Reward: The “patron” faction may grant
coin or gear, tightening false alliances.
Misdirection Through Rivalries
Temple leaders weaponize their own rivalries to divert holy adventurers. Each faction sends the Paladin toward an
enemy outpost—real cultists, but of another Temple.

=== page 11 ===
A
1. Waterside Hostel of Nulb
seedy stronghold of secrets on the bank of
Imeryds Run. The Waterside Hostel is a
cracked jewel in Nulb’s gutter crown—a
tangle of tavern, inn, and haven for outlaws
that clings to the riverbank like a leech.
Stone foundation. Timber bones. Smokestained rafters. Its rooms creak, the ale is
sour, if something bites you in the night, pray it’s a rat.
Owner: Dick Rentsch (covert operative of the Earth
Temple under Romag)
Function: Inn, tavern, smuggling waystation
Atmosphere: Perpetual tinderbox—kegs of menace
“Rooms are cheap. Lives cheaper.” —Local saying
scratched into the outhouse door.
Physical Features
Two stories: field-stone foundation, patched timber
walls; lean-to sheds and a rickety gallery facing the
river. The roofline sags under too many winters.
Tavern Room: Low ceiling, smoke-thick air, lantern
light the color of old butter. Sound stacks under the
beams; whispers carry farther than you think.
Semi-Private Rooms (B–D): Cramped bunk rooms
with warped doors and rusted latches. Mildew,
sweat, and old blood in the boards. “Privacy” is
something you rent by the hour, lose by the minute.
Hostile Hospitality
Dick Rentsch: The gruff publican mask hides a
patient recruiter and sorter for the Earth Temple. He
weighs every guest for utility: coin, leverage, or
sacrifice. He smiles with his mouth, listens with his
eyes, and remembers everything.
Wat (barkeep): Quiet, sharp, and loyal—to Alrrem’s
Fire Temple. The bar is a cold war line: Earth vs.
Fire under the same roof. Each man tolerates the
other, Hedrack demands no schisms in Nulb.
Serving Staff
Dala & Pearl (cutpurse wenches; level-3 thieves):
pour ale, lift purses, start rumors.
Two manservants (level-2 fighters): sleep in the loft
above the gallery with chain, shields, light
crossbows, and orders to crack heads fast.
Hostel Structure (for DMs)
The Waterside was a decent inn but The Temple’s rise
rotted it into a predator den. Dick and Wat run a
laundering and staging house.
At night, the place transforms into a boiling pot of
violence and plotting. Brawls are common, secrets are
whispered over spilled ale, and death is always just one
drink away.
Room Rates
Service
Cost
Common Room Cot
5 sp / night
Small Room Bunk
7 sp / night
Private Room (B-D)
30 sp / night
Political Ties, Infamy, and Survival
Madame Selentis (Nysera Krivaltis): The spider over
Nulb’s web. Her Temple guards shadow convoys, lift
captives, and collect what’s owed. The Waterside is
useful, so she lets Dick run it—so long as it stays
useful.
Romag (Earth Temple): This is his surface foothold:
screening recruits, moving coin, and holding “special
guests” for pickup. Dick answers to Romag when it’s
profitable, and to Selentis when it’s wise.
Alrrem (Fire Temple): Present only as whispers and
Wat’s eyes. Fire uses the bar to watch Earth, not to
claim the ground.
Belsornig (Water Temple): Keeps his hands off the
Waterside; his crews drink and deal across the
bridge at the Boatman’s Tavern.
Neutral Ground (with teeth): Every faction uses the
Waterside. None dare torch their own table. Fights
end fast unless someone important gives orders.
Infested & Infamous: The rooms itch. The beds bite.
And if you snore too loud, you might not wake up.
Dagger Behind the Ale: It’s well-known that staying
at the Waterside Hostel is a gamble—but in Nulb,
sometimes that’s the best you can hope for.
Nightfall Rule: When the sun drops, the Waterside
boils—fights, deals, and whispered heresies. Blood is
bad for business, but “accidents” happen. The only
law here is sold to the highest bidder—and Selentis
buys in bulk.

=== page 12 ===
The Waterside Tavern at Night
By day, the Waterside is just another miserable tavern
in a miserable town. But at night, under the smoky haze
and guttering lanterns, it becomes something else: a
crucible of tension, where secrets flow with the ale and
violence simmers beneath the surface.
Wat – Night Bartender, Hidden Snake Click here
When the sun goes down, Wat takes the bar. Calm,
careful, always watching. He smiles with his mouth,
never his eyes. To the drunks, he’s just another barkeep.
To those who look closer, he’s something else entirely—
an agent of a rival Temple faction, using the tavern.
“One more for the road? Just remember who poured it.”
Dala – Cutpurse, Lover, Eyes of the Room Click here
Dala moves through the tavern like a knife in the dark—
fast, quiet, smiling just enough to be dangerous. She’s
loyal to Dick, both as a lover and operator, and serves as
his eyes and ears among the nighttime crowd.
Pearl – Pickpocket, Watt’s Paramour Click here
Pearl plays the harmless wench act well—soft voice,
fluttered lashes, gentle touches. It’s all theater. She’s a
seasoned cutpurse, and Wat’s paramour, quietly helping
him unravel Dick’s hold on the tavern. She limits her
thefts to the drunk and the distracted—but if Wat asks,
she’ll go deeper. “She dances between tables, and walks
away with your purse.”
The Manservants – Bouncers, Brutes, Quiet Muscle
Two veterans guard the tavern floor once the lights dim
and the drinks spill. They act like hired fists—and they
are—but there’s a reason no one throws a second punch
in the Waterside after dark. They don’t need orders to
act—they just nod, grab, and break. “They don’t talk.
They just hurt you.”
Tensions Behind the Bar
Wat (Fire Temple → Alrrem): Plays the quiet
barkeep, feeds Pearl daytime tasks and Fire intel;
steers inquisitive guests toward Earth or Water
“splinter” problems—never Fire assets.
Dick Rentsch (Earth Temple → Romag): Smiles and
sorts; keeps a private favors-ledger; tolerates Wat
only under Hedrack’s “no schisms” orders.
Dala (night shift, Dick’s lover): Lifts purses from Firefriendly marks, runs Dick’s errands, passes keys and
gossip upstairs; will cut for him.
Pearl (day shift, Wat’s paramour): Picks only drunks,
hides Fire messages and coin, nudges do-gooders
toward rivals or out of town.

=== page 13 ===
First Visit to the Waterside
Dick Rentsch sizes up the adventurers as they step into the
dimly lit tavern room of the Waterside Hostel, his eyes
narrowing slightly as he leans back against the worn bar. The
clink of mugs and low murmurs fill the background, but
Dick’s voice cuts through, gruff and unwelcoming.
“Ah, fresh faces in Nulb,” he begins, his tone dripping with
a mix of curiosity and suspicion. “Don’t see many new folks
‘round these parts without a reason. So, what brings you to our
little slice of paradise, eh? Don’t suppose you’re here for the
scenic views.” He chuckles darkly, a sound that doesn’t quite
reach his eyes. Dick straightens up, crossing his arms over
his broad chest, his gaze still fixed sharply on the
adventurers. “Listen, I run a tight ship here, and while you’re
welcome to fill your bellies and wet your whistles, understand
this—“ his voice drops, a stern edge creeping in, “I don’t
tolerate trouble. You start any, and you’ll find yourselves out on
your arses quicker than you can draw a blade. Got it?”
He pauses, letting his warning sink in, then continues, the
undercurrent of threat remains. “Now, tell me, what’s your
business in Nulb? Looking for work, trouble, or something else?
Be straight with me—it’ll save us all some time.”
Nightfall in the Tavern: Five Types
When dusk falls and the lanterns gutter low, the tavern
at the Waterside Hostel changes skin—becoming a
volatile crossroads of factions, fortunes, and quiet
knives. What looks like noise and drink is really sorting
and surveillance under Dick Rentsch’s and Wat’s eyes.
Day shift — Pearl (quiet, watchful)
“You plant yourselves like you own the table. You pay first. You
want small beer, river ale, or the black pitch that sticks to your
tongue? I’ve got bog grog if you like forgetting, marsh gin if you
like pain, and river whiskey if you like both—unless you’re
foolish enough for the Black Bottle. What’ll it be?”
1. Villagers
Fisherfolk, mud-cutters, and marsh scavengers from the
Nulb surrounds drift in for bitter ale and a short
forgetfulness. Most are lightly armed, if at all.
Presence: 2d6 early evening; half remain by last call.
Behavior: Wary of outsiders; speak names softly.
They know who’s new, who’s lying, and who’s
dangerous.
Hooks: A quiet nod toward a “wrong” crew (bandits
posing as traders); a missing cousin last seen near
the Hunting Cottage; rumors of “splinter cultists” in
the fens (bait from someone else’s mouth).
Tells: They look to Dick before they answer.
2. Rhennee Bargefolk
Nomadic riverfolk moor their flats and come under
Dick’s strict eye—coin first, always. Cloaked, close-knit,
and superstitious, they drink in a circle and leave in one.
Presence: 1d6+2; sometimes none for weeks.
Admittance: Pay in advance; tolerated, watched.
Hooks: Smuggling runs, river-only items, cryptic
rumors about pirate beacons or vanishing lights near
the old fort upriver. Trust is the price.
Tells: Never drink alone. Never forgive a slight. A
wrong word earns a cold stare and a colder river.
3. Bandits & Mercenaries
Ex-soldiers, blades-for-hire, and ambitious thugs fill
benches with their backs to timber. Some are passing
through; others are shopping for work—clean or not. A
Crimson Reaper or three might be here between jobs.
Composition: Small crews (1d4+1) or lone knives;
sometimes a recruiter in a clean cloak.
Motivation: Coin, cover, or a chance to join a faction.
Caravans: Overland trains swing through in warmer
months; the same men who “guarded” them last
week might “rob” them tomorrow.
Hooks: Protection rackets that lead to rival turf; a
“lost ledger” someone wants found (or destroyed); a
bounty with a suspicious sponsor.
4. River Pirates & Smugglers
Hardened by the Imeryd’s Run, they drink hard and
trade harder. Most Water crews prefer the Boatman’s
Tavern across the way, but a few show at the Waterside
to eavesdrop, fence small goods, or test Earth loyalties.
Trade Focus: Contraband, weapons, bodies to move,
and goods that don’t ask questions.
Interactions: Will deal with PCs—but never without
eyes on the door and a hand near steel.
Hook Potential: Smuggling routes, illegal crossings,
stolen manifests, whispers of a river-fort where tides
run wrong. They respect strength, fear open magic.

=== page 14 ===
5. Temple Agents
Not all sinners wear their shame. Beneath the noise:
Earth Temple screeners, Fire Temple listeners, and the
occasional Greater Temple courier passing like a
shadow. They look like brigands, drovers, sellswords—
until you notice how they sit back-to-wall and how the
room tilts around them.
Presence: 1d2–1d4 “civilians” each night; roles vary.
Engagement Strategy: It can take days of careful
talk, observation, and cross-referencing to spot
patterns: who arrives after who, which table empties
when Dick stands, who never seems drunk.
Leave-Time Lurkers: Off-duty cult troops drift
through in twos and threes. They speak little of “the
Temple,” but stories leak—on purpose—guiding
zealots toward rival outposts (Earth → blame Water,
Fire → blame Earth/Water).
Undercover Operations: PCs won’t grasp the
Temple’s full reach here, but they may realize some
“bandits” are auditioning recruits or marking targets
for a handoff to Selentis’s guards.
Running the Room (DM Quick Use)
Which turf? The Waterside is Earth-leaning (Dick), with
Fire eyes (Wat) on the tap—Water business mostly stays
at the Boatman’s.
Watch the wenches: Dala (night, Dick’s lover)
nudges talk toward Earth’s interests; Pearl (day,
Wat’s paramour) steers curious do-gooders toward
Fire-friendly “splinter cults.”
Neutral with teeth: Brawls pop; feuds don’t—unless
someone important wants them to. If steel shows,
the loft guards start with crossbows.
Signal the net: A raised lantern or a wrong song
verse can summon “concerned locals” (bandits), a
“constable check” (Malvaar in defeat), or a quiet
Temple pickup that empties a table without a sound.
Waterside Menu
Ales & Cheap Spirits
Imeryd Small Beer 2cp: Thin and sour, like it’s been
rinsed through old grain. Locals say it keeps you
sober enough to run.
River Ale 3cp: Flat, woody, and served warm; the
barrel does most of the talking. Good for washing
down bad news. “Black Pitch” Stout 6cp: Thick as
tar with a bitter bite that clings to your tongue.
Leaves a dark ring in every mug it touches.
Bog Grog 8cp: Ale cut with rotgut until your eyes
water. One mug loosens lips; two erase last names.
Marsh Gin 1sp: Juniper forward with a swampy
aftertaste. Burns clean, then comes back mean.
River Whiskey 2sp: Grain-sweet at first, then a hard
downstream pull. Warms the chest and fogs the
edges of the night.
Dick’s Black Bottle 5sp: Oily, opaque, and
aggressively private. It tastes like a dare and finishes
like a confession.
River Grub
Eel & Onion Stew 4cp: Greasy sheen with bones that
hide in the broth. Smells better than it looks, sits
heavier than it should.
Catfish Chow 5cp: Gray, salty, and stubbornly filling.
A dockhand’s hug in a chipped bowl.
Blood & Barley Pottage 3cp: Iron on the nose, barley
on the teeth. Lingers like a bad promise.
Turnip Bone-Broth 2cp: More marrow ghost than
meat. The heat helps; the flavor doesn’t.
Swamp-Eel Pie — Flaky top over a slick, peppered
mush. Eat it fast before it remembers it’s a fish.
Mystery-Meat Hand Pie 2cp: Grease on the fingers
and questions in the mouth. The pastry is honest; the
filling is not.
Bread & Bites (Old Mavrek’s)
Hard Loaf Slice 2cp: Dense and toothy, forged rather
than baked. Keeps for weeks; forgives nothing.
Lard Smear (+ pickle) 3cp: Shine on the bread, sour
on the tongue. Cheap fuel for long nights.
Cheese Rind 2cp: Tough, salty wedge that fights
back. Better with whiskey; tolerable without.
Night shift — Dala (smile like a knife)
“You reek of road and luck. You want something that lies nice—
river ale—or something that tells the truth—bog grog? I can
drown you in black pitch, set you right with marsh gin, or burn
the edges off with river whiskey. If you’re feeling brave or stupid,
I’ll crack Dick’s Black Bottle. Coin on the wood, then you drink.”

=== page 15 ===
Guests at the Waterside Hostel
Room A — The Common Room
Twenty bunks. One latrine bucket. No peace.
By day, the common room is just a cheap place to
sleep. By night, it’s a powder keg of fear and steel. The
scent of mildew, sweat, and boiled rat stew chokes the
air. Bunks creak. Fights break out over blankets. But six
of these cots are claimed—not rented.
The Crimson Reapers
The Crimson Reapers are wolves in a too-small pen.
Dirty, bloodstained, and always armed, they’ve turned
the center of the common room into their den.
“Don’t look at ‘em. Don’t talk to ‘em. Don’t sleep too close.”
The Reavers’ Domain Click here
The middle of the common room belongs to the
Crimson Reapers, and no one dares encroach on their
space. Their bunks are pushed together, forming a
barricaded section, and their gear is strewn about as if
they own the place. Anyone foolish enough to move too
close is met with hard stares, sneers, or the cold steel of
a dagger held just loosely enough to be a threat.
Territory Claimed: Six bunks pushed together, gear
strewn like territory markings
Attitude: Predatory, aggressive, daring anyone
Weapons: Daggers always on hips, crossbows leaned
nearby, hatchets tucked into bedrolls
Behavior: Loud, lewd, half-drunk—never off-guard
Tactics & Trouble
Mocking outsiders—especially adventurers—just to
watch them squirm.
Intimidation “games”: fake challenges, sudden
shoving matches, knife tosses
Violent retaliation for any perceived disrespect: a
kick, a knife, or a brawl Feast first, drink deep, never
pay—Rentsch doesn’t stop them.
DM Tip: If players interact, roll tension like a combat
initiative countdown. Every failed CHA or WIS check
tightens the coil. A full fight could draw in nearby
bandits, mercs, and tavern guards—chaos in a bottle.
Room B — The Mercenary Barracks
They’ve fought in four wars. This one’s just cheaper.
The door to Room B doesn’t lock, but that doesn’t mean
it’s unguarded. Inside, the Broken Blades Click here
sleep light, eat cold, and speak in short sentences.
They’ve seen too much to joke, and too little to forget.
Armor hangs from bedposts like steel skins shed for a
few hours. Swords rest beneath pillows. Crossbows
point at the door when they sleep. They keep to
themselves. Mostly - until someone knocks too loud.
Broken Blades Quick Facts
Faction Status: Mercenaries—no loyalties but coin
History: Veterans from campaigns in Dyvers, the
Wild Coast, and failed crusades in the Kron Hills
Leadership: Dren Halveth (firm), Brakka (erratic)
Tensions: Loyalty is paper-thin; Fights among them
are common
Room C — Vacant Quarters
Room C is one of the few semi-private chambers
available at the Waterside Hostel—a rare bit of calm in
the constant churn of violence and noise. For now, it
stands empty, the bunks made, the floor swept, and a
single flickering lantern left burning low.
The room smells faintly of old pipe smoke and damp
timber. Scars from previous tenants—knife marks in the
wall, dried blood in the floorboards, a shattered mug in
the corner—hint that peace here is temporary.
Room D — Crimson Reapers Click here
“They run their gang like a cult. Zelt’s the blade. Zak’s the knife
in your soul.” — Pearl, whispering too close
Room D isn’t just rented—it’s fortified. The Crimson
Reapers, a notorious gang out of Dyvers, have turned
this upper room into their war room. Thick timbers
reinforce the door, sealed with three visible locks and
one hidden mechanism. The room breathes menace.
Weapon rack: Short swords, daggers, and a custom
crossbow with silver bolts
Rough-hewn table: Scarred with burns and etched
maps of Verbobonc, the Gnarley, and river routes
Locked chest: Marked with the sigil of Dyvers—holds
gold, forged seals, coded scrolls
Lighting: Always dim. Always one candle too few
Scent: Pipe smoke, damp wool, old blood
The Reapers’ Operations Room
Rom Khavernus (“Hollow Jack”): Click here Operations
Leader. A former Dyvers noble and operations leader.
Fallen alchemist. Arcane mastermind.
Maldrith the Hexed: Click here His second—a
whispering Orcus-priest, cloaked in rot and ritual scars.
The rest of the gang doesn’t speak around him.

=== page 17 ===
A
2. Otis’s Smithy and Stable
cornerstone of Nulb’s ragged
infrastructure, Otis’s Smithy & Stable is the
best-maintained structure in town—smoke
curling from the forge, the ring of hammer
on steel echoing through the muddy alleys.
Known for his formidable strength and his
seemingly simple life as a blacksmith, Otis
hides a deeper, more complex role as a guardian and
observer, aligned with the forces of good against the
encroaching darkness of the Temple of Elemental Evil.
Arrival at Otis’s Smithy and Stable
The yard smells like hot iron, wet hay, and tired horses.
Smoke trails from the forge. Somewhere behind the
building, a hammer rings metal into obedience. The boy
appears from the shadows near the gate, wiping grease onto
his pants.
He’s maybe fifteen. Wiry. Dirt in the creases of his neck.
Eyes like someone who’s seen a body or two and didn’t have
the luxury to flinch.
Chon (guarded but respectful): “Don’t see many strangers
come in this clean. I’m Chon. You want stalls or steel?”
Adventurer (dismounting, glancing around): “We’ve got
tired mounts and heavier packs. Looking for a place to stable
‘em. Maybe some armor work.”
Chon (nods, jerks a thumb toward the stalls): “Five silver a
night. Grain, water, bedding. They’ll be upright in the morning
—unless they weren’t when you got here.”
Adventurer (half-grinning): “And grooming?”
Chon (leading the horses, not looking back): “Three more.
Gets you clean hooves, brushed tails, and less stink. Otis don’t
do miracles, keeps ‘em better than most wives keep husbands.”
Adventurer (handing over coin): “Sounds fair. Do that.”
Chon (taking the reins, quieter): “Right. I’ll see it handled.
Otis’ll be out if he wants to talk blades. Otherwise, you need
something… knock loud, and don’t reach too quick.”
He disappears into the stalls, voice trailing behind like a
whisper carried on the reek of smoke and horse.
Otis’s Cottage (Interior)
Tucked behind the forge, Otis’s modest cottage reflects
a spartan life lived in secret. A straw-stuffed pallet rests
beside a battered wooden chest containing well-worn
clothing and rugged adventuring gear. A single chair
and table, both scorched from candle work, serve as his
planning space. Beneath a loose stone under the old
anvil lies a hidden cache. This is no mere smithy—it’s a
ranger’s lair, prepared for the storm that’s coming.
Services & Prices
Stabling & Feed:
Overnight Boarding: 5 sp / night per horse
Standard Feed: 2 sp / day | Premium: 4 sp / day
Grooming: 3 sp (basic) / 6 sp (full treatment)
Smithy Services:
Horse Shoeing: 5 sp (basic) / 8 sp (specialized)
Armor Mending: 10 sp (minor) / 15–30 sp (major)
Weapon Maintenance: 5 sp (sharpen) / 8 sp (repair)
Custom Orders: Prices vary; Otis is picky with
commissions
Otis, Master Smith Click here
Otis stands as a paragon of strength and skill, his
physical prowess matched only by his strategic acumen
in the greater geopolitical landscape of Nulb.
Appearance: A burly man with a bushy beard,
embodying the physicality of his trade.
Drive: Seeks to protect Nulb from external threats
while satisfying his personal quest for justice.
Local Relations: Maintains a necessary rapport with
Lady Nysera Krivaltis, ensuring his business thrives.
Chon, Smith’s ‘boy’ Click here
Not the sharpest tool in the shed but loyal and diligent
in his duties. Manages the care of the horses, ensuring
they are fed, groomed, and ready for use. Simpleminded yet content; motivated by a stable job.
Sammy, Rat-Faced Apprentice Click here
A young, keen observer with a sharp intellect masked by
his unassuming appearance. Assists with metal works,
slowly learning the trade secrets from Otis. Curious and
ambitious, driven by a desire to master the craft.

=== page 18 ===
N
3. Mother Screng’s Herb Shop
estled in the heart of Nulb like a tick
behind a wart, Mother Screng’s shop
smells of sage, rot, and secrets. Locals
drift in for salves and sleeping draughts,
unaware the real business happens in
whispers and behind locked drawers. It’s
more than a shop—it’s a watchpost in a
war few know is being fought. The shop exudes a
peculiar charm, from its weathered exterior to its
aromatic interior, and is staffed by the enigmatic crone
Mother Screng and her equally peculiar “daughter,”
Hruda Murfles.
“You come for poultice or poison, I’ll give you what you need.
But it’ll cost.” —Mother Screng
Exterior
A crooked shack of moldy boards and creeping ivy. The
sign—“Mother Screng’s Herb Shop”—hangs limp on
rusted chains. Vines claw up the walls, and behind the
building, six chickens strut the dirt like they own it. The
place leans, but it hasn’t fallen. Not yet.
“My daughter may not have my charm, but she’s sharper than
you’d expect. Watch your tongue around her, or she’ll cut you
with hers.” —Mother Screng
Interior
Inside, it’s a labyrinth of jars, racks, and bundled herbs
hung like trophies from the rafters. Shelves groan under
the weight of dried roots and bone-colored bottles. A
cauldron bubbles on the back hearth, always full, never
empty. Labels are scratched in crabbed ink, unreadable
unless without years and patience. (most don’t)
Goods & Prices
Common Remedies
Antiseptic Salve – 5 gp (heals 1d4, stops infection)
Sleeping Draught – 15 gp (8-hour rest, no dreams)
Clotting Powder – 10 gp (stabilizes dying instantly)
Rare Concoctions (Trusted customers only)
Elixir of Vitality – 50 gp (cures 1 level of exhaustion)
Spiderwort Decoction – 75 gp (neutralizes poison)
Hidden Defenses & Secrets
Behind the Cauldron is a hidden compartment
Items: Scroll of Commune, Potion of Heroism, and
300 gp in bribe money
Homing Pigeons: Messages are regularly dispatched
to Verbobonc, Furyondy, and Veluna
Trapped Vial: A decoy bottle labeled “Fever Tonic”
explodes into a blinding flash if opened without
speaking a code phrase “The roots remember what
the leaves forget.”
Proprietors of the Herb Shop
Mother Screng (Canoness Y’dey in
disguise) Click here
An elderly crone with sharp eyes and a sharper mind.
Screng has served Nulb’s people for years—but only a
few know her true identity as Canoness Y’dey, a spy and
agent of the Church of St. Cuthbert.
She monitors Temple activity, reports to Verbobonc
and Veluna, and supports adventurers working
against the cults.
Wears the guise of a harmless healer
Secretly stores scrolls, coded documents, and
enchanted potions
Keeps a dagger behind her herbs, and prayers
behind her sneers
“Don’t trust those potions from the pirates. What I sell will heal
you; what they sell might pickle you.”
“Herbs, potions, and powders—more than you’ll ever
know what to do with. But if you’re desperate enough,
I’ll find what you need.” - Mother Screng

=== page 19 ===
Relationships & Politicals
Relationship with Boatman’s Brothel (The Broker)
Screng sells tonics and quiet poisons to buyers tied to
the loft above the Boatman’s—where Elvanna runs the
rooms, Mardun keeps order, and Lorveth “the Broker”
Thrask moves flesh and secrets. She deals because she
must; she listens because she’s dangerous when
informed. The loft links to the tavern’s ware-rooms by a
concealed hatch—useful for smuggling, worse for
vanishing people—and Screng maps its rhythms by who
comes limping in for salves.
Elvanna’s Loft serves Temple recruitment,
blackmail, and trafficking; Screng times her
messages by their “big nights.”
Thrask keeps ledgers and keys; when his runners
need mixes in a hurry, Screng waters the wine—just
enough to make brutes slow and tongues loose.
Mardun’s presence means pressure is never far;
Screng survives by smiling, selling, and never being
in the same room as a confession.
Madame Selentis (Greater Temple)
Screng and Selentis maintain a cold truce. Selentis
buys rare herbs and expects silence; Screng sells and
counts footsteps. Selentis oversees Nulb’s surface
logistics and keeps the river and road quiet; Screng
reads that quiet like scripture, then pouches her notes
for Veluna.
Selentis’s bandits move captives and goods through
Nulb; Screng’s “harmless” shop watches and warns
along the same routes.
Screng’s cover as an old crone lets her work under
everyone’s nose—exactly how Canoness Y’dey
planned it.
Relationship with the River Pirates
Though they prefer the Boatman’s Tavern, river pirates
often drift toward Mother Screng’s shop for remedies,
hangover cures, or something stronger. Screng provides
what they need—no questions, no promises—but
watches them all with the eyes of a hawk. She’s earned
a grudging respect from the likes of Captain Tolub and
Skole, who suspect she’s more than just a hedge witch.
Relationships with Temple Agents
Romag (Earth Temple)
Romag uses the Waterside Hostel as his ground hub;
his orders travel by cutouts, not handshakes. Screng
sells only via intermediaries and salts some remedies to
fade under strain—bad poultices make bad soldiers. She
keeps it deniable and distant.
Belsornig (Water Temple)
Belsornig keeps his hands at the Boatman’s and off the
Waterside; tests come as false customers and leaky
rumors. Screng feeds scraps and watches river traffic
for when his net tightens.
Lucius Graeme (Temple Courier)
Lucius walks the Waterside stairs as a go-between for
the Greater Temple. When his trails brush Screng’s
door, she lets the message pass, notes who retrieves it.
Smigmal Redhand (Assassin Commander)
Screng has no appointment with Smigmal, only the
sensation of being measured. When Crimson Reaper
business heats at the Waterside, Screng shortens her
words and lengthens her memory.
Quiet War, Holy Thread
Behind the counter: pigeons for Veluna, a hidden cache,
and a mission—Mother Screng is Canoness Y’dey in
deep cover. Every sale might be a signal; every “old
woman’s kindness,” a knife wrapped in gauze.
Hruda (Murfles) Click here
A surly, short-tempered woman who calls Screng
“Mother” but shares no blood. In truth, Hruda is an
elven operative of Veluna, a seasoned adventurer who
keeps a dagger beneath the counter. Has a reputation
for insulting pirates to their faces
Mother Screng’s First Encounter
The door creaks open. The sharp scent of herbs and damp
wood hits first—then a thick, bitter tang of something
boiling in the back. Dozens of dried plants dangle from the
rafters like shriveled bats. A crooked figure stands behind
the counter, hunched in layered robes, her white hair tied in
a bundle like old twine.
“Well now… you lot smell like steel, mud, and bad decisions.
Come in, then. I am Mother Screng.”
She stirs the bubbling pot beside her without looking up.
“Looking for a cure, a curse, or something to make your enemies
sleep with their eyes open? I’ve got all three… and tea, if you’re
brave.”
“Names aren’t needed. Coin is. And if you’re here about the
blackroot shipment, tell the Brother he can wait.”

=== page 20 ===
T
4: Boatman’s Tavern and Nulb Market
he Boatman’s Tavern and Nulb Market is
the lawless heart of Nulb, a seedy den
where pirates, bandits, smugglers, and
mercenaries converge to trade stolen
goods, broker dirty deals, and drown their
sins in cheap ale. Owned in name by
Lodriss, but truly controlled by a shadow
network of criminals, the tavern serves as a vital hub for
bandits, river pirates, and agents of the Temple of
Elemental Evil. Though appearing chaotic and
disorderly, it is a well-managed enterprise under the
watchful eyes of Lodriss and her lieutenant Skole.
Outside Appearance
The Boatman’s Tavern appears unwelcoming at first
glance. Rough-hewn wooden planks and thick stone
pillars support the structure, with stained glass
windows set high, clouded with grime and filth. The
establishment seems to carry an air of disinterest, as
though it cares not for its patrons’ comfort or approval.
Structure and Layout
1. The Tavern – Mainroom of Boatman’s (Faces Pier) A
dim, smoky space filled with raucous laughter,
spilled ale, and the dull thud of knives in wood. The
tavern serves as the unofficial town hall for Nulb’s
underworld. It is here that pirates arrive,
mercenaries are hired, and Temple meet envoys.
2. The Boatman’s Warehouse (Also Faces Pier)
Stacked high with crates of stolen goods, smuggled
arms, and Temple-bound supplies. Guards from the
Crimson Reapers watch over the inventory,
occasionally helping to load covered wagons at night.
3. Nulb’s Black Market Hall - Boatman’s A shadowy
bazaar where poison vendors, artifact traders, and
slavers conduct their trade. Disguised cultists hawk
trinkets imbued with elemental power. Information
and favors are often the true currency.
4. The Brothel of Boatman’s Tavern “Elvanna’s Loft”
(Second Floor) Elvanna Thorne runs this operation
with cruel elegance. Her courtesans act as spies,
blackmailers, and recruiters. The brothel doubles as
a Temple initiation ground for select patrons.
5. The Basement (Hidden Below) Beneath the worn
timbers and riotous laughter of the Boatman’s
Tavern lies something far darker than old kegs and
salted meat. The basement complex, hidden behind
a trapdoor cleverly concealed behind the bar, is a
decaying warren of shadows—a haven for smuggling.
6. The Flooded Prison Room - Hidden Basement A
trapdoor behind the bar drops into narrow stone
halls give way to mildew and iron, and the floor tilts
toward a half-flooded chamber of rusted cages, a
stained rack, and chains. Lanterns spit smoke, river
mist creeps in, and a plank-braced tunnel snakes off
toward a ruined shack for midnight handoffs. It is
Hosk “Chains” Varlek’s kingdom.
The Nulb Market: A Bazaar of the Illicit
Adjacent to the tavern, the Nulb Market is where
contraband changes hands. Weapons, poisons, stolen
goods, and even slaves pass through the market,
overseen by Lodriss and her contacts. The stalls here
aren’t run by honest merchants but by those willing to
risk dealing in smuggled Velunese wine, stolen gnome
gems and silver, and relics looted from ancient ruins.
Lodriss: the shrewd former camp follower, rules the
market’s dealings but treads carefully among her
powerful patrons.
The Crimson Reapers: use the market to fence
goods, and meet with potential recruits.
Captain Tolub’s pirates: offload plunder from the
Velverdyva River, ensuring a steady supply of blackmarket goods.
Booth Sales: Merchants rent tables to sell goods,
with 10% of all sales going to Lodriss.
General Store Section: Items are stored on tall
shelves throughout the warehouse, catering to
common needs.
Pirates at Boatman’s Tavern
When Captain Tolub makes port, the room tilts his way.
The Iron Dagger puts off a few boats, a quartermaster
stakes a back table, and Skole tightens the house rules
so business—not brawls—sets the tempo. Tolub’s full
company runs to about thirty river pirates, but only a
handful (1d8+2) drink here at once; the rest mind the
docks, the warehouse doors, or “escort” cargo through
the hidden cellar with river access.

=== page 21 ===
The River Pirates and Nulb’s Economy
Pirates are the tide that lifts Nulb’s black market. They
control the moorings in practice, skim “handling fees”
on every fat barge, and feed the Nulb Market with a
steady trickle of contraband—wine from Veluna, gnome
silver and stones, war spoils that should have stayed
buried. Lodriss takes her tithe (10%) off stall sales;
Skole enforces peace long enough for a fair to look like
a market. Formal authority stays away because it learns
fast: here, fees make more noise than laws.
Influence on Nulb’s Trade
Boatman’s has become the river’s black-market
exchange. Nightly lots change hands under lantern light;
Broker arranges “special cargo” upstairs; Temple
couriers with plain faces buy quiet passage in the
crowd. Prices of staples swing with the Iron Dagger’s
schedule, honest fishers get squeezed, and caravans
route around official ports to meet Tolub’s boats on the
sly. The pirates keep the taproom loud and the dockside
orderly enough to move goods—because in Nulb, trade
survives what law cannot.
Relationship with Temple Agents
Lodriss has an unspoken alliance with temple agents,
allowing the cultists to conduct business within Nulb
without interference. The tavern serves as an informal
meeting ground for cultists, pirates, and mercenaries
who align with the Temple of Elemental Evil. Cultists
occasionally use the tavern for secretive gatherings.

=== page 22 ===
Skole Welcomes Adventurers
As you step into the dimly lit, smoky interior of Boatman’s
Tavern, a hush falls over the rowdy conversations. Eyes flick
in your direction—some filled with curiosity, others with
suspicion. Just as you start to take in the room, a burly man
with a thick, muscular build and a layer of grime on his
apron looks up from polishing a grimy tankard. His face
splits into a crooked, almost sardonic grin as he sizes you
up. “Well, well, what do we have here?” Skole drawls, his
voice a rough, gravelly sound that cuts through the chatter
around you. “A band of newcomers, eh? Haven’t seen you lot
around before. Brave souls, wanderin’ into Nulb without a clue
where ya are.” He chuckles, a low, rumbling sound, as if he’s
in on a private joke.
He leans forward on the bar, squinting at you. “You lot
lookin’ for drink or trouble? Round here, we serve both in plenty
—though trouble’s got a nasty habit of findin’ you whether you
ask for it or not.” He chuckles darkly, nodding toward a few
unsavory types nursing their mugs at the corner tables. They
shift slightly, casting sideways glances, measuring you in
silence.
Then Skole gestures lazily with his thumb towards a
rickety table by the window. “Take a seat if you can find one
that ain’t sticky. Or join the river rats by the fire if you’re after
stories of…adventure,” he says, his eyes glinting with
something between amusement and a challenge. “But don’t
go thinkin’ you’ll get a warm welcome. Nulb ain’t the kind of
place where folks get friendly easy, if you catch my meanin’.” He
straightens, glancing at your gear, an eyebrow raised. “Just
watch yourselves. Don’t spill nothin’ on the floor—it’s filthy
enough as it is.” With that, he turns back to his tankard,
though you feel his gaze lingering on you from the corner of
his eye, ever watchful.
Skole: Gruff, watchful, no-nonsense. Doesn’t like
Temple politics but fears Lodriss more.
“If yer bleedin’, clean it up yerself. Floor’s seen worse.”
Lodriss – The Real Owner Click here
Though Skole manages the tavern and market, it is
Lodriss who holds true ownership. A former camp
follower with a shrewd business mind, Lodriss has
leveraged her relationship with Captain Tolub the river
pirate leader, to maintain dominance over the tavern
and its revenue.
Skole the Proprietor Click here
Skole, a former smuggler and riverman, manages the
tavern on behalf of its true owner, Lodriss. He is wellknown in the village, both for his size and his skill at
managing unruly patrons. Skole often stays at the
tavern overnight, particularly when the crowd is rowdier
than usual.
“One hand on your drink, the other on your dagger—
that’s Nulb for you.” Skole

=== page 23 ===
4. Boatman’s Tavern – Mainroom
The Beating Heart of Nulb’s Decay
Dim, smoke-choked, and forever echoing with the
clamor of mugs and muffled threats, the mainroom of
Boatman’s Tavern is where Nulb breathes. Not the
breath of life, but that of rotting commerce, broken
oaths, and whispered curses. Positioned just off the
pier, the tavern opens directly into the swamp-laced
boardwalk where pirate skiffs and black-sailed barges
roll in with the tide.
This is the unofficial town hall of Nulb’s underworld.
Deals are struck in the open, blood is spilled without
consequence, and Temple agents, slavers, pirates, and
bandits mingle beneath hanging lanterns and warped
timber beams.
Entering the Tavern from the Dock
The warped dock planks groan beneath your boots, slick
with river mist and algae, as the salt-stained double doors of
the tavern loom ahead—swollen with damp and marked
with old knife scores. A faded symbol of a boatman’s oar,
cracked and half-burned, hangs above the frame like a
warning.
You push open the doors. Heat and noise slap you in the
face. The air inside is thick with the stench of sweat, sour
ale, and wet wool. Smoke curls from lanterns and the center
fire pit, mixing with the haze of pipeweed and something
more acrid—burned meat, maybe. Or blood.
Wooden beams hang low overhead, sagging like a drunk’s
shoulders. Tables crowd the room in disorderly rings, sticky
with spilled drink and crusted with salt. Rivermen and
swamp traders bellow, argue, gamble, and drink like it’s their
last night above the mud.
At the far end, a hairy mountain of a man—Skole, no
doubt—wipes a mug with a rag that’s dirtier than the cup
itself. His one good eye catches yours for a moment. He
nods once… slow… as if measuring your price. A tray clatters
nearby as a serving wench—frowning, worn—pushes past
you with a grunt. Behind her, her younger companion smirks
as she twirls a loose strand of hair, clearly listening to every
word around her. Somewhere near the hearth, a knife slams
into wood with a thunk. Laughter follows.
You’re not just in a tavern. You’re in Nulb now. And every
eye wants something.
Description & Mood
The tavern is carved into the corner of a repurposed
warehouse. Rain-stained rafters loom overhead, and the
air is thick with the scent of wet boots, boiled turnips,
and unwashed bodies. The stone hearth offers only
occasional warmth, choked by soot and damp logs.
Grime-slick tables surround a central fire pit, where
flickering flames catch the gold glint of teeth and knives
alike.
At any hour, one might hear:
The slap of a thrown tankard.
The growl of dice across a sticky tabletop.
A scream, swiftly silenced.
Or the melodic cooing of Elvanna’s girls scouting for
their next mark.
Tavern Details
Capacity: Up to 30 patrons shoulder-to-shoulder.
Lighting: Dim lanterns, fire pit, occasional candle
stubs.
Drinks Served: Cheap ale, bitter beer, and sour wine.
No labels. No refunds.
Clientele: At any time, 1d4 + 2 villagers and 1d6 + 6
rivermen can be found here, often joined by river
pirates from Tolub’s crew.
Activities and Encounters
Smuggler Dice Games: Loud, fast-paced,
occasionally rigged. The stakes range from gold to
human lives.
Temple Talks: Cultists meet here in public, masked
as traders or mercs.
Recruitment & Bribery: Madame Selentis’ agents
may test adventurers here first.
Brawls: Fistfights are hourly; knife fights, nightly.
Serving Wenches & Brothel Ties
The tavern employs Ketta and Norla, two tavern maids
who carry trays, swat hands, and quietly observe. Both
report to Lodriss—and indirectly to Elvanna.
Ketta is sour-faced and quick with a pitcher.
Norla has a sharper mind than she lets on and uses
flirtation to overhear valuable gossip.

base chances. Adjust them based on the current
state of the campaign, recent player actions, or
significant events in Nulb.

wake, and adventurers are cautioned to tread carefully

=== page 25 ===
4. Boatman’s Black Market Hall
A Bazaar of Shadows
The Indoor Market Hall of Nulb is no innocent
gathering of farmers and craftsmen. This is a shadowy
bazaar—a place where masks are worn as often as
blades, and every smile carries the scent of betrayal.
Facing the village side of Nulb and operating under the
unspoken blessing of the Temple of Elemental Evil, this
market is where contraband breathes, and morality
withers.
The hall connects to the Boatman’s Tavern via an
internal door and includes large iron-bound oak doors
facing the street for patrons. Inside, a mix of open-air
stalls, curtained booths, and shelf-lined storage creates
a chaotic maze of illicit commerce. Lanterns cast amber
light across muddy flagstones, while incense and
swamp smoke disguise the rot of desperation.
General Layout and Access
Main Doors (Village Side): Two large, iron-bound
oak doors provide access for patrons. Usually
guarded by hired thugs who demand a visible
weapon or bribe.
Tavern Door: A connecting door leads into the
Boatman’s Tavern, allowing fluid movement
between drink and deal-making.
Warehouse Access: A third reinforced door leads to
the warehouse section, used for loading bulk
shipments or smuggled goods.
Market Features
Booth Rentals: Ramshackle booths, crates-ascounters, and curtain-shrouded tables line the hall.
Merchants pay a 10% tithe to Lodriss.
General Supply Section: A corner of tall wooden
shelves holds used common goods—rope, rations,
flint, tallow, torches, cheap weapons—no questions.
Artifact Alley: A narrow row of stalls specializing in
looted relics, cursed trinkets, and counterfeit holy
items. Some of it is real. All of it is dangerous.
The Shadow Nook: A curtained alcove where
poisons, alchemical brews, and deadly flora are sold
in hushed tones.
Slave Cage (Hidden): Iron cages located in the
warehouse, where a large door leads to the true
holding area—beneath the floor. In the basement
below lies a secret chamber, sealed with iron bars
and guarded lay the true prisoner chamber.
Atmosphere & Activity
Smells: Iron, mold, alchemy smoke, sweet wine,
leather, and blood.
Sounds: Low bargaining, clinking chains, distant
laughter, and the occasional crack of a whip.
Guards: 4–6 thugs patrol, but violence is only
stopped if it interferes with trade or profit.
Light: Dim lanterns hang from rusted chains. Some
corners are kept intentionally dark for illicit
whispers.
First Steps into Nulb’s Black Market
The iron-bound oak doors groan as you push them inward,
coughing on the sudden shift from open air to smoke-thick
gloom. The hall is dim, stinking of mold and boiled leather,
its floor smeared with old mud and unspoken things.
Lanterns sway from rusted chains, casting crooked shadows
across rows of stalls, curtained booths, and slouching
patrons who eye you like carrion birds watching fresh meat.
Somewhere in the back, a hooded vendor whispers over a
vial that glows blue. Another sharp-eyed figure tugs a
covered crate toward a booth ringed with stolen dwarven
steel. Low bargaining buzzes like flies on a corpse.
But before you can step further— “Hold up.” Two figures
peel away from a crate near the warehouse access—thugs in
piecemeal leathers and stamped iron gorgets. One leans on
a thick cudgel; the other drags a blade through a whetstone,
slow and deliberate. They block your path, side by side, near
a heavy door that reeks of rust and recent movement.
The first one jerks a thumb over his shoulder and smirks
through crooked teeth. “New faces, yeah? No call to be
wanderin’ back here just yet.”
His eyes slide over your weapons. He doesn’t look
impressed. “Lodriss don’t like surprises. This ain’t a village
market—you don’t browse unless someone vouches.”
The other one narrows his eyes, still stroking steel across
stone. “Best find your coin and purpose fast, friend. Or go
back to the tavern where folks bleed quieter.”
Insight Check (DC 12):
They’re not trying to start a fight—they’re asserting
control. Newcomers get one warning. Push too hard,
and things escalate.
Dialogue Options:
Polite Deference: “We’re here to trade—no trouble.”
(Disarms suspicion, they offer directions.)
Name-drop Lodriss or Selentis: “We were sent by
someone upstairs.” (Roll with Advantage; may grant
access.)
Bluff Check (DC 15): Claim to be meeting a vendor.
Push Past or Threaten: Triggers combat or nearby
guards call for backup.

=== page 26 ===
Whispered Deals in the Dark
In the Market Hall, every deal has layers. The coin buys
the goods, but the price is always greater: allegiance,
silence, or damnation. Those who linger too long leave
poorer—or changed. Lodriss always remembers a face.
Black Market Seller Quotes: “Where’d you get this?”
“Let’s just say it fell off a wagon—straight into
opportunity.”
“Came downriver on a barge with no name and
fewer questions.”
“From a merchant who didn’t value it enough to
keep breathing.”
“Found it in a ruin, next to a skeleton that looked
surprised.”
“Gifted by a friend… after a bit of convincing.”
“A noble left it behind while running for his life. Very
generous fellow.”
“Came through Captain Tolub’s hands—so you know
it’s authentic.”
“Temple tithe that didn’t quite make it to the altar, if
you catch my meaning.”
“Recovered from a caravan that got lost just south of
Hommlet.”
“Traded it for secrets. You wouldn’t want the other
half of the deal.”
Sample Merchants and Items
Tarn the Toothless – Sells potions of dubious origin.
May offer black lotus poison for the right coin.
Grey Myra – A pale-eyed woman dealing in cursed
idols and elemental trinkets.
Orven’s Odds – Fences stolen noble jewelry from
Dyvers and Verbobonc. His booth always has a
curtain.

=== page 27 ===
4. Boatman’s Warehouse
The Veins of Illicit Trade
Occupying nearly a third of the Boatman’s Tavern and
Market structure, the Warehouse of Nulb is the
lifeblood of the town’s shadow economy. Facing the
swamp-stained piers, this vast, sagging structure hums
with constant activity: loading, lifting, shifting, and
hiding. By day, it appears a busy trade depot; by night, it
becomes the artery of the Temple’s supply network,
where goods vanish from the manifest and reappear
bound for the dark halls of Elemental Evil.
Structural Layout & Entry Points
Pier-Side Cargo Doors: Two pairs of towering ironbound oak doors open to the Nulb docks. Wagons
and barges pull in under cover of fog, guided by dim
lanterns and thick rope lines.
Interior Access: Heavy oak doors connect to both the
Indoor Market Hall and the Boatman’s Tavern,
allowing fluid movement of goods, guards, and
informants.
Basement Access: A set of stone steps near the back
wall leads down into the basement storage and
secret prisoner room (see below).
Second Floor Access: A set of rickety wood stairs
hugs the western wall, climbing up to a gallery level
above. A wooden crane platform, centered in the
floor opening, is used to hoist crates from dock
wagons or basement lifts. A worn winch system
remains in service, though prone to loud creaks.
Main Floor Inventory
The main floor is a cluttered tangle of:
Crates, barrels, and pallets of standard goods.
Dried fruits, smoked meats, cheap wine, bulk cloth,
rope, wax, tools, nails, wagon parts, and mundane
arms and armor.
Stamped goods from Dyvers, Verbobonc, and Wild
Coast merchant houses.
Second Floor: Private Quarters &
Smuggler’s Cache
Crane Platform: Suspended over the warehouse
floor, this platform allows cargo to be lifted to or
from the second level.
Locked Cargo Room: Tucked behind a reinforced
iron door, this chamber stores all high-value, illicit
Temple-bound goods: ritual supplies, sacred idols,
rare alchemical reagents, and blackmail documents.
The lock is complex, magically trapped (DC 18
Investigation or Thieves’ Tools to open).
Servant & Guard Rooms: A secured hallway leads to
the small sleeping quarters for Lodriss’s personal
thugs and the two serving wenches (Ketta and
Norla). Each room is sparse but heavily locked. The
hallway is patrolled and trapped against intruders.
Basement Level: Contraband Storage &
Secret Prison
The stone staircase from the main level descends into a
cool, dark storage space. Illicit trade goods such as
banned books, magical arms, stolen relics, elemental
charms, and poisons are stored here in moisture-proof
crates. A false wall in the rear of the basement leads to
the Secret Prisoner Room:
Five reinforced slave cages with shackles, lined with
straw and alchemical sedatives.
Used for holding captives prior to transfer to Captain
Vesrek, cult rites, or ransoms.
Guarded discreetly by Crimson Reaper enforcers
under direct supervision of Lodriss.
Scene: Warehouse Confrontation
You step into the warehouse and are hit by the stench of
mildew, pitch, and sweat-soaked timber. Dust motes hang
like ghosts in the lanternlight, suspended above rows of
stacked crates and dangling coils of rope. A gust of river
breeze creaks the oak doors behind you shut with a thud.
Then, boots scrape across the stone floor—slow,
deliberate. Two men emerge from behind a stack of barrels
near the central aisle. One is broad-shouldered with a
sagging eye and an iron-ringed cudgel. The other, lean and
sharp-eyed, rests a hand on the pommel of a curved blade.
The broad one speaks first, voice like gravel soaked in ale.
“This ain’t no market stall, friend. Only names on a ledger
walk in here.”
He taps his cudgel twice against the floor. “You see your
name anywhere?”
The wiry thug flanks you with casual menace, circling a
few feet to the side. “Not smart, poking where you ain’t
wanted. Some crates bite back. Others scream.”
He grins, revealing three gold teeth. “If Lodriss knew you
were sniffin’ around unsupervised……she’d charge us extra
for the cleanup.”
The larger one takes a step closer. “So unless you’re here
to load freight or unload secrets—turn your boots around.
Or we’ll be selling that armor off your corpse by sundown.”

=== page 28 ===
4. Boatman’s Tavern Basement
The Forgotten Depths Beneath the Ale
Beneath the worn timbers and riotous laughter of the
Boatman’s Tavern lies something far darker than old
kegs and salted meat. The basement complex, hidden
behind a trapdoor cleverly concealed behind the bar, is
a decaying warren of shadows—a haven for smuggling,
detention, and torture. While most believe it to be a
simple storeroom, it houses a chilling secret known only
to Tolub, Lodriss, Selentis, and a trusted few.
Tolub’s Smuggler’s Chamber (Northern
Basement)
This low-ceilinged, torch-lit chamber behind reinforced
warehouse doors is Captain Tolub’s private landing
zone for illicit river cargo. The flooring is stone-set,
permanently damp, with moss creeping between the
cracks. Stacked crates and unlabeled barrels are piled
up like a maze, their contents hidden beneath tarps.
Contents: Spices from distant ports, crates of stolen
textiles, black-market weapons, and barrels of
Velunese wine—all looted during Tolub’s river raids.
Dock Access: At low tide, a concealed ramp opens to
the rear pier, hidden beneath a trapdoor disguised as
a freight-loading dock. Slaves, weapons, or rare
cargo can be quietly moved in and out.
Security: Two of Tolub’s crew members always
remain nearby, armed with cutlasses and orders to
kill anyone snooping. Some crates are rigged with
tripwire noisemakers.
Relationship to the Temple: Tolub stores and
delivers Temple-bound goods here, though he
resents their control. He is tolerated by Selentis and
Lodriss for the usefulness of his spoils.
Main Tavern Storage (Main Basement)
Located at the foot of the wharfside stone steps, this
section is used for the Boatman Tavern’s day-to-day
operations. Compared to the rest of the basement, it
smells of grain and brewing yeast. A long row of dusty
wine racks line the back wall, housing bottles of local
red, fermented berry mash, and a few exotic imports
taken from pirate loot. Smoky wall-mounted oil lanterns
flicker and cast long shadows over crates and barrels,
giving the room a dim glow. Moisture clings to the
stone, and a faint mist creeps in from the pier with each
tide, curling along the ground like a ghost. Stacked
casks of ale and piles of salted meat are bound with
thick rope and labeled with crude chalk tags.
Contents: Ale barrels, smoked fish racks, sacks of
barley, wheels of aged cheese, dried fruit, and
tankards of spiced root mash.
Signs of Overlap
Keen eyes may
notice duplicate
barrel marks or
mismatched
manifests—a clue
that legitimate and
smuggled goods
occasionally blur.
