=== page 76 ===
Pirate Crew Aboard The Iron Dagger
The pirates of The Iron Dagger aren’t just nameless
cutthroats—they’re feared and infamous along the
Velverdyva. Each has earned their place through blood,
betrayal, and brutal efficiency.
“Only two rules aboard the Dagger: Don’t cross the Captain,
and don’t drop the rum.”
Command Crew
First Mate: Marlen “Splitjaw” Tosk (CR 1/2 | Bandit
Captain variant) A wiry, sunburned man with a cleft
lower lip and a voice like rusted chain. Brutal and
cunning, he runs the ship when Tolub’s ashore.
“Order’s the difference between a crew and a pile of
corpses.”
Second Mate: Della “Nails” Vaust (CR 1/2 | Thug) A
grim-faced woman with black gloves and callused
hands. Oversees smuggling and cargo—her hammer
keeps order in the hold. “Every box tells a story.
Most of ‘em involve screaming.”
Bosun: Droggin “Clatter” Melk (CR 1/4 | Bandit) A
hulking ex-miner with missing teeth and a limp.
Keeps the crew in line with knotted rope and
backhanded slaps. “Rig wrong once and I’ll have
your fingers in the bilge.”
Specialists
Boarding Mate: Corlin “Hookeye” Jass (CR 1/4 |
Guard variant) Scarred and bearded, with a brass
hook over his missing left eye. Leads the charge
when boarding enemy vessels. “I like ‘em screaming
when we board. Screaming makes it sporting.”
Boarding Mate: Tam “Ratknife” Bell (CR 1/4 | Guard
variant) Gaunt and twitchy, with a long scar down his
cheek and too many hidden blades. “I do my best
work in the dark—close and personal.”
Elite Sailor: Lurin “Crow’s Nest” Dask (CR 1/8 |
Scout variant) One-eyed sharpshooter and self-styled
lookout commander. Keeps a nest of pigeons for
coded messages. “Ain’t much you can’t see from up
high. Especially when someone’s lyin’.”
Elite Sailor: Jeska “Six-Fingers” Mirel (CR 1/8 |
Scout variant) Slender and silent, missing her left
ear and infamous for her deadly aim. “Put a bolt in
an eye at forty paces. That’s not luck—that’s
practice.”
Crewmen (Pick or Roll Names)
These 12 regular sailors form the bulk of the Iron
Dagger’s working crew. Each has their own tales—many
not worth repeating—and most would slit your throat for
a silver piece if Tolub wasn’t watching.
Brigg “Shivs” Mallor, Hegg “Two-Toes” Dann, Sorli
Red, Grent of Dyvers, Bask the Younger, Cindrel
“Lockjaw”, Tornic Stave, Old Marran, Wix “the
Whistle”, Falla Rake, Donnet “Gallows” Gurn, Kree of
the Cold Marsh.
Operations and Activities of The Iron
Dagger
The Iron Dagger isn’t just a ship—it’s a floating weapon
of intimidation and profit. Under Captain Tolub’s brutal
leadership, it carves a blood-slicked wake up and down
the Velverdyva, ferrying contraband, terror, and
whispers of darker alliances.
Black-Water Raids & River Tribute
The Dagger doesn’t waste time with threats. Merchants
who don’t pay Tolub’s “dock dues” are dragged ashore,
stripped, and left to rot—or chained and sold. River
traffic that refuses to kneel finds itself boarded at night,
gutted at dawn. Survivors, if any, are sold at quiet
anchorages further south.
“They don’t call it a dagger for nothing. Cuts deep, and never
clean.”
Smuggling for the Cult
Tolub’s loyalty lies in coin, but even coin has patterns.
His crew ferries black-market cargo for the Cult of the
Crushing Wave—crates of forged blades, amphorae of
harsh spirits, and relics best left sealed. Smuggled
goods vanish into hidden cellars or through secret trails
toward the Temple of Elemental Evil.
Nulb: Harbor of Sins
Nulb is more than a hideaway—it’s home turf. The Iron
Dagger docks at the east end of the old dockworks,
where the Boatman’s Tavern serves as Tolub’s
backroom office and informal hiring hall. Uses the
Boatman’s Warehouse to stoe cargo. There, he trades
favors, hires muscle, and bribes Lodriss and Skole to
trade cargo to Madame Selentis for the TOEE.
Tactics & Terrain
The Iron Dagger is sleek, shallow-keeled, and deadly.
She lurks in tributaries, strikes fast, then slips into
swamp-shadow. Grappling hooks and gangplanks are
her teeth—her crew the snapping jaws. Combat is short,
brutal, and merciless.
Reaction Upon Recognizing Adventurers
Tolub, a savvy and seasoned pirate, knows that
adventurers often pose a threat. When he recognizes
such individuals in his territory, he considers several
possible responses based on his evaluation of their
strength:
Feigning Ignorance: Tolub often pretends to be a
mere brawler and tavern regular, inviting the
adventurers to drink and gamble with him. This
casual demeanor lulls the characters into a false
sense of security. If they fall for the ruse, he subtly
signals his crew to launch a surprise attack, using
the opportunity to rob or capture them.

Verbobonc 576cy, Click here to Top


=== page 77 ===
Deflecting and Deceiving: In instances where he
deems the adventurers too dangerous to confront
directly, Tolub feigns ignorance while subtly
deflecting their attention. He directs them toward the
Hall of the Scarlet Moon, spinning tales of possible
answers to their quest there. Meanwhile, he
discreetly dispatches a bandit to warn the Fire
Prophet, who will then prepare an ambush for the
adventurers.
Immediate Assault: If Tolub is confident in his
advantage—or if he’s cornered without an easy
escape—he attacks the adventurers directly, calling
on his crew for backup. Tolub fights ferociously,
relying on his magic greataxe and leather armor
reinforced with magical protection.
Meeting Captain Tolub
As you step into the dimly lit Boatman’s Tavern, the
raucous laughter and clinking of mugs fade to a low
murmur as the patrons notice your entrance. At the
center of it all, a hulking figure with a mane of shaggy
hair and a thick beard squints in your direction, his
scarred hands wrapped around a tankard. This is Tolub
—Captain of the Iron Dagger, leader of the river pirates,
and unmistakably the man in charge here. His eyes,
sharp and calculating, sweep over you, taking in every
detail of your gear and stance.
He raises his tankard in a mock salute, his voice a
rough rumble that cuts through the smoky air. “Well
now,” he drawls, his tone friendly but laced with
curiosity, “ain’t often I see fresh faces strollin’ into my
tavern, and lookin’ so… well-armed, too.” He takes a
slow, deliberate sip of his drink, eyes never leaving
yours. “What brings you lot to Nulb, eh? Sightseein’? Or
perhaps…” he pauses, letting his gaze linger just a
moment too long, “a bit of work?”
You can feel the eyes of his companions narrowing in
on you, their postures shifting as they settle back to
watch. Around Tolub’s table sit four of his crew—a
ragged, dangerous-looking bunch. Each one bristles
with rough-hewn confidence and the scars of a hard life
on the river. The largest of them, a grizzled brute with a
crooked grin, chuckles low under his breath, nudging
the wiry sailor next to him with an elbow. “Fresh meat,
eh?” he mutters, loud enough for you to hear, and his
grin widens as he sizes you up.
Another pirate, a slender, sharp-eyed woman with a
mess of wild hair, lazily runs a finger along the edge of
her dagger. She doesn’t take her eyes off you, and
there’s a gleam of something dangerous in her gaze—a
silent dare, as if she’s measuring how much fight you’ve
got in you.
Tolub raises his tankard again, casting a sidelong
glance at his first mate, a scarred, one-eyed brute who
leans in close. “You reckon they’re lookin’ for work or
trouble, Cap’n?” he drawls, his voice a rough whisper,
though he doesn’t seem too concerned about keeping it
private.
You sense a mixture of interest and suspicion in his
eyes, as though he’s already weighing your purpose. He
leans forward, voice dropping to a near whisper, though
you’re certain everyone nearby is listening. “See, folk
like you don’t wander into this town without a reason.
Not unless you’re lost… or lookin’ for somethin’
specific.” He flashes a grin, his teeth glinting in the low
light, but his eyes stay cold. “So, which is it? Friends of
Madame Selentis, perhaps? Or… friends of the law?“
Tolub’s grin fades just slightly, and he watches you
with a measured look. “Y’see, Nulb’s got all sorts,” he
continues, tapping his fingers rhythmically on his
tankard, “traders, rivermen, and folks who don’t take
kindly to strangers askin’ too many questions.” He
gestures around the room, where eyes flicker away from
you—either out of caution or quiet threat. “Lucky for
you, I’m a curious sort, and I like knowin’ who’s who
around here. So… how ‘bout we skip the pleasantries?
You tell old Tolub who you are, and maybe, just maybe,
I’ll tell you what you’re gettin’ yourself into.”
Around him, his crew watches you closely, fingers
tapping on tankards or resting on weapons, muscles
tense and ready. The atmosphere thickens with the
weight of their suspicion, each one daring you to give
the wrong answer. He leans back, crossing his arms
over his chest, and tilts his head, waiting. The weight of
his gaze feels like a test.
Tolub’s Relationship with Key Figures
Lodriss: the owner of the Boatman’s Tavern and
Tolub’s lover, plays a significant role in Tolub’s
operations. While she maintains a veneer of
independence, she is loyal to Tolub and helps him
manage his affairs in Nulb. Lodriss often provides
information and handles some of the logistical
details of Tolub’s business, allowing him to focus on
larger matters. Although their relationship is largely
one of convenience and mutual benefit, there is
genuine affection between them.
Belsornig: Tolub is a high-ranking member of the
Cult of the Crushing Wave, where he serves as an
enforcer and ally to Belsornig, the Water Prophet.
Tolub often transports goods and personnel for the
temple and has been known to meet with other
temple agents in Nulb. While he doesn’t fully
subscribe to the cult’s fanaticism, Tolub sees the
partnership as beneficial to his goals and remains a
staunch supporter as long as it serves his interests.
Madame Selentis: Tolub views Madame Selentis
(Nysera Krivaltis ) as a valuable ally but a potential
threat. Their relationship is transactional, with both
recognizing the other’s usefulness in maintaining
Nulb’s chaotic equilibrium. Tolub secretly gathers
information on Madame Selentis plans, wary of her
ambitions.
Rival Crews: Tolub sees rival pirates like Captain
Vesrek as nuisances rather than serious threats,
though he ensures his dominance by sending clear,
brutal messages to those who challenge him.

Pirates of The Crimson Trader
The crew of a The Crimson Trader functions much
more like a military ship than a typical pirate operation.
As such, there is no pirate charter, and each member of
the crew is payed a base amount of coins weekly along
with the possibility of earning additional bonuses should
hauls be particularly good. The rules of this ship are
different because it is part of a much larger
organization. The party should notice that this is a
powerful ship with hardened pirates on deck. A level of
intimidation should be apparent. The players are
unlikely to fare well in a direct assault.
Discipline is the only law aboard this ship—break it, and you’ll
meet the lash or the blade.” - Captain Vesrek
Operations & Activities
Under the ruthless command of Captain Marad Vesrek,
the Crimson Trader is integral to the dark logistics of
the Temple of Elemental Evil, serving primarily as a
slaving vessel that brings human cargo and contraband
into Nulb. With regular stops in Nulb timed to coincide
with Temple needs, Vesrek ensures a steady supply of
prisoners and goods reaches key Temple figures.
Raiding and Capture: Vesrek’s crew ambushes
merchant ships, isolated villages, and unguarded
caravans along the Velverdyva River, capturing
victims to supply Nulb’s thriving slave market.
Smuggling Operations: Concealed compartments
aboard the ship transport illicit goods for Nulb’s
black market, facilitated through Lorveth “The
Broker” and Lodriss at the Boatman’s Tavern.
Temple Logistics: The Crimson Trader regularly
delivers captives directly to Temple contacts such as
Barkinar at the Greater Temple and Canon
Belsornig of the Water Temple, solidifying Vesrek’s
standing within the Temple’s dark hierarchy.
Nulb Ties & Rivals
Captain Tolub (Iron Dagger): Rivalrous yet
occasionally cooperative. Both captains have
temporarily allied to launch coordinated raids.
The Broker: Essential business partner; handles
distribution of slaves and contraband within Nulb.
Regularly negotiates exclusive deals with Vesrek
Madame Selentis: Sees Vesrek as both a valuable
asset and potential rival. She indirectly taxes and
closely monitors his operations through her agents.
Canon Belsornig: Primary Temple contact; regularly
receives slaves and contraband from Vesrek,
providing temple contracts.
Lodris & Skole: Operate a locked sub-cellar beneath
the tavern as Vesrek’s drop-box. Captives are tallied
and disguised as “market stock,” then routed either
upstairs to the Broker’s Brothel or by night cart to
the Hunting Cottage.
Crew of the Crimson Trader
Captain Marad Vesrek, the Crimson Trader
Click here A predator in captain’s garb, Vesrek is a man
of precision and cruelty. With sharp eyes and a scarred
right hand, he commands with a quiet, deliberate
menace. Born in Safeton’s slums on the Wild Coast,
Vesrek rose through the ranks with grit and guile. His
ties to the Slave Lords and rumored dealings with the
Scarlet Brotherhood have turned him into more than
just a pirate—uses Nulb as a piece on a larger board​.
Traits: Manipulative, ruthless, intelligent
Quirks: Frequently sharpens his shark-tooth hilted
rapier mid-conversation
Base of Operation: The Boatman’s Tavern
Karith “Scar” Drayal – First Mate Click here
Once a corsair of the Hold of the Sea Princes, Scar is a
grizzled man with a brutal sense of discipline and
tactical brilliance. His face bears the mark of a betrayal
—three deep scars across his jaw from a mutinous lover.
He is fiercely loyal to Vesrek but keeps his own secrets.
His barked orders crack like cannon fire, and none
aboard the Crimson Trader question her resolve.
Background: Formerly of the Sea Princes; joined
Vesrek after sinking her mutinous ship
Role: Oversees daily operations, training, and whip
discipline among the deckhands

This ragtag collective of sailors, raiders, and saboteurs
form the backbone of the Crimson Trader. Known as

wear knotted across their chests, they range from quiet
killers to cackling firebugs. A few are ex-soldiers, others

Crew & Captives of The Crimson Trader

The Crimson Trader – Slaver Galley
The Crimson Trader is a flat-bottomed galley built for
stealth and speed, cutting silently across the rivers and
coastal inlets of the Flanaess. With a hull blackened by
pitch and compartments hidden beneath the deck, this
vessel ferries slaves, cult offerings, and contraband for
the Temple of Elemental Evil. While docked in Nulb or
Narwell, it masquerades as a merchant vessel—but
when it hoists its infamous purple sails, blood follows.
Ship Type: Flat-bottomed slaver galley
Home Port: Safeton; often docked discreetly in Nulb
Armament: Iron-plated ram, mounted ballistae
Features: Concealed smuggling reinforced holds
Captain’s Quarters: Trapped chest (poison needle).
75pp, 400 gp, and 500 sp; Fire Opal Gem 500 gp.
Barracks: Holds well-armed warriors in splint mail.
Cargo Hold: Often contains 27–28 slaves in
deplorable conditions.
Captain Vesrek Secrets and Motivations
Born in the slums in Safeton of the The Wild Coast ,
Vesrek rose from a life of destitution by sheer will and
brutality. The son of a dockworker and a washerwoman,
Vesrek grew up in squalor, learning early the value of
wit and ruthlessness. His early years as a dockside
enforcer taught him the value of leveraging fear and
alliances. A fateful encounter aboard the Iron Tide,
where he saved his captain from mutiny, marked the
beginning of his rise in the ranks. After years of service,
Vesrek commandeered his first ship, the Crimson
Trader, which became his ticket to wealth and infamy.
Motivations
Captain Vesrek is driven by power and wealth. While he
serves the Slave Lords and the Temple of Elemental
Evil, he harbors ambitions to expand his influence
further. The discovery of the artifact like the Yellowskull
could become an obsession if he learns of its existence.
Scarlet Brotherhood Operative: Uses his piracy to
secretly funnel intelligence and resources back to the
Brotherhood; keeps meticulous hidden ledgers.
Hidden Ledger: Detailed records of his illicit
operations with Lorveth, the Temple, and the Scarlet
Brotherhood—potentially devastating if exposed.

A
Madame Selentis & The Greater Temple Cell
velvet knife runs Nulb. Madame Selentis
smiles from the ruined balcony of the Old
Mayor’s Manor and counts cargo in men,
coin, and secrets. She is Hedrack’s quiet
hand in the village—the broker of silence,
the keeper of routes, the one who makes
sure the Temple is a rumor until it isn’t. Her
“guards” are not town watch; they are temple brigands
in plain coats, drilled to move at night, vanish by dawn.
“Order is a story we tell the frightened. I sell the ending.”
Organizational Overview
Role: Greater Temple controller of Nulb logistics,
discipline, and deniability
Base: 33. Old Mayor’s Manor (walled lot; shuttered
façade; active by night)
Chain of Command: Reports to Hedrack;
coordinates shipments with Feldrin (Temple
logistics master)
Forces (“Temple Brigand Guards”): ~28–34 regulars
(bandits/thugs), 6 veterans (squad leaders), 1
lieutenant (captain statline)
Cover: “Estate stewards” who “collect late taxes” for
a dead mayor; no temple insignia in public
Rule: Keep Nulb dirty, busy, and small. Make every
problem look like pirates and bandits—not priests.
The Old Mayor’s Manor (Command Post)
Sagging portico, boarded windows, garden gone to
nettles; two lanterns only ever lit together when a
convoy is incoming.
War Room: river charts, rota boards, wax-sealed
tallies from Boatman’s Market and Waterside.
Cellars: lock-pens (short hold), counterfeit tools, dye
vats, and a trapdoor to a rat-run to the next cottage.
Signals: raven cage on the roof; three short peals on
a cracked bell = scatter to sites “1–4”.
Readiness: Daylight skeleton crew (6). Night ops
deploy in 2–3 fireteams of 6–8 with a runner each.
What Selentis Actually Runs
The Nulb Funnel: She and Feldrin time river drops,
market intake, and night carts to the 55. Hunting
Cottage and its tunnel to the Central Oval Cavern.
From there freight, recruits, and prisoners are sorted
deeper into the ruins.
Plausible Deniability: All hand-offs pass through
“criminal” faces—Lodriss & Skole at the Boatman’s
Tavern/Market, The Broker upstairs (brothel), and
hired teamsters across the bridge.
Discipline: Bribes logged, witnesses bought, loose
tongues cut. If blood must be spilled, Smigmal
Redhand’s people do it outside town.
Madame Selentis is not a queen of criminals or a selfstyled ruler of Nulb. She is something far more
dangerous—a loyal servant of Supreme Commander
Hedrack, sent to the lawless village to safeguard the
Temple of Elemental Evil’s covert operations. Once a
noblewoman of Verbobonc, she was marked for
execution after her father’s betrayal during the 569 CY
uprising. Hedrack ordered her extraction and placed
her under the watchful direction of Lucius Graeme. She
now serves as Hedrack’s political shadow in Nulb,
quietly stabilizing the village’s chaotic factions to protect
the Temple’s supply routes and recruitment channels.
From Noble Exile to Temple Agent
Family Disgrace: In 569 CY, Lord Eldris Krivaltis
was exposed and executed for providing intelligence
and aid to the Temple of Elemental Evil. The family
was stripped of land and title.
Lucius Graeme’s Intervention: Acting on Hedrack’s
orders, Lucius rescued the young noblewoman from
prosecution. She vanished from public records with
forged documents, false burial rites, and reappeared
in Nulb ten years later under Temple protection.
False Identity: From that point forward, Nysera
became Madame Selentis, a minor noble widow
from the Kron Hills with trade ties to Dyvers. Her
true name is classified as a Temple Secret by
Hedrack’s direct decree.
Purpose Reforged: Nysera no longer seeks
restoration or noble status. Her role now is to serve
the will of the Elder Elemental Eye and Hedrack’s
command, ensuring Nulb remains a critical node in
the Temple’s resurgence.
“Madame Selentis” is just noble enough to command
respect in dockside dealings, and just obscure enough to
escape scrutiny by more zealous cultists. Her mask is a
masterpiece of survival, forged in the flame of disgrace.

Command Structure
Madame Selentis: Click here Agent of the Greater
Temple. Charismatic and ruthless. Proxy,

Sir Torvel Hawkes: Click here Commander, loyal to

Temple Guard Captain Krael Vortash: Operations

Temple Brigand Guards (Her Men)
Composition: 18–24 total brigands.

Equipment & Uniform
Black-and-white tunics bearing the raven emblem

Keep Waterside Hostel violent but “ordinary” (let

Daily Operations & Strongholds

cottage across the Imeryds Run.
Old Mayor’s Manor Garrison: Guards patrol the
perimeter and watch the upper balcony.
Mobile Squads: Patrol the village streets in pairs or

They notably avoid open confrontations in the
Boatman’s Tavern, aware of its ties to Temple

Relationships & Levers
Hedrack (Supreme Commander): Gives objectives,

Smigmal Redhand (Broken Tower): Shared

Romag / Belsornig / Alrrem: She plays them like

Boatman’s Tavern & Market (Lodriss & Skole): Firststage intake. They get skim and protection; she gets

The Broker (Brothel): Converts “cargo” into coin or

Constable Malvaar: A paper shield. She feeds him

Stables (51): Stablemaster Varek is paid to count

River Pirates:

DM Notes & Tactics
First Contact: PCs notice “laborers” with matching
rope wraps on the left wrist.
Soft Pressure: Selentis always offers a legal fiction
—“You are trespassing,” “Those crates are city
taxes”—and a way to walk away poorer and alive.
Escalation Clock: Each public disturbance advances
a 4-step track: Watchers → Shadowing → Street
Edit (staged brawl) → Night Knock (home invasion).
Paper Trail Treasure: Seizable ledgers at the Manor
tie Boatman’s cellars → Broker → Hunting Cottage
by initials and weights, not names. Decoding them
exposes Feldrin’s calendar.
Misdirection Machine: When holy PCs arrive, her
agents nudge them to:
Shattered Monastery (Earth)
River Fort on Imeryd’s Run (Water)
The Etters watchtower (Fire)

Time
Activity
Day
Paperwork, bribes, and listening. Couriers to Dyvers and Verbobonc markets. Guards in workman’s clothes.
Dusk
Spotters take posts at Bridge, Waterside, Boatman’s piers, and Stables (51). “Lost mule” lantern warning signal.
Night
River off-loads (Tolub or Vesrek) → cellars under Boatman’s → Broker sorts → Selentis’ runners cart select crates or

Predawn
Streets washed, bodies gone, books balanced. Nulb wakes “normal.”

=== page 82 ===
S
House Velkori — The Rhenn Attloi Family
outh of the shadowed heart of Nulb, where
the old Pilgrim’s Way curves toward the
haunted ruins of the Temple of Elemental
Evil, a camp of brightly painted wagons rests
just inside the treeline of the Gnarley Forest.
This is the traveling home of the Attloi, a rare
and shunned branch of the Rhennee people
who have forsaken the waterways for the land.
Dismissed as traitors by their seaborne kin and
distrusted by the villagers of Nulb, the Attloi endure,
ever adaptive, ever elusive—merchants, mystics, thieves,
and survivors.
Though they trade wares and services openly in
Nulb’s grimy taverns and dockside alleys, their true
camp lies downriver, tucked in the tall grasses by the
Imeryds Run, where the smoke of their cookfires drifts
lazily toward the treetops and song under the stars.
Origins and Culture
The Attloi represent a landbound divergence from the
Rhennee’s barge-dwelling tradition, forming wagon
trains that wind through the back roads of the Flanaess.
Their identity is Rhennee to the core—insular, proud,
and cunning—but tempered by a hardened resilience
that comes from living under the scorn of both outsiders
and their own kin.
Their wagons are painted in ochre, rust-red, and
forest green, heavy with talismans and windchimes
carved from bone and horn. The Attloi speak Rhopan
among themselves and rarely, if ever, share it with
outsiders. Fortune-telling, animal husbandry,
leatherwork, and fire-juggling are common trades, but
beneath it all is a foundation of smuggling, spying, and
the illicit arts.
Despite facing prejudice from villagers, bandits, and
even fellow cult agents in Nulb, the Attloi continue to
conduct business with whomever has coin or secrets to
offer. Their moral compass skews toward survival—they
deceive outsiders with ease but adhere to strict codes
within their own bloodlines.
The Camp at Pilgrim’s Hollow
Set at the edge of the Gnarley Forest, just out of
bowshot from Nulb’s edge, the Attloi camp is a transient
ring of wagons known locally as Pilgrim’s Hollow.
Smoke curls from iron kettles, and children run
between drying lines of cloth and tanned hides. Elders
sit near the fire, sharpening blades or whispering fate
into cards.
During the day, Attloi adults walk into Nulb to trade,
steal, spy, and deliver messages—especially to the
Boatman’s Tavern or the contraband broker Lorveth
Thrask. At night, the camp remains lively, draped in
colored lanterns and flickering light. It is during these
twilight hours that stories are told, oaths made, and
sometimes dark deals struck beneath the gaze of stars
and spirits.
Activities in Nulb
Illicit Trade: Smuggled herbs, rare trinkets, and
minor magical items pass through Attloi hands to
fences in the Boatman’s Tavern.
Information Brokering: Vethra sells divinations and
secrets to those willing to pay.
Watchers of the Cults: Though they do not realize
the Temple is rising again in full, the Velkori are well
aware of Canon Belsornig ’s movements and unrest.
Camp Defense: The Attloi warriors are not many, but
they are fast, clever, and merciless. Woe to any who
try to rob their wagons.
Politics and Perceptions
In Nulb , the Attloi are seen with a mixture of disdain
and necessity. Pirates tolerate them for their wares,
while cultists hire them for errands too low for their
acolytes. Villagers suspect them of curses and theft.
Mistress Selentis does not interfere with their activities
—rumor suggests that Selentis has had her fortune read
by Old Eyes.
The Velkori family remains proudly neutral in Nulb’s
violent politics, dealing with everyone but pledging to no
one. Still, there are whispers that Vethra sees
something in the wind… something foul rising from the
old temple path, and she’s preparing to move the
wagons soon.
Motivations
Velkori Lineage Preservation: Above all, Vethra
protects her kin.
Power through Secrecy: Information is more
valuable than coin—and safer than loyalty.
Spiritual Sight: Vethra believes a great storm of fate
is rising in the east. She intends for her family to ride
the edge of it, not be crushed beneath it.
Concerns: Smigmal Redhand and the Broken Tower
Though the Attloi keep a low profile in Nulb, they are
not blind to the dangerous powers stirring beyond its
borders. One such threat is Smigmal Redhand , the
merciless Commander of the Outer Defenses for the
Temple of Elemental Evil. Her base of operations—the
Broken Tower—increased bandit traffic on the south
roads, and wagons laden with goods vanishing into the
wilderness.

=== page 83 ===
Vethra “Old Eyes” Velkori Click here
Matron, Fortune-Teller, and Diplomat. A short, ironwilled woman with clouded blue eyes and a mass of
silver curls wrapped in red silk. Vethra is both feared
and respected, not only for her piercing gaze that sees
through lies and futures alike, but for her brutal sense of
pragmatism. She reads omens in smoke, cards, and
bones and commands loyalty through wisdom and will.
“You ask me what the bones say? They say stay away from the
ruined temple. But you won’t listen. None of you ever do.”
Vethra Velkori – Introduction
You feel her before you hear her—the weight of a gaze
too old and knowing to belong to anyone still drawing
breath. A short, broad woman steps from behind a
curtain of copper bells, her clouded blue eyes fixed on
you as though she’s already read your bones. Her silver
curls spill from beneath a crimson scarf, and her fingers
—calloused and stained with ash—clutch a deck of worn,
curling cards.
She stops before you, close enough that you catch the
scent of old incense and wet earth.
“You carry the scent of choice, stranger,” she says,
her voice like dry leaves brushing stone. “The wind
follows you—but not always at your back.”
She lifts her chin slightly, tilting her head like a raven
considering prey.
“I am Vethra of House Velkori. Old Eyes, if you prefer
what the road calls me. Matron to these wagons, blood
to all who carry the brass braid.”
She taps the edge of her cards against her palm once
—soft, deliberate.
“Sit, if you like. I offer you three: smoke, card, or
bone. One for each path not yet chosen. The price? A
truth for a truth—yours for mine.”
Her eyes, pale as river fog, never leave yours.
“Deny it, and still the wind turns. Accept it, and
perhaps you will know which storm you ride.”
Eryk Velkori Click here
Role: Caravan Leader and Fire Dancer. The eldest of
Vethra’s sons, Eryk is charismatic and loud, his clothes
jingling with bells and braids. He handles trade in Nulb,
extorting bandits or making deals with the temple
agents or Selentis. He’s known to dance across burning
coals during festivals—and fights like a devil when
cornered.
Talla Velkori Click here
Role: Scout and Bladewoman. Talla is silent and sharp
as a flensing knife. She runs the southern woodline and
keeps watch on Nulb’s comings and goings. It is said
she once slit a bandit’s throat without drawing her blade
—just whispered in his ear and let his own fear kill him.
Orsik Velkori Click here
Role: Whisper-Walker and Spy. A boy of only seventeen
winters, Orsik trades in secrets, plying drunks for
information in the taverns and sniffing for weaknesses
in cult ranks. He’s already learned the names of Romag
and Belsornig’s lieutenants—and memorized their faces.
“There’s blood coming. Not coin, not secrets—
blood. I’ve seen the eyes of Redhand’s men. They don’t
look for profit. They look to kill.”
--- Talla to her kin around the fire

=== page 84 ===
A
The Forest Rats – A Brotherhood
cross the scattered homes and outposts
surrounding Nulb, a loose gang of boys has
formed, bound by hardship, mischief, and
an unspoken loyalty to one another. They
call themselves The Forest Rats, a name
earned from their countless hours darting
between trees, sneaking through village
alleys, and spying on the dealings of the dangerous
people who call Nulb home.
In the lawless village of Nulb, where mercenaries,
cultists, and cutthroats dictate the balance of power,
there exists a group of young survivors who refuse to be
swallowed by the darkness. They call themselves The
Forest Rats—a loose gang of farm boys, millers’ sons,
and orphans who navigate the dangerous world of Nulb
with quick wits, stealth, and reckless bravery.
Though dismissed as mere troublemakers by the
village’s criminals and overlords, these boys have seen
and heard more than most, making them a valuable—
and unpredictable—force in the brewing storm of the
Temple of Elemental Evil’s resurgence.
“Nobody pays attention to a bunch of boys climbing trees and
chucking stones. That’s why we know more than the lot of
them.” — Kiel Trosk
Origins of the Forest Rats
The boys of the Forest Rats hail from three distinct
homesteads on the outskirts of Nulb. Each family
struggles under the increasing control of the cult of the
Elder Elemental God, and the growing criminal
syndicates within the village.
With fathers and older brothers too occupied with
survival, these boys banded together for companionship,
protection, and adventure. Over time, their games of
hide-and-seek evolved into full-fledged scouting
operations, eavesdropping on criminals, tailing
suspicious strangers, and mapping out secret paths
through the Gnarley Forest.
Activities and Objectives
While largely seen as a band of mischievous boys, The
Forest Rats have grown into something more—a small
but vital information network within Nulb. They act
independently, without fully understanding the greater
forces at play, but their actions can significantly impact
the village’s balance of power.
Primary Activities
Scouting & Espionage: The boys sneak around Nulb,
watching the river pirates and the cultists of the Cult
of the Elder Elemental God.
Mapping Safe Paths: They maintain a mental map of
hidden trails through the Gnarley Forest, avoiding
bandit camps and dangerous areas.
Minor Sabotage: From loosening saddle straps to
placing obstacles in smuggler trails, their pranks
sometimes disrupt serious operations.
Trading Information: The boys keep tabs on
anything unusual happening in Nulb, and for the
right price (or trust), they might share what they
know.
Members of the Forest Rats
Kiel Trosk, The Scout (16): Click here Bramblethorn
Ranch (31): The cautious and calculating observer,
Kiel acts as the group’s strategist, carefully mapping
out their movements and keeping the others from
getting into too much trouble.
Gavrin Veyne, The Protector (19): Click here
Millhouse (30): The oldest of the group and its
unspoken leader, Gavrin’s strength and experience
make him the one the others look to in a fight.
Edris Veyne, The Daredevil (14): Click here
Millhouse (30): Eager to prove himself, Edris is
quick-witted and fast on his feet, often the first to
volunteer for risky scouting missions.
Edric Thorne, The Spy (14): Thorne’s Cottage (29):
A bold and daring boy, Edric often pushes the group
toward greater acts of rebellion, spying on Mistress
Selentis men from the trees.
Tomas Thorne, The Dreamer (9): Thorne’s Cottage
(29): The youngest of the group, Tomas doesn’t
participate in their riskier schemes but idolizes the
older boys, carving small wooden animals as tokens
of their adventures.
“They’re just kids, right? But my men keep coming
back with stories about a ‘ghost’ in the woods and
missing gear. So, either we got spirits with sticky fingers
or some brats need a lesson.” - Krael Vortash

=== page 86 ===
The Forest Rats
The Forest Rats are a dynamic way to introduce
elements of espionage, rebellion, and local knowledge
into the campaign. They may serve as allies, informants,
or even the catalyst for uncovering Nulb’s secrets.
1. Rat Hunt: The party learns that Madame Selentis
men are hunting for a group of boys accused of
stealing something valuable. Do the adventurers help
them or turn them in?
2. A Test of Trust: The Forest Rats have crucial
information about a hidden cult meeting, but they
won’t share it unless the adventurers prove
themselves as allies.
3. The Vanishing Boy: Tomas Thorne has gone missing
in the woods, and the older boys fear something
unnatural has taken him. Will the party help track
him down?
Nulb Constable (47)
1. A Broken System: Malvaar calls upon the
adventurers to assist in one of the few cases that
require the Constable’s intervention — a case
involving a corrupt merchant trying to sell off stolen
goods. The adventurers must decide whether to
expose the Constable’s weakness and the temple’s
control over him or help him save face.
2. Malvaar’s Last Stand: When the Temple decides to
dispose of the Constable after he begins questioning
his role in Nulb, Malvaar turns to the adventurers for
help. He will offer them critical information about
the Temple’s operations in exchange for their
protection. Will the adventurers help him make a
final stand, or let the corruption consume him?
3. The False Law Premise. A string of “accidents”
among the serfs of Aldren Valegrave at 26.
Valegrave’s Farmstead—thresher mishaps, ditch
drownings, grain-silo “slips”—has the village
whispering. Constable Edrick Malvaar stamps the
inquests as misadventure, but his seals are bought
and his courage leased. The deaths hide a darker
engine: the Greater Temple’s procurement route
overseen by Madame Selentis (with Feldrin’s
quartermasters in the background), using the farm
as a quiet staging point for recruits, prisoners, and
grain.
What’s Really Happening.
Selentis’s temple guards move night wagons through
Valegrave’s barn, then to the Nulb Stables (51) and on
to the Hunting Cottage (55) and its tunnel.
Malvaar is coerced: paid in coin, threatened with
“river justice.” He signs off every death to keep the
peace—his peace.
Tell-tale clues: blackcap residue (from Mother
Screng’s stock), unusual red wax seals on flour
sacks (Valegrave), and stables ledgers with erased
entries timed to the night runs.
How PCs Get In.
A bereaved aunt begs for truth at the Waterside
Hostel; or Screng slips the party a coded note: “Wax
and water don’t mix—ask the stable.”
Malvaar, cornered, pleads: “I’m no judge, I’m a
hinge. Push me—just don’t break the door.”
Scenes & Leads.
Farmstead Sweep: shallow graves behind the
millstream; shackled marks beneath calluses; a
hidden shrine plank with Selentis’s sigil.
Stables Audit: double-booked stalls, shaved brands,
ledger “ghost lines”; stablehands mention “redhaltered teams at moonrise.”
Night Wagon Sting: intercept the convoy to the
Hunting Cottage; temple sergeants carry pre-written
inquest slips bearing Malvaar’s seal.
Choices & Outcomes.
Shield the Constable (quiet justice): flip Malvaar as a
witness/informer; he feeds you timings and names,
keeping the law façade intact.
Expose Him Publicly (loud justice): the Greater
Temple dispatches hush crews; a bounty lands on
the party; Malvaar is removed (or “drowns”).
Cut the Head: seize the ledgers + wax seals; deliver
to Verbobonc agents (Otis/Cannoness Y’dey) for
wider action against the route.
Burn the Route: sabotage Valegrave’s wagons or
spook the Stables; Temple logistics reroute for 2–4
weeks, lowering Nulb heat and starving local cells.
Ties & Risks.
Selentis answers subtle slights with disappearances;
botch the sting and her sergeants escalate to
Smigmal’s cutouts.
River Pirates (Tolub) may be hired as movers; their
tar reek lingers on the bodies.
Reward: leverage over Malvaar, a live informant
network, and disruption to the Temple’s supply
chain—without tipping the whole uprising (yet).
Dunstan’s Boatwright (11)
1. The Last Nail: Beyard offers the party a hidden
message inside a wagon he is forced to build for the
Temple. Can they deliver it before it’s too late?
2. A Family in Chains: The Crimson Reapers decide to
take the Edreks hostage after Beyard refuses to craft
a hidden vault for stolen goods. The party must
intervene before the family disappears.
3. Tibber’s Tune: Tibber sings a song at the tavern that
contains coded information about a Temple
shipment—someone wants him silenced.
4. The Assassin’s Past: Madame Selentis demands to
know the truth about Leika, forcing the party to
decide whether to protect her or expose her past.
5. Blackmail Material: Tibber once saw a Temple
agent dragging a blood-soaked crate off a barge late
at night. He hasn’t spoken—yet.

=== page 87 ===
Dunstan Bravlin’s Tale of the
Peg-Leg and the Fens
Scene Setup The adventurers arrive at Bravlin’s
Dockhouse, where Dunstan and his son Orryn are hard
at work repairing a small riverboat—a battered skiff halfgutted by a monster’s claws. Dunstan’s whalebone pegleg taps a steady rhythm on the planks as he oversees
the shaping of new hull strakes.
Rain threatens the horizon. Fog clings to the water.
The smell of pitch, river rot, and swamp reeds hangs
heavy in the air.
Dunstan Bravlin (gruff, leaning on a rib of boat
frame): “You lot lookin’ for a ferry or a funeral? ‘Round
here, it’s often both.”
Adventurer: We heard you used to run the rivers.
Something about the Fens of Tor. You’ve seen
Zassil’torr?
Dunstan (scoffs, spits off the dock, nods slowly): “Aye.
I’ve seen it. Felt it too. Took my leg, didn’t it?”
He lifts his whalebone peg and knocks it once on the
dock for emphasis.
“Back then, I was no dockhand. I ran with a crew—
Bravlin’s Banner, they called us. Took a job for Tolub
hisself, running barrels of Daggercap Mushrooms and
silvered weapons up the Run, past the weeping reeds
and deep into the swamp-bog.”
Dunstan (voice low now, haunted): “We got too close
to Torfen. The lizardfolk called it Zassil’torr. Stilt-village
in the mist, bone lanterns swingin’ in the dark like
swampfire. Thought we’d trade. Offer iron tools and
steel knives for poison-frogs and bark tinctures. Good
trade, yeah? But we didn’t count on him…”
Orryn Bravlin (quietly, with respect): “The Witch
Doctor. Ssarkosh the Whispering Flame.”
Dunstan (nods gravely): “He was there. Painted in
blood and ash, his breath hissin’ like a steam kettle.
Said we’d come without the blessing of Semuanya. Said
we brought… rot into the waters. I tried to reason, but
my deckhand Drevik insulted a Marsh Mother. Called
her a ‘frog with breasts.’ Gods help us.”
Adventurer: What happened?
Dunstan (grips his knee, eyes far away): “They let us
leave. Thought we were safe. But an hour out, in the
deepest muck, they struck. Lizardfolk raiders with war
spears, gliding like ghosts on their swamp-lizards. Came
out of the reeds, no sound, no warning. Killed two men,
pulled me overboard. Something big bit my leg—thought
it was a croc, but it hissed. Spoke to me in Draconic.
Said I’d been marked.”
“When I woke up, I was back on the skiff, fevered,
blood everywhere. My leg gone from the knee. The
Witch Doctor let me live. I don’t know why. Maybe to
send a message.”
He leans in, voice low and grave.
“That swamp’s alive, friend. With gods and ghosts. If
you go pokin’ into Torfen, you best not blink. The
lizardfolk ain’t just beasts—they’re a people. Divided,
yes. But some want peace, others want our heads on
poles.”
Dunstan (spits again, this time into the fire pit): “Now
I build boats for those foolish enough to try again. Tolub
pays me well. So do the Temple’s men. Even the pirates
come to Bravlin’s Dock when their hulls are chewed by
marsh horrors. But me? I stay put. My sailing days died
with my leg in the black water of the Fens.”
Narration Option for DM:
Dunstan Bravlin’s tale hangs heavy in the damp air, the
rhythmic scraping of Orryn’s planer the only sound for a
moment. There is something else in his gaze—not just
regret, but fear, the kind born of a lesson learned in
blood. The kind that whispers of ancient gods still
watching from behind the swamp’s misty veil.
The Gallows Table (13)
1. A Rare Performer: A travelling bard is set to perform
in the square, but they secretly carry a message for
the adventurers, slipping it to them in plain sight
during their act.
2. A Public Execution: The party arrives in time to
witness a public execution—but the condemned
claims to have crucial information that could change
Nulb’s fate.
3. The Merchant’s Plight: A travelling merchant is
being harassed by a group of Crimson Reaper
Brigands in the square, and the adventurers must
decide whether to intervene.
4. The Cage’s Contents: The party hears strange noises
coming from the iron cage at night and investigates,
uncovering an unsettling secret.
5. Smuggler’s Meeting Spot: The square is used by
Felix Fahnor and the The Crimson Reapers as a
neutral meeting place for arranging trade routes.
Fishing Shack (10)
1. The Fisherman’s Secret: Bracken overhears critical
information about a significant shipment bound for
the Temple of Elemental Evil. Fearful for his family’s
safety, he seeks adventurers’ aid, offering to guide
them through the dangerous waters and marshes.
2. A Dangerous Favor: Annya asks adventurers to
deliver a secret shipment of moonshine and
medicinal herbs to 3. Mother Screng’s Herb Shop .
Unbeknownst to the party, this shipment also
contains documents stolen from Tolub’s pirates,
implicating them in dealings with the Temple.
3. Young Rebel: Edran is caught trying to sabotage a
pirate shipment. The adventurers must choose
whether to help Bracken free him, risking the wrath
of the pirates, or use the situation to gain leverage
with Tolub’s crew.
4. Unwanted Attention: Mira attracts the interest of
dangerous figures such as Skole or pirates wanting
to exploit her skills. The adventurers must intervene
to protect her, possibly drawing them into Nulb’s
darker political webs.

=== page 88 ===
Otis’s Smithy & Stable (2)
Otis keeps his head down, but he’s no common farrier—
he’s a covert ranger-knight watching the Temple’s
resurgence from behind the anvil. He’ll test strangers
before he risks his cover, offering work that looks like
errands and turns into intelligence-gathering,
interdiction, and rescue. His shop and stalls give him
reason to talk to everyone who matters in Nulb—drivers,
pirates, stablehands, smugglers—making the smithy a
natural quest hub.
Earning Otis’s Trust (quick gate)
Step 1 (Low risk): Discreet favors (deliver a “shoeing
chit” to the Nulb Stables (51); fetch lamp oil without
visiting the Waterside bar).
Step 2 (Proof): Bring back any one of: a red-wax sack
seal (Valegrave), a scrap of river-tarred line (Tolub’s
crew), or a ledger rubbing with “ghost lines” (erased
stall entries).
Step 3 (On mission): Otis shares timings, map
marks, and joins covert actions if the party shows
restraint and sense.
Hooks from the Forge
The Red Halter Run
Otis suspects night wagons are swapping teams under a
red halter at Nulb Stables (51) before vanishing toward
the Hunting Cottage (55). He wants eyes on the swap
and a count of guards—no heroics unless a prisoner is
spotted.
Hoofprint Ledger
Match odd shoes Otis has pulled off cult wagons to
tracks around Waterside and Boatman’s. A rubbing of
stall-boards and a sketch of nail patterns will expose
which stablemaster is cooking bookings.
The Lantern That Didn’t Come Home
One of Otis’s owl-couriers (used for message drops in
the Gnarley) is overdue. Track it to a riverside snare
near the Wharf; recover the reed-tube note before
pirates sell it. If returned unopened, Otis opens up—
literally—showing a corner of his cache.
Bread, Wax, and Blood
Follow a routine sack of Mavrek’s bread stamped with
Valegrave’s red wax. The route—Bakery → Waterside
back door → Stables → night wagon—proves the
provisioning chain. Swap one sack with a chalk-marked
twin to trace where it lands.
Black Bottle, Blackmail
A regular at Waterside pays with “Dick’s Black Bottle”
chits. Otis thinks it’s a hush-fund for Temple leavetroops. Win (or steal) a chit, then trade it to Wat for a
cask pickup time. Ambush? No—photographic memory:
note faces, livery, and which pier.
The Broker’s List
Madame Selentis keeps a rotating inventory upstairs at
Boatman’s (brothel) for Temple provisioning. Lift a
single page: names, weights, and a discreet “H.C.” mark
(Hunting Cottage). Bring it to Otis; he’ll cross-index
carts and shoe orders. (If caught, claim you’re checking
a room rate.)
Constable’s Quiet Turn
Deliver a bent nail (Otis’s signal) to Constable Malvaar
with the phrase, “Shoeing done before moonrise.” If
Malvaar meets you later at the bridge, he’s in—expect a
name and a night, but you must stage the arrest
yourselves.
The Reaper’s Order
The Crimson Reapers commission a batch of narrowbladed shortswords “for river work.” Otis pretends the
quenching failed; you “escort” the refund to Boatman’s
Warehouse and mark the counting-room lock with black
pitch so Otis can later ID the exact chest.
Whispers from the Broken Tower
A stablehand talks about grain sacks that jingle. Walk a
load as hired help toward the Hunting Cottage; if you
reach the dry well, plant a greased wedge so the tunnel
hatch won’t re-bar. Otis wants that exit to stay
“accidentally open” for a future pull.
Mother Screng’s Mismatch
Screng spots blackcap in “healing” draughts heading to
Boatman’s guards. Swap one crate for real salves; let
the Temple sergeant’s men realize they’re not getting
their usual sedatives before a job. Otis watches who
panics and adds a name to his board.
Fire That Isn’t Fire
Alrrem’s envoys are telling hotheads to “cleanse
heretics” at rival shrines. Otis wants that rumor
amplified—hand a forged prayer slip to the right
loudmouth at Waterside, then be across the river when
Water and Earth go to “purge” each other.
Last Light at the Wharf
On nights when the Wharf lantern gutters twice,
smugglers transfer prisoners. Otis can’t be seen there;
he asks you to cut the second wick and start a bar fight
at Boatman’s at that exact moment, forcing the transfer
to abort.
How Otis Reacts
Careful professionals: He shares timings, maps, and
eventually fights beside them on high-impact strikes
(never for bar-brawls or glory plays).
Loud heroes: He downgrades to indirect support—
tools, cover stories, and coin for witnesses.
If blown: He burns the shop trail (dogs, cache,
papers) and vanishes into the Gnarley, leaving one
steel token at the Waterside rafters: “Try again.”

Mother Screng’s Herb Shop (3)
On the wall behind Mother Screng’s cluttered counter
hangs a tattered, hand-scrawled list of available herbs.
To the average visitor, it looks like pricing and
descriptions of stock.
Hidden Function: To agents of Eluna, Verbobonc, or
Furyondy, this “inventory list” serves as a message
board coded with symbols and underlined letters.
Using a successful DC 15 Intelligence (Investigation)
check, an adventurer may decode:
*Arrival of allied agents
*Location of
safehouses
*Coded requests for
sabotage or
observation
*Emergency rally
points (e.g. “Gather
beneath the Grain
Tower”)
The coded list updates
weekly via homing
pigeons or Hruda’s
nighttime adjustments.
Adventurers who
uncover its meaning may
contact allies or receive
missions from distant
superiors, and
maintain cover.
Decoded Meaning for Observant or Aligned PCs:
“White raven” = Temple agent sighted in Nulb
“Traveler’s Grace” = a healing potion for contact
“Visitors from the East” = River Pirates or temple
agents sniffing around
Hruda’s warning = PCs may be under suspicion
Closing line = Message to allies: danger is near
Quests at Mother Screng’s
1. Herbs for the Wounded
A recent brawl at the Boatman’s Tavern has left several
wounded, including a young druid who needs rare herbs
to survive. Mother Screng needs someone to retrieve
Ghostcap Mushrooms from the southern Fens near the
haunted Monastic Hut.
Objective: Retrieve 3 Ghostcap Mushrooms from the
Fens of Tor.
Challenge: The area is crawling with undead and
swamp beasts.
Reward: Healing potions and favor from Mother
Screng.
2. The Bitter Brew
A local pirate is spreading a new brew laced with
poison. Mother Screng suspects the Iron Lash is behind
it and needs someone to confirm the source and retrieve
a sample.
Objective: Obtain a flask of the tainted brew from the
Iron Lash or Boatman’s Tavern.
Challenge: Sneak into the brothel or win the trust of
a pirate.
Reward: Spiderwort Decoction and a coded contact
passphrase for future messages.
3. The Missing Message
A homing pigeon sent to Verbobonc with a critical
warning hasn’t returned. Hruda fears the message was
intercepted and a courier must now deliver it by hand.
Objective: Escort a sealed scroll to Otis at his smithy.
Challenge: Bandits on the way may recognize the
party as allies of the resistance.
Reward: Rare elixirs and access to secret Temple
intelligence.
Harlow’s Cottage (54)
1. The Fisherman’s Final Gamble
Harlow knows that Nysera, the Crimson Reapers, and
the Cult all want something from him. He’s looking for a
way to tip the scales in his favor—and he’s willing to
take risks. Harlow might hire adventurers to help him
escape or turn factions against each other.
2. The Son’s Choice (Moral Conflict)
Jonas must choose between his father and his ambition.
He stays with his family, turn against the Reapers.
He joins the Reapers, against his father.
He turns to the Cult, becoming something far worse.
3. The Wife’s Revenge (Dark Twist Hook)
If Sera loses her husband, she won’t grieve—she’ll plot.
If Harlow dies, Sera might seek revenge against
Nysera, the Reapers, or even the players.

=== page 90 ===
Serena Daughter of Rhenn
Hook: A Father’s Shame, A Daughter’s Chains
Quest Type: Roleplay, Investigation, Rescue
Quest Level: Tier 1 (Levels 3–5)
Location: Nulb – Docks, Boatman’s Tavern, Brothel
(The Iron Lash), Rhenn Camp
On a moonless night, the party notices the usually
colorful Rhennee Rhenn-folk camp outside Nulb oddly
quiet. Talla Velkori, their scout, intercepts the party with
a wary glare and a whispered plea:
“Eryk’s daughter is gone. Taken. This land steals people in the
dark.” - Talla Velkori
If the adventurers speak with Eryk Velkori at his camp,
they find a broken man nursing bruises and shame. He
reveals that his daughter Serena, a quick-handed and
sharp-tongued girl of eighteen, vanished after a brawl at
the Boatman’s Tavern. The Rhenn had been drinking
and dancing, entertaining the river pirates, when
tensions with the Crimson Reapers exploded into
violence.
“I don’t remember the end. We woke up on the docks. Blood in
my mouth. Serena was gone.” - Eryk Velkori
Witnesses suggest Serena Click here was last seen in
the company of Lorveth “The Broker” Thrask, Skole,
and the sultry and silent Lodriss, a regular figure at the
Brothel. Eryk suspects a setup—he believes Serena was
sold to pay for damage caused during the fight.
Investigation Phase
Boatman’s Tavern and Nulb Market (4)
Speaking with Pearl or Dala (serving girls), or Captain
Tolub (if well-inclined), reveals that Serena was forcibly
dragged out after the brawl. A Reaper named Burgan
mentions “a debt repaid” and that Lorveth handed her
over to Elvanna Thorne at the brothel.
The Brothel of Nulb (22)
Talking to Elvanna reveals she now holds Serena as a
servant-slave—legally purchased through Nulb’s gray
market practices. She refers to Serena as
“compensation” for damages caused by the Rhenn at
the Boatman’s. She’ll smirk:
“If you want her back, it’ll cost you 500 gold. That’s the going
rate for beauty, debt, and disobedience.” - Elvanna
Players can negotiate, intimidate, pay, or plan a heist—
but brute force will bring down the full wrath of the
Temple agents and The Crimson Reapers.
Optional Subplot – Serena’s Story
If freed or rescued, Serena (Level 3 Thief, Chaotic
Neutral) opens up to the party:
Mona helped pay off a debt she didn’t even owe.
She’s been kept “safe” but under watch—used as
leverage.
She knows her father is being coerced into
ambushes along the Forest Road.
She is clever, wounded in pride, and has been
waiting for her chance to escape.
Resolution & Rewards
Buying Freedom (500 gp): Serena is released from
the Iron Lash. She returns to her family, and the
Rhenn’s trust is fully earned. The party gains
advantage with the Rhenn, and their inventory.
Rescuing Her by Force: Dangerous. The entire
brothel may be alerted. If successful, Serena flees to
the camp. The Rhenn are grateful, but The Crimson
Reapers and Lorveth place a bounty on the party.
Failing to Intervene: The Rhenn begin to quietly pack
camp. Within a week, they vanish from Nulb—along
with their information, influence, and underground
access.

=== page 91 ===
Eryk Velkori – “A Father’s Shame, A
Daughter’s Chains”
You step through the mist that clings to the muddy rise
outside Nulb, where the usually vibrant Rhenn camp
lies unnaturally still. The air smells of ash and river rot.
The jingle of bells is gone—replaced by silence thick
enough to choke on.
A shadow steps from the firelight. It’s him—Eryk
Velkori, leader of the caravan, eyes once full of heat and
fire now sunken, bloodshot, and rimmed with sorrow.
He clutches a half-drained bottle of Imerydy’s Rum, and
sways slightly with the weight of grief.
“So…” he rasps, barely above a growl. “You come
walkin’ in like crows on a corpse. Lookin’ for trade? Or
tales? Or maybe a map to the hells, eh?”
He stares at you through tangled braids and pain.
“She gone. My firelight. My Serena.” His voice cracks,
but his stare doesn’t waver. “Boatman’s Tavern saw the
last of ‘er. We were drinkin’, dancin’… even made the
Reapers smile. But I blinked, just once, and woke up
with blood in me mouth and nothin’ but a whisper on
the wind.”
He tosses the bottle into the fire with a hiss.
“Those bastards—Zelt’s rats, them Reapers. Or
maybe Nysera’s Talons dragged her to the Iron Lash,
thinkin’ she’s just another pretty neck for their chains.”
His fists clench, the bells in his sleeves silent for the
first time you can remember.
His voice hardens, a tremble of rage returning.
“I’m no seer like me mam… but I know this: Serena
didn’t vanish into smoke. She’s flesh, blood, and fight.
And I need folks what ain’t afraid to crawl through
pisswater and blade to get her back.” His eyes finally
meet yours, full of storm and steel.
“So. You got guts for ghosts? Steel for slavers? Or are
you just here for pity and songs? ‘Cause if you ain’t, then
step inside my firelight… and I’ll show you a father’s
shame worth burnin’ the world over.”
Vethra “Old Eyes” Velkori’s divination
Here is a follow-up scene with Vethra “Old Eyes”
Velkori’s divination, written in immersive second-person
dialogue, thick with Rhennee mysticism and drama. It
follows the moment after Eryk pleads for aid, and the
adventurers agree to seek answers. This scene can
serve as a narrative transition, giving the party a clear
but cryptic lead toward the Iron Lash, the Waterside
Hostel, or a crimson-marked barge.
Scene: “Smoke, Card, or Bone”
The fire dims to coals as Eryk steps aside, his breath
ragged in the silence that follows. Then, without a word,
the crowd of Rhenn clears. You feel it before you see
her: a gravity in the air, like a storm watching from
beyond the trees. Vethra Velkori sits cross-legged in the
shadows of her wagon, a worn blanket draped with
bones, blackened cards, and a copper bowl that smells
of clove and blood. Her clouded blue eyes don’t look at
you—they look through you.
“My boy burns with fury. That’s a path easy to follow,
easy to lose y’self in. But you…” her pale gaze settles on
you, “you got more than fists. You got fate. Sit.”
She gestures to the blanket.
“Smoke, card, or bone. The winds already whisper…
but I must listen proper.”
If the party chooses “Card”:
She fans out a deck of faded tarokka, her fingers quick
despite the years.
“Ahh… the Chain. The Betrayer. The Flooded Gate.”
Her lips tighten as she draws a fourth card and turns
it with a hiss of breath.
“A barge. Crimson-painted and cursed. Sailin’ low on
the Velverdyva, heavy with souls that ain’t singin’ no
more.”
She looks up at you. “She was taken there. Drugged,
bound, traded—like meat.”
If the party chooses “Bone”:
She tosses wolf knuckles and pigeon vertebrae into a
shallow bowl and rattles them with a low chant. The
bones click, scatter, fall. She leans close, inhaling the
shape they form.
Her voice darkens. “She may be on her knees, but she
ain’t broken yet. Not with my blood in her.”

If the party chooses “Smoke”:
She burns a lock of braided black hair, muttering in a
dialect older than Common. Smoke swirls, then shapes
—a crooked house with shifting shadows and a narrow,
high window.
“A tavern with too many secrets,” she says softly.
“The Waterside. It sees all that slips between coin and
curse.”
Then, fainter: “A man with a red sash and no soul—
watch him. He deals in whispers and iron.”
Conclusion
Vethra’s gaze sharpens, her voice as final as a dagger
drawn.
“Three paths. Only one holds her now—but the others
will bleed for tryin’. Choose fast, child. The river don’t
wait for grief.”
She leans back, exhausted, and the smoke clings to
the inside of your throat like a promise.
Valegrave Manor (26)
1. Breaking the Chains: A serf girl escapes Valegrave
Manor, begging the party for help. If the party
investigates, they uncover evidence of slavery and
dealings with the Temple. Will they destroy
Valegrave’s operation, or use him as an informant?
2. Intercept the Shipment: A caravan bound for the
Temple of Elemental Evil is set to depart from
Valegrave Manor. The party must stop the shipment,
uncovering evidence of the Temple’s supply chain.
3. Black Ledger: Hidden behind a wall panel in
Aldren’s bedroom is a stained ledger recording
prisoner trades, payoffs to Commander Feldrin, and
a bribe made to Lucius Graeme. The party is sent to
investigate, but if they find proof, Nysera will demand
swift retribution.
4. The Slave Rebellion: The serfs are preparing an
uprising, needing weapons and leadership. Will the

Breaking the Chains — the girl
behind the ruins
Scene setup (read aloud)
You pass a burnt-out cottage—charred ribs, ash
underfoot. A soft hiss, a waved hand. In the doorway’s
shadow, a mud-streaked girl in torn homespun beckons
you low. Her wrists are rubbed raw. She keeps glancing
at the road as if it bites.
Approach
She shrinks deeper into the ruin until you’re close
enough to smell smoke in her hair. She’s shaking, trying
to be brave.
She whispers, fast:
“Please don’t call out. They’ll hear. I… I ran. From the
farm. I need help. Real help.”
Her voice (use these lines as needed)
If you ask her name. “I’m Ivia. Just field work.
Turnips, barley… whatever they point at.”
If you ask who did this. “The master with the ledger
—Valegrave—and his whip-man. They say it’s ‘debt.’
It’s chains. Please don’t send me back.”
If you ask what she wants. “Please—stop the wagons
tonight or take me somewhere safe first. If you can’t
fight them now… take the book they hide. It has
names. Prices. He cares about his jounral.”
If you offer water, a cloak, or a calm word. (Tremble
eases; she speaks clearer.) “Thank you. There’s a
loose stone in the rear wall, big as a bread loaf. The
cellar door sticks—lift, then pull. The ledger’s under
a floorboard by his bed; plank next to chest.”
If you ask how the Temple is involved. “I don’t know
their prayers. I hear the men talk—‘deliveries for the
chapel under the earth.’ Some nights they bring
people, not sacks. The pirates get coin. The rest go
where th road turns to mud.”
If you ask who’s hunting her now. “The overseer.
They call him Dog-Tether. He follows the ditches so
you don’t see him. If I’m caught, they beat the others
till someone speaks.
If you agree to help. “Bless you. I’ll show you the
back lane and where the hedge is thin. I can’t go
inside again. I can wait at the old cart-yard by the
well. If you don’t come by moon-high, I’ll leave.”
What she knows (simple, true)
Timing: Two wagons leave after dusk—one toward
the Old Mayor’s Manor, one toward the marsh path.
Signs: Men with red cords on their sleeves handle
the wagons; a black-coat checks the book.
Routes: They avoid the High Road at night; cut
behind the stables and along the fence lines.
Proof: The ledger (names, payments), a broken iron
cuff in her pocket, and a grain chit stamped with
Valegrave’s mark.
DM notes (quick use at table)
Tone: Keep her scared but clear—short sentences,
breathy starts, flinches at shouts or whistles.
Trust switch: Any kindness (water/blanket/soft voice)
grants advantage on Persuasion/Insight checks with
her. Barked orders or flashing holy symbols in public
draw attention.
Complication: If the party raises voices or lingers, a
pair of Valegrave toughs circle the lane within 1–2
rounds (“Girl! You seen a runaway?”).
Choices:
Hit the wagons (free captives, seize ledger).
Infiltrate the farm (rear wall stone → cellar →
master’s room).
Turn Valegrave (use ledger to force names, routes,
and Temple ties… then judge him).
Her last plea. She grips your sleeve, eyes glassy but
steady: “Don’t promise if you can’t come. If you can—
come before the moon’s high. I won’t come back. Not
ever.”

=== page 93 ===
Madame Selentis: Quest Web
1. Power Struggle in Nulb (Against
Selentis)
Hook: One of Selentis’s rivals—Skole (Boatman’s floor
boss), Dick Rentsch (Waterside), or Lodriss (market
mistress)—quietly hires the party to prove Selentis is the
Temple’s civilian handler.
What’s really going on: Selentis runs the Old Mayor’s
Manor as a covert hub for sorting prisoners,
contraband, and orders flowing from the river and
wagons to the Hunting Cottage and its tunnel into the
Temple. Evidence exists—if you dare the manor cellars.
Lift a ledger or sealed order from Selentis’s
command room.
Shadow a night transfer from the Boatman’s docks
to the manor, then cottage (map times, faces, crates).
2. Mission of Blood (Pro-Selentis)
Brief: Selentis wants Captain Tolub (and thus
Belsornig) checked without open war. She orders a
“lame the wolf, don’t kill it” operation. Wreck a pirate
rendezvous at the Boatman’s (plant false “Earth
Temple” sigils to frame Romag).
Knife-work option: remove Grud Squinteye, Tolub’s
brutal mate, to fracture crew discipline. Why it
matters. Tolub is Belsornig’s river fist; Selentis is his
land counterweight, and the tavern is their neutral
chessboard.
Twist: Belsornig’s go-betweens offer the party a
better purse to expose Selentis’s informants.
“You look like you’ve got more sense than the usual sellswords,
there’s power shifting in this filth-ridden town… and some of us
ain’t keen on being beneath it.” Madame Selentis
3. The Rise of the “Baroness” (ProSelentis… or Against)
Aim: Secure leverage over slaver-captain Vesrek.
Run: Board the Crimson Trader, copy manifests
tying him to Temple shipments and Nulb cellars (the
manor stores Vesrek paperwork).
Fork: Turn the evidence over to Selentis to polish
her “public” legitimacy—or to Verbobonc agents to
put a bounty on her head next.
4) The Constable’s Last Badge
Hook: Constable Edrick Malvaar drinks to forget he’s a
puppet. Selentis keeps him pliant with coin, fear, and
staged “wins.” PCs can break him… or use him.
Redemption: extract blackmail ledgers from the
manor; free him to act as your lawful screen.
Leash: fabricate proof he’s skimming Temple coin.
Fallout: If exposed clumsily, Lucius replaces Edrick.
5. The Silent Road (Pro-/Anti-Selentis)
Mission: Intercept a midnight convoy: Boatman’s →
Manor → Hunting Cottage → Tunnel.
Decide whether to seize, poison, or ghost-escort the
load to learn the schedule deeper in.
Inside the cottage. Gefreid’s logs, bugbear timings,
rune-stones, and the worked cave to the Temple—
this is the artery.
6. Break the Chain (Anti-Temple)
Job: Sabotage the Hunting Cottage tunnel node to stall
the uprising without revealing how you knew.
Details: Goblin whistles, bugbear fire-teams, carrion
crawler contingencies, even a planned cave-in
protocol—Gefreid runs it like a ledger.
Success: Weeks of supply shock; Selentis scrambles
to patch the route, giving PCs time to move on the
manor.
7. Parley in the Grand Hall (Social)
Scene: Selentis invites the party to “negotiate” under
crossbows in the ruined ballroom—her velvet glove over
iron. Choices.
Trade names and routes for immunity.
Offer to take a contract against her rivals (Tolub,
Rentsch, Skole) earn temporary safe-harbor in Nulb.
Hidden Clock. If talks stall, a “house fire” starts—
stirges loose, dire hounds unchained, and a polite
bow from the balcony.
Rewards & Levers (use as needed)
Documents & Ledgers. Shipment schedules, slave
manifests, pirate cuts—real power at your table is
paper and signatures.
Pardons/Passes. Temporary writs from the
constable or stamped “market scrip” that buys them
five minutes in the Boatman’s back rooms.
Allies on a String. A frightened clerk, a bandit
sergeant tired of bugbear bullying, a barmaid
informant.
Failure States (Escalation Ladder)
Quiet Knife. A messenger vanishes; prices go up;
doors shut, lost corporation.
Smigmal’s Shadow. Assassin dog the party’s trail.
Feldrin’s Teeth. Bugbear “inspectors” appear in
town to “audit” the problem.
Invitation Withdrawn. The Grand Hall parley
becomes a trap.

The fallen noble lady
Given by: Mother Screng
Location: 33. Old Mayor’s Manor
Quest Type: Infiltration, Espionage, Political Intrigue
Recommended Level: 4–6
A Whispered Request in the Back Room
In the dim candlelight of the back room of her herb
shop, Mother Screng ushers the adventurers behind a
woven curtain of dried swamp grasses. The air smells of
chamomile, crushed root, and suspicion.
“I’ve known power-mongers and I’ve known monsters, and that
one…” she says, pausing to glance toward where the Old
Mayor’s Manor sits, “…is something altogether different. She
trades in people, secrets, and silence. Bring me what strips the
mask.”
Briefing. Screng suspects Madame Selentis (the
“Baroness”) is the land-side handler for Temple
logistics, brokering prisoners, coin, and orders between
the riverside crews and the Hunting Cottage tunnel. She
believes proof of identity, allegiance, and routes is
hidden in a secret room inside the manor.
Objective
Enter the Old Mayor’s Manor without starting a
general alarm.
Locate the secret room (false bookcase).
Extract hard evidence tying Selentis to Temple
leadership and Nulb logistics.
Exit clean and deliver the intelligence to Screng.
Deliver the intelligence to Mother Screng discreetly.
Approaches (choose one or mix)
Soft Feet: Night climb to the balcony; bypass window
latch (Thieves’ Tools DC 15).
Soft Words: Pose as river factors or caravan brokers
seeking the “Baroness” (Deception DC 15;
advantage with forged scrip from Boatman’s).
Inside Help: Bribe a footman with coin and a
“transfer chit” (Persuasion DC 13) to gain a fiveminute pass in the entry halls.
Hard Way: Create a ruckus at the stables/market to
pull guards off the manor, then slip in (Group Stealth
vs. passive 12–14).
Security at a Glance
Entry Atrium. Two servants, one guard on a slow
circuit (Perception +2).
Wards. Subtle alarm sigils across thresholds (Arcana
DC 14 to notice; Dispel Magic DC 14 to suppress for
10 minutes).
Rotations. 2 bandit guards inside; 4 outside on the
grounds (two-by-two, lanterns; exchange every 20
minutes).
Animals. Leashed dire hounds released if a gong is
struck; stirges in a net-covered cage near the grand
hall (used as a “panic swarm”).
Visitors. Runners from Boatman’s or the Waterside
drop messages after dusk; once per night a sealed
crate arrives bound for the Hunting Cottage.
Stealth Clock (4-segment)
1: Footman “hears something.”
2: Courtyard pair drifts inside to “look around.”
3: Gong; hounds loosed.
4: House lockdown; a messenger sprints to the docks.
The Secret Room (the “Sanctum”)
Location: Illusion-shrouded bookcase door off the
atrium reading alcove.
Find: Investigation DC 17 (tool bonus if you’ve cased
the house), or Arcana DC 15 to notice the glamor.
Open: Hidden latch (Thieves’ Tools DC 15).
Trap: Glyph of Warding (paralysis; Con save DC 16,
3 rounds). Resets at dawn.
Scry-screened: The chamber is lined in leadleaf;
scrying and clairvoyance fail within.
Key Contents
Temple Correspondence between Nysera and
Romag, Smigmal, Belsornig, and Hedrack.
A House Krivaltis jeweled goblet, tied to her lost
heritage and political ties to Dyvers.
Wand of Polymorph (5 charges), used to disguise
agents or eliminate liabilities.
Coded maps and reports linking supply chains from
Nulb to the Hunting Cottage south of Nulb.
Inside the Sanctum — Evidence Table
Roll or choose 3–5 items; each gives a different lever.
d6 Evidence (what it means)
Use at the table
1 Sealed letter from “L.”—coded scheduling note matching barge arrivals.
Proves a handler above Selentis; lets PCs predict a
shipment night.
2 Coded route map: Boatman’s → Manor → Hunting Cottage → tunnel.
Hard link between town and Temple; +2 on any check to
intercept a convoy.
3 Ledger of “special transfers” (initials, payments, headcounts).
Blackmail fuel; +2 to Intimidation vs. Selentis.
4 House Krivaltis goblet (Dyvers hallmark).
Identity tie to Dyvers nobility; audience with city agents.
5 Wand of Polymorph (5 charges) with notes: “mules made silent.”
Tangible magic reward; hints at cleanup operations.
6 Correspondence fragments: directives echoed by Romag / Belsornig /
Hedrack in different hands.
Faction web; use to pit temples or prove Greater Temple
oversight.

Cottage Shop Ruins (17)
The scorched shell by the muddy lane is more than a
ruin—it’s a switchboard for Nulb’s worst secrets.
Burned coopers’ shop, bones under the hearth,
whispering stone, and a cellar reached by a rusted ring
beneath a fallen beam (DC 15 Investigation). Temple
die-hards made their last stand here; the locals still
avoid “the Firebones” on principle. Agents use it as a
dead-drop and candle-signal site, especially when the
Wharf or Wainwright are watched. Otis’s smithy sits
within earshot—he quietly watches who comes and
goes.
A. “Dead Drop Gone Missing”
The rear “window” shows last night’s signal—a stub of
tallow gutter scrawled into a candle-sign—but the cache
is empty. Madame Selentis wants it found before her
rivals do.
Objective. Track who lifted the packet; recover or
destroy it.
Southbound sign: Boot scuffs and a snapped hedge
twig point to Poacher’s Cut—the footpath leaving
Nulb’s south hedgerow toward the cottage.
Complications. Romag’s scout lays a counter-drop to
smoke out whoever comes looking.
Outcome. Returning the message earns Selentis’s
favor; handing it to Otis opens resistance lines.
B. “The Cracked Doll”
A child’s doll with red marble eyes sits amid moldy
crates—the soul-splinter inside calls for warmth.
Objective. Return the splinter to its body…or bargain
with a patron who wants it instead.
Paths. Mother Screng can attempt a risky
reintegration; the Temple will pay to keep it buried.
C. “The Whisper Below”
On storm nights the cellar mouths an Abyssal prayer—
something Temple-made is waking.
Objective. Silence the relic or trace the resonance.
Relic resonance: A shard in the cellar harmonizes
with the elemental / ley-line under the temple ruins.
Arcana (DC 14) reads a directional pull due south.
A charcoal note: “Rill at mile marker, then east to
the pines”—a wayfinder to the cottage.
D. “Candle for a Crown”
A candle-signal brings not Selentis’s runner but a
Crimson Reaper cut-out with Orcus ink under the skin.
They want to use the ruin for a meet.
Objective. Play both sides: sell the time and place to
Selentis while extracting coin from the Reapers.
Complications. Romag’s watchers also use the site
when they need to move unseen through town.
Outcome. If the party stages a three-way sting, they
can kick off a shadow wars.
E. “Ash Shack Stakeout”
Otis asks the party to quietly log every visitor for three
nights; he suspects new handlers are taking over the
drop. (He keeps watch from his forge.)
Objective. Identify patterns (boots, passwords,
candle codes) and who resets the trapdoor.
Finds. DC 15 check reveals the cellar ring under a
beam; the cache lists Earth-temple ciphers and
Selentis’s routing marks.
F. “Candle, Coin, or Coffin” (1-Session
Micro-Heist)
Word spreads that a “big packet” will drop tonight.
Three factions converge: Selentis’s runner, a Reaper
collector, and Romag’s scout. Walk Poacher’s Cut to a
waypoint outside town (a broken cart wheel in a ditch)
before deciding to continue to the Hunting Cottage.
Goal. Decide who gets the packet—or swap it with a
forgery that incriminates someone useful.
Payoff. Handing it to Selentis earns black-market
help; to Otis, resistance intel; to Romag.
Treasure & Clues in the Cellar
Cache: 240 sp, 38 gp; Iron Mask of the Earth
Temple; potion of gaseous form; scrolls (darkness,
meld into stone); masterwork sickle; cracked
porcelain doll (red marble eyes).
Signals: Rear-window candle indicates a ready drop.
Who’s Using the Ruin Tonight?
Keep the ruin quiet and mean. Let the place speak first—creak, soot, the candle nub—then let factions collide if the
party pushes. The site exists to route them toward Selentis’s network, Romag’s Earth cell, or the Hunting Cottage
tunnel—your choice based on where you want the Nulb arc to break next.
d6
Event
1
Selentis courier leaving a ledger chip.
2
Crimson Reaper pair swapping victims’ trinkets for coin.
3
Romag scout testing new countersigns.
4
Otis pretending to fix a hinge, actually counting faces.
5
Smugglers spooked by “voices” (Abyssal echo).
6
No one—just the cellar whispering, and prints headed south toward the Hunting Cottage.

The Gilded Shackle (19)
A counting-house wearing a chapel’s face; a ledger
where prayers go to be laundered.
Jereader Zomawyn runs this “church” like a blackmarket bank—washing coin for pirates, bandits, and
Temple lieutenants, brokering bribes, and keeping just
enough secrets to survive their feuds. Beneath the altar
sits a working vault; the true hoard lies hidden in his
quarters behind wards and poisoned steel.
1. “Balance the Books” (Heist • Social)
A rival faction wants proof that Zomawyn launders
Temple wealth. Infiltrate the chapel after hours, swap a
page in the day coffer ledgers with a forged duplicate,
and walk out under the collectors’ noses.
2. “The Price of Mercy” (Moral Choice •
Assassination)
Zomawyn offers sanctuary to a hunted NPC—if the
party removes a troublesome priest in Hommlet who
threatens to expose his books. Take the job, fake the hit,
or turn the tables on the moneychanger.
3. “Golden Thread to the Docks”
(Investigation)
Follow Tolub’s ledger anomalies from the Shackle to
the wharf: identify falsified cargo tallies and seize a
scrip chest before it reaches the Iron Dagger.
Zomawyn’s scribes “repair and inventory” the pirate’s
books—catch them in the act.
4. “Two Masters, One Purse” (Temple)
Play Romag and Belsornig against each other using
Zomawyn’s double-dealing—plant a false margin in a
ledger to suggest he favors the other. Watch which
priest moves first, then sell the truth to the loser.
5. “The Dyvers Wire” (Travel • Intrigue)
A corrupt Dyvers prelate receives looted relics routed
through the Shackle. Intercept the courier, secure proof,
decide who gets exposed: the bishop or Zomawyn.
6. “Keys, Whispers, and Needles”
Find the true hoard: a floorboard, a blackwood square, a
lock that wants a key and a whispered prayer. Inside:
temple-stamped plates, soul contracts, and an unofficial
map of the Nulb↔Dyvers black economy.
7. “Selentis’s Cut” (Espionage •
Leverage)
Madame Selentis moves prisoner-sale proceeds through
the vault. Copy her deposit markers without stealing
them and you gain leverage over her convoy timings—or
hand the copies to Skole to choke her take.
“Every coin has two faces; always know both.” - Jereader
“A tithe to Zilchus is a down payment on your own future. Pay
wisely… or learn the cost of poverty.” —Jereader Zomawyn
8. “Proxy of the Mouth” (Intel)
Hedrack never meets Zomawyn; Lucius Graeme is the
go-between. Shadow a coin shipment, plant a tracer
sigil, and learn where Lucius stashes Temple bribe
rosters around Nulb.
9. “Break the Shackle” (Revolt • Street)
Rally debtors and small traders squeezed by loans to
stage a ledgers-burning “tithe strike.” Survive the
collectors’ retaliation and keep the crowd from getting
butchered when the vault wards flare.
10. “Contract of the Damned” (Caper)
Steal, void, or rewrite one blood-ink contract binding a
named pirate or brigand. The parchment is in the hushwarded chest; tampering without a counter-clause might
curse the signer—or the thief.
DM Notes
Security Tone: Expect two Veterans and a rogueacolyte within earshot; alarms/wards bring help fast,
and Lucius’s protections complicate divinations.
Interfaction Threads: Tolub’s books, Selentis’s
deposits, and the Earth/Water priest rivalry are your
clean lines out into Nulb’s other sites. Use a single
ledger scrap to route players toward the Wharf, Old
Mayor’s Manor, or the Wainwright depot.
