Graveyard of Nulb (44)
1. “The Herald’s Quiet”
Giver: Osric Vell (in a dry whisper, paid in secrets)
Premise: Osric believes an unmarked coffin holds a
long-dead Herald once tied to the Elder Elemental
Eye. Temple men have started probing the old
sections by night.
Objective: Find the Herald’s grave (follow a pattern
of weathered stones and old iron nails), retrieve the
coffin’s relic, and keep it out of Temple hands.
Complications: Warded plot (Arcana/Religion DC
14). Stirred grave-wight rises if the coffin is forced. A
hidden spy runs south to warn the Hunting Cottage.
Payoff: Osric grants a one-time Grave Whispers favor
(free Speak with Dead on a named corpse) and a
rumor that points straight to the next convoy’s route.
2. The Hexed Bones of Orcus
Faction Involved: Maldrith, Hexed Priest of Orcus
Quest Type: Horror / Combat Encounter
Osric Vell recently buried three bodies dumped at the
graveyard gates—mutilated and rotting, their skin
marked with sigils of Orcus. At night, the graveyard
pulses with necrotic energy. What Osric didn’t know:
Maldrith placed cursed talismans on the bodies to test
the area for undeath-conduits.
“Maldrith wants something buried here. I don’t know
what it is, but he’s left marks—runes—under the soil.
They burn when the moon is full.”
3. “Bones on the Cart”
Temple brigands (working for Selentis) exhume
“special dead” to harvest sigils and bones for rites. They
load coffins onto a low cart at dawn.
Objective: Shadow the cart out of town to confirm
the overland hand-off, or hit it for the manifests.
Complications: The cart has a hidden shrine-tile
(glyph: fear, Wis DC 13). If a fight gets loud, a pair of
dire hounds from the manor arrives within 2 rounds.
Payoff: Manifests show the Nulb → Hunting Cottage
route for the next week.
“You want to know about the broken glyphs near Vakaros’
stone? That wasn’t my doing. Something is stirring them.”
4. “Glyphmarked Dead”
Giver: Cleric/Paladin instincts or Seressa’s hints.
Premise: Maldrith has etched faint glyphs of Orcus
beneath select graves. When five are active, a minor
breach opens and undead “leak” toward the
Waterside.
Objective: Detect and break three glyphs before the
next moonrise; each requires holy water, salt, and a
name of the interred.
Complications: Breaking a glyph summons a stitchthing (medium undead) or draws Seressa, who is
compelled to watch; harming her angers Osric.
Payoff: Sanctifying a plot reduces random undead
incidents in Nulb for a tenday and grants the party
quiet favor with Osric and Mother Screng.
5. “Payment in Silence”
Giver: Madame Selentis (through a polite
intermediary) or the - Constable, if approached first.
Premise: A Temple courier was murdered; both
sides need his last message—clenched in his jaw.
Objective: Convince Osric to permit (or perform)
Speak with Dead and extract the route pass-phrase
without starting a faction incident.
Complications: Seressa demands a token (“a ribbon
or a true name”) before she lets the jaw unclench; a
pirate lookout watches from the fence. Bolts if seen.
Payoff: Pass-phrase grants advantage to infiltrate the
Old Mayor’s Manor or Boatman’s back rooms.
6. “The Pine That Remembers”
Giver: Seressa (soft, insistent)
Premise: A black pine’s bark shows new sigils; the
soul beneath tries to rise—a trafficked victim tied to
the river crews.
Objective: Find the token that binds her (ledger
scrap, locket, ribbon) and set the grave right, or she
will join Maldrith’s web at moonrise.
Complications: The token is in a pirate’s pocket at
Boatman’s; taking it quietly earns respect.
Payoff: Lay the spirit to rest and Seressa will appear
once again (“House that isn’t a house” = manor,
“cottage that hunts” = Hunting Cottage).

Durnic’s Stablehouse (46)
1. Quiet Hooves, Loud Secrets (Stealth •
Surveillance)
A dusk convoy arrives, horses walked bareback to keep
noise down. They’ll ride out toward the Hunting Cottage
before midnight.
Objective: Shadow the riders; identify the hand-off
point and recover a ledger token or route mark that
ties back to Temple tunnel traffic. (The tunnel
system south of Nulb moves supplies and prisoners.)
Complications: Bugbear scouts and goblin runners
play relay along the approach paths.
Payoff: Proof of the overland supply chain usable
with the Constable or Mother Screng for favors.
2. Letters in the Saddle (Heist •
Intrigue)
Romag’s courier stables his mount and leaves a
saddlebag locked in the loft.
Objective: Lift, copy, or swap the sealed letters.
Complication: Tampering risks triggering a faction
feud if the decoy points to the wrong rival.
Payoff: Leverage on Romag (or a planted fake to
misdirect him).
In Nulb, no one gets out clean.
3. Mira’s Last Deal (Social • Moral
Dilemma)
Mira wants out; the Crimson Reapers will take her—if
she delivers “a favor.”
Complication: If the PCs balk, the Reapers “adjust”
the price—Mira’s freedom for a theft at Waterside.
Payoff: Mira’s testimony on routes, faces, and times;
a grateful insider thereafter.
Objective (pick one):
Plant a marked chisel in a Water-Temple tack trunk
(frames Belsornig’s crew).
Divert a Fire-Temple scout’s remount to arrive lame
at the Etters.
4. Ash on the Wind (Ambush • Counterrecon)
Fire-Temple scouts use the yard to switch mounts and
vanish toward the Etters watchtower.
Objective: Snatch a scout’s route-stone and cloak pin
—proof tying the Etters outpost to Nulb.
Complication: The scout carries a false map meant
to bait rivals into an ambush.
Payoff: Evidence useful to play Earth vs. Water vs.
Fire, or to sell to the Constable.
5. Burn Notice (Defense • Set-piece)
A faction decides Durnic needs to be “taught”
obedience; the stablehouse goes up unless someone
intervenes.
Objective: Hold the yard three rounds while Mira
opens the cattle-gate and Durnic douses beams.
Complication: Attackers use oil skins and smoke
pots; saving the horses is its own challenge.
Payoff: Durnic becomes a steadfast ally; stable
resources and hideouts open to the party.
6. The Overheard Plot (Investigation)
Mira hears Temple riders whisper about a shipment
“for the Cottage.”
Objective: Trace the shipment and identify who signs
for it at the Hunting Cottage.
Payoff: A clean line from Nulb logistics to Temple
access—exactly the proof outside powers want.
7. The Stolen Steed (Recovery •
Leverage)
A Verbobonc noble’s warhorse is hidden under an alias
in Durnic’s back stall.
Objective: Return the horse (earning patronage) or
use it to draw out the thief’s handler.
Complication: The rightful owner’s agent and a
Reaper buyer arrive the same night.
Payoff: Gold, a minor writ from Verbobonc—or a new
enemy if mishandled.
Running Durnic & Mira
Durnic is weary and pragmatic; he’ll help if it
protects Mira or keeps the yard standing.
Mira trades whispers for options; if spurned, she’ll
risk darker allies.
Consequences (pick 1–2 per success/failure)
Selentis tightens the vise: Higher “protection” tithes;
convoys rerouted and harder to track.
Pirate reprisal: Night attack with firepots if WaterTemple mounts were fouled.
Fire-Temple heat: Scouts set a roadside ambush
near the Etters if their remounts go missing.
Romag’s suspicion: Waterside eyes start following
the party if a letter goes astray
“Funny thing about protection—don’t pay for it, and suddenly
you need it real bad.” - Durnic
DM Notes
This site is a low-profile intercept point—safer than
confronting factions inside the taverns.
Harming the stablehouse angers multiple power
players, so victories here echo across Nulb politics.
Tie any overland pursuit back into the Hunting
Cottage tunnel network.

=== page 99 ===
Slaver Captain Marad Vesrek
The Crimson Trader and its ruthless captain are
tangled in a web of corruption, power, and heresy
stretching from the docks of Nulb to the dark halls
beneath the Temple of Elemental Evil.
1. Reckoning on the Docks
Patron: Madame Selentis (“Nysera”)
Pitch: Vesrek’s Scarlet Brotherhood ties and his
habit of keeping his own ledgers make him useful—
but dangerously independent. Selentis wants
leverage or a leash. She’ll pay for proof.
Objective: Infiltrate the Crimson Trader or the
Boatman’s Brothel offices to copy or plant evidence
tying Vesrek to the Scarlet Brotherhood and slave
consignments; alternatively, replace one ledger page
with a forged “double-book.”
Complication: Elvanna’s loft is a web—hush-wards,
muscle (Mardun), and the Broker’s paper trails will
notice a missing page; Selentis wants Vesrek close,
yet compartmentalized, not openly toppled.
Outcome: Delivering copies (not originals) lets
Selentis squeeze Vesrek without sparking a war;
turning the proof over to Belsornig or Tolub shifts
the balance in the river-faction triangle.
2. Redhand’s Bait
Patron: Smigmal Redhand
Pitch: Smigmal hates Temple liabilities. Vesrek is
profitable, but his Brotherhood stink draws
attention. She wants him shamed, not necessarily
dead.
Objective: Frame Vesrek as a leak to Verbobonc by
planting a coded courier token (or “witness” name)
aboard the Crimson Trader, then seed the rumor
through the Waterside/Boatman’s grapevine.
Complication: Lady Selentis’s watchers haunt the
brothel and tavern; a clumsy rumor frames the
wrong rival (Tolub), igniting pirate reprisals.
Outcome: If the party pulls it off, Smigmal owes a
quiet favor (maps, patrol times near the ruins). If they
bungle it, Vesrek tightens security and starts hunting
informants.
3. The Brotherhood’s Brand
Patron: Zilchus priest (Gilded Shackle) or Mother
Screng (indirect)
Pitch: Proof exists—hidden ledgers and scarletthreaded scrolls—that Vesrek runs Brotherhood
intelligence through Nulb and the Brothel. Fetch
them, and the whole river changes course.
Objective: Lift the hidden ledger and cipher scrolls
from Vesrek’s cabin (or Lorveth “the Broker’s” room
across from Elvanna’s) without alerting the scribe
network.
Complication: The Brothel tracks secrets like coin;
Elvanna’s crawlspace to the warehouse makes
pursuit quick if the alarm goes.
Outcome: Handing the proof to Selentis gives her a
velvet garrote on Vesrek; selling it to Belsornig buys
the party river immunity—until it doesn’t.
4. Tides of the Past
Patron: An old Wild Coast contact (Safeton/Narwell)
Pitch: Someone from Vesrek’s Safeton/Wild Coast
rise wants old sins aired—mutiny, betrayal, and the
bloody birth of the Crimson Trader.
Objective: Gather testimony and proofs (tattoo
marks, charter fragments, former crew accounts)
that Vesrek betrayed his captain to the Brotherhood
to seize the ship.
Complication: Vesrek buys silence fast; witnesses
vanish into Elvanna’s Prison Room or onto Tolub’s
boats.
Outcome: Exposing his Wild Coast crimes cracks his
alliances; Selentis keeps him “close,” Belsornig calls
him expendable, and Tolub circles for turf.
Optional escalator (drop-in)
5. Countermanded by the Dark
Patron: Feldrin, on Hedrack’s leash
Pitch: Hedrack keeps Vesrek valued but expendable,
timed by Feldrin so shipments pass unseen. A rival
has learned the timetable; plug the leak—or become
it.
Objective: Identify the informant using the Brothel’s
blackmail ledgers; swap the rendezvous hour to
ambush a rival captain instead.
Outcome: If successful, Vesrek “owes” the party—
and collects—later. If not, shipments stall and
Selentis tightens her grip on Nulb’s riverside.
DM Running Notes
Vesrek is the Temple’s profitable conduit—but he’s
running his own game (Brotherhood ledgers,
selective sales, keeping options open).
Selentis
wants proof
and pressure,
not a bonfire
on the docks;
she’ll keep
Vesrek close
while taxing
his land-side
operations.
Belsornig
treats Vesrek
as profitable, expendable; Tolub is the practical rival;
either can be flipped into short-term allies against
the other.
The Brothel (Elvanna/Lorveth) is the paper nexus—
contracts, hush-wards, crawlspaces to warehouses—
perfect for heists and counter-heists.

Sahl’s Cottage (52)
1. A Fisherman’s Plea (Low-Level)
Sahl, feeling guilty, asks the adventurers for advice or
aid. He is unsure who to trust, but if the party has
shown kindness, he may offer Reaver information.
If the adventurers convince him to resist, they must
prepare for retaliation.
If they help him smuggle, they gain access to the
Reaver network but become entangled in Nulb.
2. Derrik’s Loose Lips (Investigation)
Derrik, in his cheerful ignorance, may reveal too much
about the Reapers’ activities to the wrong people.
If Selentis hears of the smuggling, she may order
their execution.
If Tolub learns of the deal, he may take his own cut
or seize their home.
If the adventurers press Derrik, he might
accidentally reveal critical information leading them
to a hidden Reaver supply cache.
3. A Reaper’s Revenge (Combat)
If the party blocks or exposes Verric Colbane’s
smuggling route (or steals a cache), the Crimson Reaper
lieutenant answers fast—by putting Sahl’s cottage to the
torch and kidnapping Derrik. He intends to move the
boy south via Poacher’s Cut to the Gnarley eaves and
hand him to a Reaper collector heading for the Hunting
Cottage.
Scene 1: Fire on the Riverbank
What the PCs see. Night wind, thatch crackling, Sahl
screaming in the lane with a bucket; two Reaper goons
finishing the job.
Sahl (to you, hoarse, desperate):
“You—please—Derrik! They took him—red scarves—into
the trees! I’ll owe you til the river runs dry—just go!”
Reaper Thug (as he retreats):
“Colbane says come collect your debt, heroes. Bring
your tongues.”
Checks/Actions
Put out the fire: 3 PC actions
(buckets/blankets/Control Flames; on failure the
cottage collapses, destroying Sahl’s hidden coin and
tools).
Clues (DC 12 Investigation/Survival): smeared red
wax seal (Reaper tally), boot tracks (4–6), willowcharcoal map scrap pointing “to the Split Stone.”
Scene 2: The Chase — Poacher’s Cut
A narrow hedgerow path south. Time clock: four
segments to the hand-off. Each segment, choose
Stealth, Speed, or Ambush approach.
Stealth (Group Stealth vs. 12): Avoid pickets, lose 1
segment.
Speed (Athletics/Survival 13): Close the gap 1
segment but risk a thorn snare (DEX save 12 or
restrained).
Ambush (Perception 13 to pick the spot): Jump a 2man rear guard for intel and route tokens.
Rear Guard (Low Tier): 2 bandits + 1 scout.
Mid Tier: 2 scouts + 1 veteran.
Rear-guard intel: “Split Stone… then Hand-Off at the
Rill Ford if the bells haven’t rung.”
Scene 3: Split Stone Clearing (Skirmish)
A glade split by a boulder; campfire low. Derrik is
tied to a cart shaft, gagged but alive.
Verric’s plan: stall here for 10 minutes, then push to
the Rill Ford to meet the collector.
Verric Colbane (calling from the shadows):
“Heroes of Nulb, you owe me a night’s work. Leave the
boy and take your hands off my business—we’ll call it
even.”
Low Tier (Lv 3–5 party): Verric (scout with extra
HP), 3 bandits, 1 mastiff.
Mid Tier (Lv 6–8): Verric (veteran statline with
scout’s Cunning Action), 2 scouts, 2 bandits, 1
trained hound (use wolf).
Tactics. Smoke pots (+lightly obscured), short
charges, no heroics—Verric withdraws at half HP
toward the Rill Ford with one scout and Derrik.
Scene 4: The Rill Ford (Final)
Shallow stream, slick stones, moonlight on reeds. A
Reaper collector (veteran) arrives on the far bank with 2
thugs and a covered cage-sledge.
Collector (flat, bored):
“Payment on delivery. If the goods scream, they fetch
less. Your call, strangers.”
Options
Negotiation: Intimidation/Persuasion 15 with proof
of leverage (stolen tally token, named boss) forces
the collector to stand down.
Cut-and-Run: Free Derrik (Athletics 12 to snap rope;
Sleight of Hand 13 to unbuckle cage) and flee; the
ford imposes DEX save 12 or prone on the first dash
through.
Stand-up Fight. If the collector drops, the crew
scatters.
NPC Dialog Bits (drop in)
Derrik (muffled, then to you once freed): “I didn’t mean
it—just talked too much—please don’t let ’em sell me to
the river.”
Sahl (after):
“I’ll mend what’s left. You… you brought my boy back. If
you ever need nets cut or boats quiet, I’ll make it
happen.”

Verric (if captured):

DM Notes & Scaling
Tuning Difficulty
Low Tier: remove the collector or replace with a
scout; cut total enemies by 1–2.
Mid Tier: add a bugbear hireling at the ford.
Smoke pots: creatures inside have disadvantage on
Perception (sight).
Environmental Edges
Burning Thatch: entering the cottage costs 1d4 fire
unless actions were spent to douse first.
Hedgerow Snare: Perception 13 to spot; failed DEX
save 12 = restrained (escape DC 12).
Rill Current: at the ford, failed DEX save 12 =
knocked prone; moving through counts as difficult
terrain.
Consequences
Verric escapes: start a Reaper Retaliation Clock (4
ticks). Each time the PCs foil a Reaper scheme, tick
once; at 4, a night hit-team comes for Sahl or a PC
contact.
Verric captured alive: he bargains—reveals a Reaper
cache near the Wharf (helenite powder, marked
ledgers) or an upcoming convoy time.
Sahl’s Cottage saved: Sahl becomes a steady ally
(hideout, river rumors, 1 free re-roll on a waterborne
Navigation/Survival check per week).
If the cottage burns: Sahl’s savings (20 gp, 2 nets, 1
healing kit) are destroyed; rebuilding takes donations
or a side job.
Faction Ripples
Selentis approves quiet rescues; she hates public
fires—reduce heat in her domain for a week.
Tolub notices Reapers grabbing locals; if PCs
embarrass Reapers, he offers a one-time blue-hemp
favor on the river.
Temple logistics (Feldrin) tighten patrols on
Poacher’s Cut for 1–2 nights after a noisy rescue.
Treasure Hooks
Reaper tally token (used to pass docks unmolested
once).
Charcoal map scrap—the other half can be found at
the Wharf, pointing to a supply cache.
Scarlet wax seal (symbol of Orcus’ eye) useful for
forging a dock chit.
Closing Beat
Seressa may appear near the ash, looking at the saved
boy. “Better to carry a living name than a lighted
candle,” she whispers, and fades—an omen that the
graveyard is watching.
Thorne’s Cottage (29)
Plot Hooks & 1 Featured Quest
Heward Thorne’s place sits where the Gnarley creeps
toward Nulb—one cabin, two gnarlhounds, a family
trying to stay invisible while every faction tugs at their
woodpile. Keep the tone low and tense; threats arrive in
pairs and leave muddy bootprints.
1. The Tally in the Woodpile (Intrigue •
Forgery)
A dock tally token (used to pass cargo without
inspection) turns up inside a split log Heward sold
yesterday. Someone is using Thorne’s deliveries to
smuggle papers past the Wharf.
Leads to: Waterside runners (Earth Temple) and a
forged chit at Boatman’s (Water Temple).
Choices: Return it to Heward and lie low, deliver it to
Selentis for favor, or plant it on a rival to ignite a
faction fight.
2. Gnarlhound Howls (Scout • Hunt)
Bran and Fenn start howling at midnight. Edric saw
lanterns moving along the hedgerow toward Poacher’s
Cut—bugbear musk in the air.
Leads to: A Reaper cache under a split elm; route
markers used by riders bound for the Hunting
Cottage.
Choices: Ambush the pickets, shadow them to learn
the convoy timing, or salt the cache and let it walk to
a bigger target.
3. Brother’s Letter (Social • Evidence)
A courier from Verbobonc’s waterfront brings a sealed
note from Heward’s brother. If the Thornes can
document Selentis’s illegal levies (names, weights,
signatures), the brother can push a quiet inquiry in city.
Leads to: Stolen copies of weigh-slips at Boatman’s
Brothel (the Broker’s books) or at the Gilded
Shackle.
Choices: Gather proof and smuggle it upriver, sell
the evidence to Selentis for protection, or trade it to
Smigmal to hurt Selentis’s grip.

Veyne’s Mill (30)
Politics-driven hooks and a compact quest for Veyne’s
Mill that plug straight into the mill’s real entanglements
with Selentis, Feldrin, Romag, and Valegrave:
Selentis’s Quiet Quota
Selentis leans on Thadric to “prioritize civic needs,”
which really means Temple convoys. PCs who shadow
the wagons find Valegrave’s men hauling flour on her
schedule, not the village’s. If they disrupt it, she notices.
Feldrin treats the mill like one gear in his supply
chain to the Hunting Cottage; one of Selentis men is
always nearby to count sacks and whisper threats when
the numbers dip. PCs can flip that watcher—or feed him
false tallies.
Romag’s Side Deal
Romag wants a slice diverted to his Earth Temple
stores, using Dick Rentsch to float “protection” in
exchange for priority grind. If the party poses as new
intermediaries, they can sting Rentsch—or string
Romag along.
Choke the Source
Valegrave’s farm steers raw grain to Veyne’s Mill; a
single bad week in the fields starves the stone. PCs who
pressure or expose Valegrave can throttle Temple
throughput without ever drawing steel at the mill.
Flour in the False Wall
Gavrin Veyne and the Thorne boys salt away small
sacks off-quota—a tiny resistance with big risk. If the
party helps hide or move the flour, they make friends; if
caught, they make enemies.
Short Quest: “The Sacks That
Sang Too Loud”
Premise. The mill’s tally slips don’t match the flour on
hand. Feldrin’s watcher suspects theft; Romag’s man
swears skimming; Selentis just wants her numbers.
Thadric begs the party to make this… go away. (He
won’t say how frightened he is, but his wheel creaks
faster when he talks.)
Objectives.
Trail Valegrave’s next wagon from farm to mill; verify
grain weight vs. delivered flour.
Identify who’s siphoning: Feldrin’s counter, Romag’s
cutout (via Rentsch), or a third party using the
Thorne kids’ caches as cover.
Decide the leak’s fate: expose, exploit, or protect the
quiet resistance.
“The mill grinds what you bring it,” Thadric mutters, hands on
the warm stone. “These days, that’s mostly nerves.”
Complications.
Quota Snap: If numbers drop again, Feldrin orders a
“quiet correction”—night blades at the millhouse.
Earth Tremor: Romag’s envoy arrives with muscle
and a better offer that smells like a trap.
Supply Starve: Any move against Valegrave
threatens to starve the stone—villagers will blame
the party when bread runs thin.
Resolutions & Rewards.
Balance the Books: Forge a passable paper trail and
nudge weights so everyone “wins” this week; earn
Thadric’s trust and discreet access to mill records.
Cut a Gear: Feed Feldrin proof that Romag’s
siphoning (or vice-versa) to buy breathing room for
the Veynes; gain a favor from one faction and the
enmity of the other.
Selentis Brigands
You hear the hopper rattle and the stone sing. Then
boots—two of Selentis’ temple brigands in the doorway,
cloaks dusted white. Thadric feeding grain, jaw tight.
Brigand 1 (flat):
“Afternoon, miller. The Lady is displeased. Counts don’t
match. This gets corrected.”
Thadric (measured):
“Stone turns what you bring. Bags settle with the damp
—numbers drift a touch.”
Brigand 2 wanders the floor, palming sack seams, eyes
moving, saying nothing.
Brigand 1:
“Drift’s one thing. Missing is another. You’re light three
and a half. That weight lands on us… and then on you.”
Thadric (swallows):
“I’ll make it right. Give me ’til dawn.”
Brigand 2 (without looking up):
“First and fast. No delays. No cleverness.”
Thadric:
“You’ll have it. Clean sacks. Count them yourself.”
Brigand 1 (steps closer, low):
“Good. Because the Lady noticed. She keeps noticing.
Next time we bring a scribe and a rope.”
Brigand 2 raps the stair with his knife flat, tests a bin
lid, flicks a glance at a re-stitched seam—lets it go.
Brigand 1:
“We’ll walk your yard. If we don’t like what we find, we
come back early. You won’t like early.”
Thadric:
“I understand.”
They turn out into the drizzle. The hopper grinds on.
Above, the two older boys lie silent along the rooftop
ridge, watching dust settle, not daring a word.

Bramblethorn Ranch (31)
Meat for the Maw (Intrigue)
Selentis’ collectors arrive early demanding an extra
“hide tithe.” If the party pushes back, she threatens to
cut Bramblethorn off from Nulb’s buyers, forcing
Ormund to choose between ruin or Temple dependency.
Earth Mark on the Hoof (Investigation)
Two night-slaughtered sheep bear green-twine stitches
and sanded-off brands—Romag’s quiet signature. Track
the intermediaries (likely out of the Waterside) before
the next herd “vanishes.”
Salt & Skim (Smuggling/Chase)
Belsornig’s pirates skim hides off Temple shipments at
the Wharf. Catch Tolub’s crew in the act or strike a deal
to steer the skimming toward a rival.
Fence at Midnight (Defense)
A “bandit” test-raid hits a weak fence line—really a
probe by a crew loyal to Smigmal. Hold the line, or
they’ll be back with fire.
The Boys’ Wire (Social)
Kiel trades whispers with the Thorne and Veyne boys;
they’ve mapped patrol gaps and convoy times. Play that
intel for protection—or sell it for coin.
Quest: “The Last Drive Before
Dawn” (Levels 3–5)
Premise. Feldrin leans on Selentis to prioritize Templebound meat. Ormund refuses Temple “security.” At
dusk, word comes: a mixed crew plans to lift half the
herd on the night move to Valegrave’s yard. The party
must push a small drive under pressure, or
Bramblethorn loses the season.
Beats.
Yard Briefing: Ormund shows torn fences and fresh
hoof-ruts; Rhia asks the party to ride flank. (Skill
checks to prep: Mending/Repair, Animal Handling
for skittish stock.)
The Creek Cut: Pirates try to peel the drive toward a
skiff on the river (Belsornig’s skim). Stop the split or
lose d6 head of the herd.
The Green Twine: At the fences, “helpful” teamsters
wave you into a bottleneck—Romag’s play. Spot the
re-stitched marks or ride straight into an ambush.
Market Gate: Selentis’ collectors demand the
“emergency tithe” at swordpoint. Pay, fight, or force
a count in the open.
“The herd moves like a tired river, and every hand with a spear
wants to dam it.”
Outcomes.
Clean Delivery: +2 standing with Ormund/Rhia;
Selentis notes your competence (and meddling).
Pirate Skim Foiled: -1 with Tolub/Belsornig; gain a
crate of salted hides as proof.
Expose Earth Interference: Romag’s intermediaries
flee; you earn a favor from Bramblethorn and wary
attention from Waterside contacts.
If the Drive Fails: Ranch loses a month’s meat;
Feldrin “offers” Temple guards next time—at the
price of autonomy.
DM Notes.
Keep the pressure—three clocks (Pirate Skim, Earth
Ambush, Selentis’ Tithe) tick in parallel.
Tie in nearby families fast: the Thorne/Veyne kids
can run messages or call in a last-minute cart.
Escalation. If the party shines here, expect a
retaliatory “probe” on the night fences.
Ormund’s Request for Help
You step into the ranch yard at dusk—dust in the air, the
herd moving like a tired river. Rope-burned hands,
lowing cattle, lanterns hooded. Ormund Bramblethorn
waits by the gate rail, hat in one fist, worry in the other.
Rhia checks cinches and counts sheep heads.
Ormund (to you, quiet and direct):
“Word’s come down the lane—mixed crew plans to lift
half my herd on the night run. Temple ‘security’ wants a
cut to ‘protect’ me. I said no. I need riders who take
coin, not orders.”
“Route’s simple on paper: hedgerow path, Creek Cut,
then straight on to Valegrave’s yard. Trouble is, it’s
never simple. Belsornig’s river rats will try to peel us
toward skiffs at the creek. Romag’s land-boys pull a
different trick—teamsters at the ford with pretty smiles
and green re-stitch twine on their sack seams. And if we
make the lane clean, Selentis’ collectors will meet us at
the gate with a new ‘emergency tithe.’”
“I won’t lose this season to three masters fighting
over the same lamb roast. You ride flank and hold them
true. Keep the herd off skiffs, nose us past any ‘helpful’
wagons, and talk the tallymen into tomorrow. I can pay
in coin… or beef and favors that spend quiet.”
Ormund (on Selentis):
“If her men meet us, let me talk. If they push, we show
numbers in the lantern light and promise first grind
from the mill on the marrow.”
Payment:
“Fifty gold on delivery.”
The gate creaks. The herd rolls out into the lane, lantern
light sliding over horns and backs. You take your place
on the flank as night gathers—and somewhere ahead,
men who call theft a tithe wait to count what isn’t theirs.

=== page 104 ===
Hunting Cottage (55)
A mile south of Nulb, a smoke-threaded “lodge” squats
at the forest’s edge. On paper it’s a hunter’s stop; in
truth it’s the Greater Temple’s throat—supplies,
captives, and orders swallowed into the dark. Gefreid
Patris runs the yard with iron routine; Commander
Feldrin owns the tunnel; bugbears keep its teeth sharp.
Everyone in Nulb feeds this place, whether they admit it
or not.
The Waterside Hand-Off (Social •
Stealth)
A midnight “guest” transfer leaves the Waterside Hostel
(Dick Rentsch fronting, Wat pouring) for the cottage:
two burlap-hooded recruits, one gagged prisoner, three
crates “soap & pitch.” Follow the handcart from the
Nulb Stables onto Pouchers Path. If you intercept
quietly, Madame Selentis notices new talent—whether
to hire or hurt.
Bread and Blood (Investigation)
Sack seams at the cottage carry green re-stitch twine
and faint double-dot chalk—the same marks turning up
at Veyne’s Mill and Old Mavrek’s Bakery. Track the
marked sacks back to Valegrave’s Farmstead to prove
the Earth Temple’s skimming scheme—or plant false
marks to spark a feud between Earth (Romag) and
Greater (Feldrin/Selentis).
Courier in the Smoke (Ambush • Intel)
Lucius Graeme rides in at dusk with waxed packets for
Gefreid’s “message alcove.” Snatch one and you’ll have
routes, names, and gate-phrases good for a week—
maybe a note from Smigmal Redhand scheduling a
Broken Tower audit.
Constable’s Quiet Favor (Law • Recon)
Constable Malvaar won’t raid—he’s not suicidal—but
he’ll pay (paper, not coin) for a snare map of the cottage
perimeter after a child lost a foot-trap to “poachers.”
Hand him a rough map and he’ll give you just enough
legal cover to stand your ground if Temple brigands
chases you through town.
“I’m not marching a handful of townsfolk into that hornet’s
nest—won’t raid, not stupid. Bring me a rough map of their
snares, and I’ll pay with a dock writ and bridge pass with my
seal. It’ll read ‘at my request,’ which means if Temple brigands
chases you inside Nulb, you can plant your feet and the gallows
won’t argue. No heroics—not their blood on my badge.”
Selentis’ Red Line (Faction)
Selentis forbids her brigands to enter the tunnel proper
without a seal—Feldrin’s bugbears answer to Feldrin,
not her. Offer to “audit” Gefreid’s books for her; sell the
same audit to Feldrin to prove her meddling. Either
way, somebody bleeds and looses trust.
“Convoy Ghosts” Audit
You come in under low branches and wet smoke. The
cottage squats ahead, barn to the left, stone well and
pens to the right. Gefreid’s men idle in the yard with
cudgels and short blades. Beyond the black pines at the
far edge, a narrow cleft in the slope is screened by brush
and stakes—two heavy shapes keep still there, watching.
A bell-rope hangs by the gate. A goblin boy peeks
from the tree line, then melts back into shadow.
Who’s Here (day vs. night)
Gefreid Patris (yard boss): Mean, efficient, answers
to Feldrin. Runs the operation and the books.
Greater Temple brigands (2–6): Yard security
(cottage/barn/well). One will shadow the PCs at 5–
10 feet.
Yard Guard (human): Spear, sour mood; yard bell
Scribe (human): Inks and stamps; bends to the
strongest seal.
Bugbear pair (cave mouth only): Stationed at the
hidden cave entrance, 80–120 ft beyond the pines.
They do not leave this post unless the cave horn or
Gefreid personally calls them.
Goblins:
Day: Hidden in side caverns near the cave mouth,
watching the cleft.
Night: 1d4 on quiet wood-patrols (stay outside the
yard; circle between 60–120 ft from the cave).
Map cue: Cave mouth sits past the pines behind
brush and stakes; a crude palisade marks the
approach. Yard bell alerts brigands; cave horn alerts
bugbears/goblins.
Props & Tells to Surface
Forged Zilchus writ (Gilded Shackle): red wax coinand-scales on good vellum.
Mismatch bait: red tithe ring on a blue chit; manacle
tag missing a second signature.
Earth marks: green re-stitch twine, faint double-dot
chalk on sack faces; yellow clay in axle grease (from
Waterside yard).
Message alcove: wall niche with tally chips and
waxed packets by the barn door.
“Names and business, now—speak clean or take the
road,” Gefreid snaps, eyes like nails.

Gate Entrance (getting in)
Yard Guard (glances at the writ): “Business?”
Deception DC 14 to pass as Selentis auditors.
Advantage if you use titles (“the Madame’s tithe
verification”) and name a dock-tally dispute.
Success → fetches Gefreid. Failure → rings yard bell
(advance Alarm Clock by 1).
Gefreid arrives, eyes the writ, then you.
Gefreid (rude candor):
He doesn’t touch the writ yet; he reads you.
One of his men slides up like a shadow watching
your hands. “Keep your hands where I can count
them.”
“New Nulb faces with a coin-priest’s paper. Wonderful.
Everything’s slower now. Hold up that stamp so my boys
remember who to hate. You get eyes on the pens, papers on the
nail, and you don’t lay a finger on anything unless I say touch.”
Gefreid spits like acid and waves you in like shooing
flies. A brigand falls in at 5–10 feet to shadow.
Gefreid (low, furious, contained):
“You have an hour. Then it’s mine. Stamp it clean and get out
of my yard. You want the pines? Bring a different seal.”
He steers you by sacks with green twine and double-dot
chalk; watches to see if you blink. The cave mouth
remains beyond the pines—no bugbears in the yard.
DM Note: If the party tries to “inspect the pines,”
Gefreid shuts it down: “Yard only. The trees belong to
those who don’t answer to paper.”
In the Barn (where the paper bites)
Three iron cages (two hooded recruits, one gagged
prisoner); a nail by a post holds prisoner papers.
The Scribe scuttles in with the ledger and stamp.
Investigation DC 13 to catch the red/blue
stamp mismatch & missing second signature.
Intimidation DC 15 (or threaten “mark
UNVERIFIED”) to force one crate opened for
spot-check.
Gefreid (grit):
“You freeze my yard with that stamp, wagons sit and people
north start asking why. Guess whose name I give them first.”
Scribe (small voice):
“Dual attestation on shackles—ah—there’s a space for the
second mark…”
Gefreid (to the scribe, without looking):
“If a page goes missing, I put you in a sack and drop you down
the well.”
Checks & Levers (5e-ish quick list)
Deception DC 14 – look like auditors (advantage
with title/jargon).
Intimidation DC 15 – crack one crate; failure without
“UNVERIFIED” = no pry bar.
Investigation DC 13 – spot stamp mismatch &
missing manacle sig.
Insight DC 12 – see that Gefreid won’t risk tearing a
Zilchus writ today.
Sleight of Hand DC 14 – swap a chit color/line at the
message alcove when he looks away.
Perception DC 12 – notice yellow clay in grease;
faint goblin prints near the treeline (night only).
Automatic leverage: Saying “Mark UNVERIFIED
and escalate tithe to the Gilded Shackle” freezes that
line 1d4 hours unless Gefreid authorizes inspection.
Game Pacing Clocks (use to pace heat)
Alarm Clock (0–3): 0 quiet; 1 yard bell; 2 extra
brigands arrive; 3 cave horn blows—bugbears harden
the cleft, goblins vanish into side caverns.
Wagon Clock (0–2): 0 oars in dark; 1 crew docks; 2
someone demands cargo move now.
Paper Clock (0–2): 0 scribe only; 1 second scribe
fetched; Lieutenant Brunk with two Greater Temple
guards show up as Feldrin’s inspector.
Important: Bugbears never leave the cave mouth
unless the cave horn sounds or Gefreid personally
calls them to the cleft. Yard scuffles do not pull them.
Possible Questions (DM to prompt)
“Show prisoner ledger against cage hooks.”
“Why is a red tithe ring on a blue chit?”
“Where’s the second signature on these shackles?”
“Open one crate; weigh against wagon slip.”
“Who authorized green re-stitch on these sacks?”
“Note UNVERIFIED until corrected; stamp it.”
Possible Outcomes
Clean Freeze (best):
Mismatches flagged; one crate inspected; line stamped
UNVERIFIED until re-stamp. Transfers pause 1d4
hours. Blame falls on Romag’s Earth crew (green twine
planted; chalk pricks everywhere). Cottage shuts for 48
hours while factions argue. Bugbears stay put; goblins
keep their heads down. Gain: copied names/counts.
Messy Freeze (good):
The PC’s force a crate to open, weapons drawn,
tempers rise—no blood. Cottage slows 24 hours;
Smigmal dispatches auditors to Nulb—heat rises at
Waterside and Boatman’s.
Hot Paper (barely):
You push too hard, weapons drawn, threaten or strike
the men; Alarm Clock hits 3. Cave horn blows; bugbears
lock the cleft; goblins melt into side caverns. You escape
with a crate, ledger or prisoner. Feldrin now tags you
“assets to neutralize.” Gefreid marks your faces.

=== page 107 ===
Scene: The Waterside Hostel –
Late Evening with Rentsch
The smoky air of the Waterside Hostel is thick with the
scent of spilled ale, damp wood, and the faint acrid bite
of unwashed bodies. A raucous laugh echoes from a
darkened corner, followed by the dull thud of a mug
slamming onto a table. A few heads turn as the
adventurers enter, but most patrons—pirates,
cutthroats, and smugglers—are too deep in their own
revelry to pay them much mind.
Behind the bar, Wat polishes a glass absentmindedly,
his keen eyes darting toward the newcomers. The real
host of this den of filth, however, lounges at a private
table near the back—Dick Rentsch. The barkeep-turnedTemple-agent leans back in his chair, a smirk playing
across his lips as he nurses a half-empty mug of
something dark and strong. Dala, one of the serving
girls, drapes herself across his lap, giggling as he
whispers something into her ear. At the sight of the
adventurers, he nudges her away and gestures.
“Well, well. Would you look at this? A crew of capable sorts
wandering my doorstep, still breathing despite the dangers out
there. You lot must be either damn lucky, damn talented… or
damn foolish.” He chuckles, motioning for the adventurers to
take a seat. “Now, don’t get me wrong, I don’t make a habit of
trustin’ just anyone. But word in Nulb says you know how to
handle yourselves, and more importantly—” he pauses, eyes
narrowing “—you ain’t exactly got your hands tied to the big
lords and do-gooders sniffing around these parts.”
He takes a slow drink before setting the mug down with
a dull thunk.
“You might say, I know people. Powerful people. And those
people, well, they’re always lookin’ for new talent. The kind of
folk who know how to keep their mouths shut, who know how
to make problems disappear.” He leans forward, lowering his
voice just enough to force them to listen closely.
“Romag. High Priest of the Earth Temple. He’s been
watchin’—and he thinks you might be worth somethin’.” His
fingers drum against the table. “But no one gets a free seat at
that table. You wanna be in, you gotta prove yourselves first.”
“See, there’s a pack of gnolls makin’ their way to reinforce the
Fire Temple. And that’s a problem—for me, for my friends, and
maybe for you, if you’re lookin’ to make some real connections.
Romag wants those mutts wiped off the map before they reach
their new masters. You take care of ‘em, and he’ll meet with you
himself. Not many get that chance, let me tell you.”
He pauses, letting the weight of his words settle.
Waterside: Veil of Shadows
The adventurers, if they have carefully avoided drawing
the attention of the Temple’s leadership, may be
approached by an intermediary—Dick Rentsch, the
owner of the Waterside Hostel in Nulb. While Rentsch
is outwardly a tavern keeper and trader, he secretly
operates as a recruiter for Romag, High Priest of the
Black Earth Temple.
Dick grins, wolfish and knowing.
“The meetin’ will be right here, down in the cellar, away from
pryin’ eyes. You do this right, and you’ll walk through the front
doors of the Temple like you belong. No sneakin’. No fightin’
your way in. Just opportunity.”
He leans back, swirling what remains in his mug before
finishing it off.
“So, what’ll it be?” He wipes his mouth with the back of his
hand. “A simple job. A little bloodshed. A lotta reward. Or do I
tell Romag you ain’t worth his time?” His expression
sharpens as he watches them, waiting for their answer.
However, this opportunity is only available under
specific conditions:
The adventurers must not be widely known as
agents of Furyondy, Veluna, or Verbobonc, nor
openly acting against the forces of the Temple.
Their activities in Nulb and the Moathouse must
have remained discreet—avoiding any overt crusade
against brigands or known Temple agents.
If they defeated Lareth the Beautiful, they must have
done so in a way that left no survivors or any
traceable evidence leading back to them.
If they engaged Rannos Davl and Gremag at the
Trader’s Shop in Hommlet, they must have
eliminated them without drawing suspicion to their
alignment.
The capture of Joseph the saboteur or Zert the
mercenary at the Inn of the Welcome Wench must
not have directly implicated the adventurers in a
greater anti-Temple effort.
Their behavior must have presented them as either
opportunistic adventurers, neutral mercenaries, or
those who could be manipulated rather than as
righteous crusaders.
If they meet these criteria, Rentsch will extend an
invitation on behalf of Romag, offering them a chance to
prove their value. If not, the Temple’s network will
recognize them as enemies, and Rentsch will either try
to eliminate them or send word to the Temple to
prepare an ambush.
Rentsch and Wat is involved in espionage and
recruitment for different factions of the Temple of
Elemental Evil. Wat is aligned with the Fire Temple,
whereas Dick is a part of the Earth Temple faction.

=== page 108 ===
Waterside Hostel Quest — “Five
Chains Upstairs” (Levels 3–5)
Premise. You overhear Dick Rentsch negotiating with
“merchants” from Narwell who are actually slavers.
They’ve got five boys chained in a private room and
intend to sell them to Romag’s Earth Temple for predawn delivery to the Hunting Cottage (then the tunnel).
Madame Selentis hasn’t clocked the deal—she only
noticed tight-tarped wagons arriving.
Scene: Common Room, After Dark
(Eavesdropping)
Low light, low talk. The Waterside breathes like a tired
beast. From the back booth—smoke and shadow—you
catch Dick’s voice, flat as a ledger line, and a merchant’s
softer tone counting by head, not name.
Eavesdrop Checks
Perception DC 13 (catch the gist): “five pieces…
Room C… before first bell… Waterside back stairs.”
Insight DC 12 (read intent): Dick’s brokering for
Earth; the “merchants” fear paperwork more than
blades.
Investigation DC 13 (if you drift past their table):
wrong tithe color on a folded chit (red ring on blue),
faint green re-stitch twine poking from a satchel.
Low lamplight. A door barred against the taproom hush.
River stink and damp rope. Dick Rentsch sits with his back
to the wall; Wat stands at the bar, polishing a mug that
doesn’t need it.
Merian Koss (slaver lead): “Merian Koss, factor for the Black
Net out of Safeton—call it the Slave Lords if you like things
plain. Caravan from the Wild Coast through the Gnarley,
wagons are in your corral with my men. I’m selling coastal
goods—ale kegs, smoked salt, sea-wool, dye cakes—and five
bound apprentices for the Earth Temple. No bruises worth
counting. You’re the buyer?”
Dick: “I hold coin and paper for Romag. If they’re for Earth,
they go through me. You won’t step near the Boatman’s—Skole
and Lodriss aren’t your friends, and Tolub isn’t your captain.”
Koss: “We don’t drink at the Boatman’s. Vesrek sails slaves to
their door; we roll ours where they’re wanted. Earth pays on
time and keeps quiet. That’s reason enough.”
Dick: “Good. My reason is simpler: I don’t like noise. Your
guards stay with the wagons, your mouths stay shut, my stables
water your teams. Price is the Nulb rate plus yard grease. Half
now, half when Romag’s men lift the chain at first grey.”
Koss (setting down a waxed folio): “Good business.”
Scene: Upstairs, Door to Room C
The corridor stinks of lamp oil and old beer. A thug
lingers at the stair head. Inside are five boys, anklechained, with two thugs and Merian Koss.
Stealth DC 13 to reach the door without notice.
Perception DC 12 at the door: muffled chain rattle;
boy whisper (“…don’t cough”).
Thieves’ Tools DC 14 to crack the cheap latch (if you
force it, Noise Clock +1).
1. Pretend to Help (Deception Route)
A. “We’re the Earth pickup.”
Deception DC 14 (drop Romag’s name; mention
“green twine / double-dot” as jargon).
On success Koss treats you as couriers.
Escort & Flip: Walk the “cargo” to the Nulb Stables,
then divert (Constable, Screng, or your own hideout).
Swap the Route Chit: Sleight of Hand DC 14 to
replace their slip → send the transfer into a dead
lane where you control the ambush.
B. “Zilchus audit—show me papers.”
Deception DC 15 to force document review.
Investigation DC 13 finds red ring on blue chit →
leverage to stall or seize papers as “evidence.”
C. “Better Cut for Dick.”-
Persuasion DC 14 with Dick: promise faster, quieter
delivery if he lets you “take over.” Success buys you
custody; fail cools him (Disadvantage on all social
with Dick tonight).
Risks: If you overplay, Suspicion Clock +1 (thugs
shadow you, Dick gets cold).
2) Stop It (Direct/Indirect Intervention)
A. Quiet Rescue
Acquire a Sleep Draught from Pearl (day shift) or
Mother Screng (cost/favor).
Spike ale: Sleight of Hand DC 14 → unconcious in
1d4.
Lift chain key: Sleight of Hand DC 13 (thug’s belt).
Stealth DC 13 to hustle boys down the back stairs.
B. Sting via Selentis
Tip Selentis (messenger or rumor). She arrives with
brigands + clerk, seizes “merchants,” and claims the
boys into her “care.”
Outcome: You gain Selentis’ favor; Earth notes you.
C. Street Ambush
Let the sale happen; intercept the handcart between
Waterside → Stables or on the south lane.
Stealth DC 13 to set the hit; Athletics DC 12 to block
cart; quick combat skirmish.

=== page 109 ===
The Slave Lords (A1–A4) — “The Black Net”
(Safeton Front)
Who they are. A syndicated slaving cartel headquartered in
the Pomarj (Highport/Suderham), with cells along the Wild
Coast—notably Safeton. In Nulb they work quiet, never
public. They prefer bribes, false ledgers, and “apprenticeship
papers” over open chains.
At the table — use this alias.
Say “The Black Net” in play (Safeton front for the Slave
Lords). Reserve “Slave Lords” for GM text, documents, or
slips of the tongue.
Cover & cargo.
Caravans move as “coastal merchants”: ale kegs, smoked
salt, sea-wool, dye cakes, rope and tackle—plus 3–8
“apprentices” hidden under trade manifests. They hire exsoldier brigands as guards, disciplined and sober.
Operating pattern (Wild Coast → Nulb).
Route: Safeton → Gnarley trails → Nulb High Road.
Park: Waterside wagon corral (never Boatman’s).
Contact: Dick Rentsch (Earth Temple broker).
Hand-off (pre-dawn): Hunting Cottage → hidden tunnel →
Temple custody (often Romag’s chain).
Sea competitor (rival method): Captain Vesrek delivers by
river to Boatman’s (pirate route, separate network).
Tells & tokens.
Octagonal black chits stamped with a knotted loop.
Waxed folios listing “apprentices” (age, trade, no obvious
marks).
Uniform lash knots on wrist-ropes; salt-treated, tarscented.
Guards drill like soldiers; minimal drink, minimal talk.
Politics in Nulb.
Avoid: Skole/Lodriss/Tolub (Boatman’s network).
Prefer: Earth or Fire Temple intermediaries (quiet ledgers,
fixed schedules).
Selentis Oversight (Greater Temple): Quartermaster to
Commander Feldrin. Mission is funneling slaves & goods
to the Greater Temple. If she detects private sales to
Earth/Fire outside her pipeline, she interferes (seizure,
punitive tithe, blacklisting, or a deniable brigand
“inspection”).
Friction: Vesrek’s pirates undercut rates and draw heat;
Selentis’ collectors skim “tithes.”
How to use them (GM hooks).
A waxed folio with “apprentice” names goes missing →
pressure from Safeton to recover or silence witnesses.
A guard offers a “buy-back” on one captive—proof of
conscience or a trap to test leaks.
A Black Net factor seeks forged Zilchus papers to move a
larger lot under “guild inspection.”
Rivalry spark: Plant evidence that a load was diverted to
Vesrek—watch cartels and pirates tear at each other.
Pearl (day shift, wiping a mug):
“They don’t say ‘Slave Lords’ in Nulb—they say Black
Net, out o’ Safeton. Kegs and dye up front, ‘apprentices’
in back. Ex-soldiers who drink water, tip with octagon
chits stamped like a knotted loop.”
The Will of the Earth
The adventurers, having made a name for themselves in
Nulb, are approached by an intermediary—Dick
Rentsch, the owner of the Waterside Hostel. Rentsch, a
secret recruiter for the Earth Temple, offers them a
chance to prove themselves to Romag, High Priest of
the Black Earth Temple. However, the deeper they
delve, the more they uncover Romag’s ambition, his
rivalries, and the volatile alliances that keep the temple
in balance.
Players may choose to ally with Romag or overthrow
him to gain favor with rival factions.
Primary Objectives
Prove Worthiness: Ambush a gnoll warband en route
to the Fire Temple, disrupting its reinforcement.
Meet Romag: Secure a private audience with Romag
and gain access to the Temple of Elemental Evil.
Unravel the Rivalry: Decide whether to support
Romag’s bid for dominance or betray him.
Infiltrate the Temple: Gain intelligence on the Earth
Temple’s purpose and the power struggle within.
Part 1: Rentsch’s Proposition
Location: The Waterside Hostel, Nulb
Dick Rentsch is in a good mood, sitting with Dala on his
lap, drinking. When the adventurers enter, he beckons
them over and offers a lucrative deal. He speaks in
vague terms about opportunities with the Earth Temple,
provided the party can prove themselves. The task?
Intercept and destroy a band of gnoll warriors on their
way to reinforce the Fire Temple.
Key NPCs:
Dick Rentsch: Owner of the Waterside Hostel
Dala: Serving wench, informant, and Rentsch’s lover.
Wat: Barkeeper, secretly aligned with the Fire
Temple, rivals Rentsch
Quest Choices:
Accept Rentsch’s Offer: The party is sent to a hidden
ambush site to attack the gnoll warband sent by King
Korvash of the Jagged Fangs tribe.
Investigate Further: A perceptive player might
realize that Rentsch is testing them for Romag, and
Wat may have counteroffers.

Part 2: The Gnoll Ambush
A Hidden Path in the Gnarley Forest
The gnoll warband consists of Gnoll raiders, hyenas,
and their leader, a brutal gnoll warrior named Ursk
Fangbite. These gnolls serve the Fire Temple and are
meant to reinforce Tubal and Antonio, lieutenants of the
Fire Priest Alrrem.
Strategy: The gnolls have scouted ahead and left
traps—if the party fails to anticipate, they’ll walk into
a counter-ambush.
Challenges:
A stealth check (DC 15) to set up a proper ambush.
A perception check (DC 14) to detect gnoll scouts.
A combat encounter, the players must wipe out the
warband before they can alert the Fire Temple.
Outcomes:
Success: The adventurers eliminate the gnolls and
return to Rentsch for their audience with Romag.
Failure: A few gnolls escape, warning the Fire
Temple, making future infiltrations harder.
Part 3: Audience with Romag
Temple of Elemental Evil, Earth Temple Chambers
Rentsch leads the party into the ruined temple,
through a hidden passage to location Room C1 and
down the stairs of 5a.
Inside the Earth Temple chambers, Romag awaits
with his bugbear bodyguards.
Romag, a calculating and paranoid man, demands

He offers further employment, hinting that the Earth

Key NPCs:
Romag, High Priest of the Earth Temple (Wants to

Bugbear Bodyguards (Loyal enforcers of the Earth

Gefreid Patris (Overseer of the Hunting Cabin,

Dialogue Hooks:
If the party asks about the Elder Elemental God,

If the party asks about other factions, Romag warns
them against Water Temple Priest Belsornig.
If the party asks about Hedrack, Romag grows silent,
stating, “Hedrack serves powers beyond the
elements. I am loyal to the stone beneath my feet.”
Quest Choices:
Pledge Loyalty: The adventurers accept Romag’s
authority and begin working for the Earth Temple.
Bargain for Information: The party secures a
foothold in the Temple but remains neutral.
Secretly Betray Him: They take his offer but plan to
aid another faction, like the Water Temple.
Part 4: The Power Struggle
The Temple’s Inner Factions
Romag’s rise in power is not unchallenged. The party
soon learns of a volatile power struggle within the
Temple:
The Rivalries
Belsornig of the Water Temple: Hates Romag and
seeks to eliminate him.
Tubal and Antonio of the Fire Temple: See Romag as
weak and wish to crush his influence.
Hedrack (Supreme Commander): Watches Romag
with suspicion, as Romag refuses to fully obey.
New Mission Options
Eliminate Belsornig: If the party truly joins Romag,

leader.
Spy for Belsornig: The Water Temple may secretly
contact the adventurers, asking them to betray

Turn Against Romag: The adventurers can use their

with another faction.
Audience with Romag
Temple of Elemental Evil, Earth Temple Chambers The
air grows heavy with the scent of damp stone and
churned earth as you descend deeper beneath the
ruined temple. The flickering torchlight casts long
shadows along the cold stone walls, shifting and
writhing like unseen watchers as Rentsch guides you
through a narrow passage.
“Stone endures, while fire fades and wind disperses. In the end,
only the earth remains.” - High Priest Romag

=== page 111 ===
The descent beneath the ruined temple is like sinking
into a tomb. The air grows thick with damp earth and
decay, pressing down with a heavy, unseen weight.
Flickering torchlight casts long, shifting shadows along
the sandstone walls, illuminating crude sigils of jagged
mountains, shattered cliffs, and the ever-watchful
symbol of the Black Earth Temple. Each step across the
dark, loose-packed soil feels as though the earth itself is
shifting beneath you, as if resisting the intrusion.
“You lot best watch your tongues,” he mutters under his
breath, voice low and wary. “Romag don’t suffer fools. He’ll
test you. If he don’t like what he hears—” he glances back over
his shoulder, his meaning clear—“you’ll not be walking out
the way you came.”
The passage widens into a vast chamber, the Temple of
Earth itself. Unlike the stone corridors above, the floor
is not hewn rock but dark brown soil, as if the temple
has carved its place within the womb of the earth itself.
Phosphorescent lichen clings to the walls and ceiling,
casting a dim, eerie glow, a sickly greenish hue that
pulses like something alive. Cressets and sconces stand
empty, unlit, waiting to blaze with fire during rituals of
devotion.
In the center of the temple rises a massive, earthen
pyramid, its packed-dirt walls worn smooth from
centuries of use. Four sets of stone steps, chipped and
cracked from uncounted ceremonies, lead to the
summit. At its peak stands a weathered stone column,
its four faces carved with deep triangles, the sacred
symbol of Elemental Earth. From heavy iron bolts, a
pair of tarnished bronze manacles dangle—a stark
testament to the sacrifices made here.
At the base of the southern side of the column, a
bronze box rests in the dirt, its surface etched with sigils
of shifting earth, its lid bearing a deep handprint, as
though someone—or something—had pressed into the
metal with inhuman force.
Four towering bugbears stand in the shadows, their
beady, yellow eyes gleaming in the dim
phosphorescence. They shift slightly as you enter,
tightening their grips on cruel morningstars, though
they do not speak.
From the far side of the chamber, a figure steps
forward. Romag, High Priest of the Black Earth
Temple.
His robes are the color of the deep soil, ragged at the
hems from years of kneeling in the dirt. His thin face is
etched with deep lines, his eyes dark and cold, like
stone that has never seen sunlight. He stands near the
base of the pyramid, hands folded within his robes, his
long, bony fingers twitching slightly, as if grasping at
something unseen.
A long silence stretches between you, broken only by
the faint rustle of shifting dirt, as if the temple itself is
breathing. Then, Romag speaks, his voice a deep,
resonant whisper, like a landslide waiting to break free.
Romag sneers.
“You stand before me alive, which means one of two things:
Either you are more capable than you look… or you are liars
who seek to deceive me.”
His eyes flick to Rentsch, who gives the smallest of nods.
“You claim to have done as I commanded. That the gnolls on
their way to the Fire Temple no longer draw breath. I am not a
man who deals in empty words. Tell me, adventurers—where
are their heads? Their weapons? Some proof that their corpses
rot in the mud?”
Romag leans forward, his knuckles tightening on the
stone arms of his throne.
“Do not waste my time with excuses. I have use for those
with strength and cunning, but I have even more use for the
example of those who think they can make a fool of me.”
A bugbear shifts at his side, flexing its fingers against
the handle of its cruel-looking morningstar.
If you present proof—trophies of the slain gnolls—
Romag’s expression shifts. A slow, satisfied nod.
“Hmph. Perhaps you are not as useless as I expected. The Fire
Temple will be weaker for this. A fine first step.”
He gestures lazily, and one of his attendants steps
forward with a small pouch—payment, no doubt.
“The Earth Temple does not reward incompetence, but
service? Service is remembered. I may have… further
employment for you, should you have the stomach for it.”
He pauses, studying you once more, then adds in a
quieter, more conspiratorial tone.
“The petty squabbles of this Temple amuse Hedrack, but I see
beyond them. There is more to the power beneath these stones
than the Fire Priests or the Water Cultists grasp. My reach is not
limited to the halls of this ruin, nor will it end when their time
comes.”
His fingers tighten, pressing against the stone of his
throne.
“Serve me well, and you will see what true power is.”
The offer hangs in the air. The bugbears remain still,
ever-watchful. Romag awaits your answer.

=== page 112 ===
Boatman’s Argument Overheard
In the shadowy alleys and dim-lit taverns of Nulb, the
adventurers find themselves unwittingly stumbling upon
a tense confrontation between two men deeply
entangled in the hidden politics of the Temple of
Elemental Evil. Wat, the barman of the infamous
Waterside Hostel, and Skole, the barkeep at the
Boatman’s Tavern, are locked in a hushed argument
that hints at deeper tensions within the town’s
underbelly. Their discussion reveals secrets of
espionage, treachery, and the struggle for influence
between the different factions of the Temple.
The adventurers have a chance to either gather
intelligence, sow discord, or simply observe and learn of
the silent war playing out behind the scenes of Nulb.
Objectives
Spy on the Argument: Carefully eavesdrop on the
conversation between Wat and Skole to learn the
nature of their dispute.
Extract Information from Skole: Wat attempting to
coerce Skole into revealing more details about his
fears regarding Lodriss and the Water Temple.
Leverage Wat’s Allegiance: Find a way to manipulate
the ongoing rivalry between the Fire and Water
factions within the Temple.
Report Back to Lodriss (Optional): If the adventurers
choose to side with Lodriss, they can inform her of
Skole’s potential disloyalty.
Setting: The Boatman’s Tavern
The Boatman’s Tavern, known for its rough crowd and
steady flow of contraband, serves as an important
meeting place for the more discreet dealings in Nulb. Its
owner, Lodriss, remains fiercely independent, ensuring
no single faction of the Temple holds sway in her
establishment.
However, Skole, now finds himself in the middle of a
growing power struggle. On a day when there are no
pirates in port, and the adventurers have made progress
in breaching the Temple but have not yet encountered
Romag, they come across Wat and Skole engaged in an
intense discussion.
The Argument - Fire versus Water
As the adventurers approach the Boatman’s Tavern,
they see Wat leaning over Skole’s table, his fingers
gripping the wooden surface with quiet menace. Skole,
clearly agitated, wipes sweat from his brow and shakes
his head vehemently.
Dialogue Snippet (Overheard)
Wat (gritted teeth): “Skole, you’re going to do what I damn
well tell you. The Alrrem (fire temple) needs eyes here, and I
need someone I can trust. You’d be wise to listen before I lose
my patience.”
Skole (frustrated whisper): “I told you, Wat! Lodriss will gut
me if she finds out! You don’t cross her unless you’ve got a death
wish. And Tolub? He’ll keelhaul me before I can even pack a
bag!”
Wat (snarling): “Lodriss won’t know, you fool. We just need a
few whispers—when the big players are in town, when
shipments are coming through. No one’s asking you to sell your
soul. Just your ears.”
Skole (angrily shaking his head): “And what happens when
she finds out? She will. And then my corpse is feeding the fish in
the Imeryd’s Run.”
At this point, if the adventurers are sneaky (a DC 14
Stealth check) they can listen in further without being
detected. If they fail, Wat and Skole will notice them,
and the conversation will abruptly stop. Skole will feign
ignorance, while Wat will eye the party suspiciously,
wary of their intentions.
Approach Options
1. Gather Information (Espionage & Intrigue)
If the adventurers manage to overhear the entire
argument, they can piece together that Wat is
working for the Fire Temple while Skole is afraid of
betraying Lodriss.
If they confront Skole later (without Wat present),
they can attempt a DC 15 Persuasion or Intimidation
check to get him to reveal that he’s being pressured
into spying for the Fire Temple.
If they succeed, they learn that Wat is working to
expand the Fire Temple influence in Nulb and is
undermining the Water Temple’s operations.
2. Manipulating the Conflict
If the adventurers wish to manipulate the situation,
they can inform Lodriss of Skole’s dilemma. If they
do so, she will take measures to ensure that Skole is
protected, but she will owe the adventurers a small
favor in return.
They could also convince Skole to report false
information to Wat, feeding disinformation to the
Fire Temple about the adventurers or the state of
Nulb.

=== page 113 ===
3. Siding with Wat
If the adventurers wish to earn Wat’s trust, they can
inform him that they have overheard the conversation
but are willing to ensure that Skole cooperates. This
may earn them favor with the Fire Temple faction in the
Temple of Elemental Evil.
4. Reporting to Belsornig
If the party is already aligned with the Water Temple,
they may choose to report Wat’s actions to Belsornig.
Belsornig would be eager to eliminate a rival’s spy and
may reward the adventurers for eliminating or
discrediting Wat.
Outcomes & Rewards
Action Taken Outcome
Eavesdrop successfully: Gain intelligence on Water
Temple operations in Nulb.
Coerce Skole: Learn about his fears and potential
weaknesses in Lodriss’ control over Nulb.
Support Wat: Gain favor with the Fire Temple
faction.
Warn Lodriss: Gain favor with Lodriss and
potentially earn a small reward.
Report to Belsornig: Strengthen ties with the Water
Temple and possibly earn a mission to eliminate
Wat.
DM’s Notes
This quest works well as an espionage-focused
encounter, allowing players to engage in roleplay,
information gathering, and faction manipulation
rather than direct combat.
If the adventurers choose to align with the Temple of
Elemental Evil, this quest can serve as an
introduction to the Temple’s internal rivalries.
If they choose to oppose the Temple, this may serve
as a way to weaken its power base by pitting the Fire
and Water factions against each other.
Wat’s Proposal – Hidden Hand
(versus Earth Temple)
Wat, the barkeep of the Waterside Hostel, has been
quietly recruiting for the Fire Temple, serving its high
priest Alrrem. Unlike Dick Rentsch, who works for the
Earth Temple, Wat is playing a more dangerous game,
acting as a double agent in Nulb’s underworld. The
adventurers have the chance to earn his favor—or
expose his lies—in a delicate balancing act.
Quest Objectives
Primary Objectives:
Establish Trust with Wat: Convince him that the
adventurers are not enemies of the Temple.
Accept Wat’s Offer: Listen to his proposal regarding
recruitment for the Fire Temple.
Sabotage the Earth Temple: Help Wat weaken
Romag’s influence by intercepting Earth Temple
supply shipments.
Secondary Objectives:
Spy on Wat’s Network: Gather intelligence on the
Fire Temple’s recruitment process in Nulb.
Expose Dick Rentsch: Play the rival factions against
one another, leveraging their paranoia.
Gain Favor with Alrrem: If the adventurers decide to
align with the Fire Temple, they could be granted an
audience with Alrrem himself.
The Encounter at the Waterside Hostel
The adventurers find Wat at his usual post—watching,
listening, and waiting. The moment they seem useful, he
makes his move.
Wat’s Opening Line (If the Party is Neutral
or Unknown)
“Funny thing about the Moathouse… been hearin’ some strange
tales about the ruckus out there. Bandits missin’, gnolls not
showin’ up for pay… That got anything to do with you lot?”
(Wat casually leans against the bar, eyes narrowing
slightly. He’s testing the adventurers to see how much they’ll
reveal.)
Wat’s Offer (If the Party Passes His Test)
“Look, you strike me as the kind that ain’t afraid to get their
hands dirty. You want coin? You want connections? Then you’re
gonna need real friends in this town. Dick Rentsch? Pfft, he’s a
fool. Romag’s clingin’ to power like a drowning man to
driftwood. Me? I work for someone who’s gonna change all
that.”
“The Fire Temple is where the real power is. We got plans,
and you could be a part of them—if you prove yourselves.
There’s a shipment comin’ in, fresh supplies for the Earth
Temple. If you were to… misplace it, well, that’d be a mighty
fine way to get noticed by some important folk.”

The Job – Sabotaging the Earth Temple’s
Supply Line
Wat wants the adventurers to intercept a shipment of
weapons and supplies headed for the Earth Temple.
The caravan is set to arrive under cover of darkness via
a hidden smuggler’s route along the High Road from
Trevil’s Fens Cottage to the Hunting Cottage.
Tactical Choices:
Ambush the Caravan: Lay a trap along the road and
take the supplies by force.
Bribe the Guards: Use gold and persuasion to
convince the Earth Temple’s hired mercenaries to
look the other way.
Steal the Goods: Sneak into the warehouse where
the supplies are being temporarily stored.
Key Challenges:
The guards are expecting trouble will be on high
alert.
If the shipment disappears without a trace, Romag
will suspect treachery and retaliate in Nulb.
If the adventurers botch the mission, Wat will be
furious and may cut ties.
The Aftermath
Success: Wat Rewards the Party
If the adventurers succeed in disrupting the Earth
Temple’s supply line, Wat is impressed.
“Well now, I knew you were the right kind of folk. Let’s just say
this ain’t the last time you’ll hear from us. Alrrem’s got his eye
on Nulb, and if you play your cards right, you might just find
yourselves in his good graces.”
Reward: Gold, stolen supplies, and a potential
audience with Alrrem.
Future Quests Unlocked: More tasks for the Fire
Temple.
Failure: Wat’s Wrath
If the adventurers fail to deliver or get caught by
Romag’s forces, Wat turns hostile.
“I don’t do charity work, friend. You were supposed to be useful.
Now I got problems ‘cause of you. Here’s a word of advice—
don’t show your face ‘round here again.”
Wat cuts off all dealings with the adventurers.
Romag becomes suspicious and may send assassins
after them.
The adventurers lose an opportunity to infiltrate the
Fire Temple.
Expanding the Conflict: Playing the Factions Against
Each Other
The rivalry between Wat (Fire Temple) and Romag
(Earth Temple) is ripe for manipulation. Clever
adventurers could:
Double-cross Wat and warn Romag, earning the
Earth Temple’s favor.
Frame Skole for the theft, turning Romag against his
own ally.
Play both sides, helping Wat while secretly working
for Belsornig.
This quest sets the stage for a larger conflict within
the Temple of Elemental Evil, allowing the adventurers
to manipulate factions, gain influence, or burn
everything down from within.
Gattas Void-Temple Operations
Gattas is a linchpin in the Temple’s network, ensuring
the supply chain from the Moathouse to the Greater
Temple remains uninterrupted.
Coordination with Gefreid Patris: Works closely
with Gefreid to manage the flow of supplies,
prisoners, and loot. Gattas’s raiding parties deliver
resources directly to the Hunting Cottage, where
they are inspected and redirected to the Greater
Temple.
Discretion: Gattas is aware of the need for secrecy
and ensures that raids are conducted far from the
Moathouse.
Political Intrigue
Though loyal to Lareth, Gattas is unaware of the latter’s
covert allegiance to Lolth and partnership with Falrinth.
Potential Manipulation: If the adventurers learn of
Gattas’s ambitions, they could exploit his desire for
advancement to create discord between him and
Lareth.
Rivalries: Gattas harbors resentment toward
Lareth’s preferential treatment of certain others,
including Falrinth and Gefried.
Adventure Hooks
Gattas provides numerous opportunities for adventurers
to disrupt the Temple’s plans.
Intercepting Raids: The party encounters a raiding
party under Gattas’s command, discovering clues
about the Moathouse’s operations.
Infiltration: Adventurers could infiltrate the
Moathouse by posing as recruits or traders, gaining
access to Gattas’s plans.
Creating Division: By sowing discord between
Gattas and other lieutenants, the party can weaken
the Moathouse’s defenses.

=== page 115 ===
Boatman’s Black Market Hall —
Plot Hooks & 1 Featured Quest
Below are drop-in hooks and a full, table-ready caper
that tie the Hall to the rest of Nulb’s web (Waterside,
Wharf Pier, Stables, Hunting Cottage, Mother Screng,
Constable Malvaar, Selentis/Feldrin, Romag, Tolub,
Vesrek, Crimson Reapers, etc.). Keep the tone tight; let
paper, bribes, and knives do the talking.
Quick Plot Hooks (use 3–5 for a session)
“Tithe Runs Red” (Greater Temple audit)
A clerk of Madame Selentis arrives with two brigands.
Play: PCs can pose as assistants (Zilchus jargon) to
help seize contraband “pending Feldrin’s review,” or
flip the audit to freeze a rival’s booth (Reapers,
Tolub’s fence, or Vesrek’s buyer).
Fallout: Favor with Selentis; Romag notes your faces
if you touch Earth cargo.
“Reaper’s Wronged Goods” (fencing war)
A Crimson Reapers runner whispers that Skole’s crew
skimmed their take; a velvet coffer.
Play: Broker a swap, steal it clean, or spark a
Reaper–Skole brawl as cover.
Cross-refs: Waterside (Reaper den), Boatman’s
Tavern (Skole), Wharf Pier (getaway).
Featured Quest: “Chain on the
Long Road”
Boatman’s Black Market Hall • Investigation → Heist •
Levels 3–5
Gattas Void—a hard-eyed runner tied to Lareth’s roadgang—rolls into the Boatman’s Black Market Hall with a
covered wagon after midnight. The haul? Goods lifted
north of Hommlet on the Long Road: trade chests, dye
cakes, bolts of cloth, a jeweler’s coffer. If the party
follows the paper, they can map the bandit logistics
chain from Lareth → Gattas → Nulb fences → either
the Hunting Cottage (Temple) or a pirate skiff.
Why it matters. Returning named goods to Hommlet
wins real allies; exposing the chain lets you turn Nulb’s
factions on each other—and proves the Temple’s supply
web isn’t just rumor.
Starting Clue (pick one to drop)
On the Hall floor: A crate branded double-oak ring
with an H scratch (Hommlet cooper’s mark) and a
green re-stitch twine seam (Earth tell).
Waterside rumor (Pearl): “Gattas Void’s wagon took
the High Road in—Lareth’s boys did the lifting; the
selling happens at the Boatman’s Black Market.”
Constable Malvaar: Receieved a lost-goods notice
from Hommlet (names, marks, partial inventory) and
a promise of paper favors for proof.
Skill nudge: Investigation DC 12 identifies Hommlet
maker’s marks; History DC 10 recalls that Hommlet
brands goods by guild.
Key NPCs
Gattas Void (middleman): Ex-merc with a ledgerbrain; works Lareth’s road hauls for a cut.
Lodriss / Skole (the Hall): Floor boss & enforcer;
they don’t care where it came from if the tithe’s paid.
Dick Rentsch (Waterside): Sometimes buys specific
pieces for Romag.
Gefreid Patris (Hunting Cottage): Receives “useful”
cargo (steel, tools) for the tunnel.
Selentis (for Feldrin): Will interfere if she sniffs a
private sale to Earth/Fire outside her pipe line.
Constable Malvaar: Swaps intel for dock papers.
Scenes & Beats
1. Midnight Delivery (Black Market Hall)
Perception DC 12: note double-oak ring + H brand
on two crates; still bears a Hommlet wax-stamp.
Deception DC 13 (pose as helpers) or Bribe 5–10 gp
to get close and “weigh the lot.”
Sleight of Hand DC 14: lift a route chit or a torn
ledger stub from Gattas’ pouch.
What Gattas says (if pressed lightly):
“Wagon picked clean north of Hommlet. My cut’s earned. After
the weigh, some goes along the river, some goes south to a buyer
who likes tools more than talk.”
2. Follow the Paper (choose a line) Gattas pays Skole,
then hands “tools/ironware” to Dick’s teamster.
Tail check: Stealth DC 13 from Hall → Waterside →
Stables → south lane.
At the Hunting Cottage: use the Zilchus trick (“dual
attestation on restraints / red ring vs blue chit”) to
freeze the intake 1–2 hours while you:
copy crate tallies (Forgery Kit or Sleight of
Hand DC 14).
swap a crate tag to reroute it back to town.
3. Proving the Chain You need two of three to convince
Hommlet/Constable (or to blackmail a faction):
Mark match: a branded crate, bolt-stamp, or
jeweler’s chiselled cipher matching the lost-goods
notice.
Chain link: a Hall ledger stub with Gattas’ mark and
lot weights plus a route chit (Hall → Stables/Wharf).
Temple junction: an intake tally from the Hunting
Cottage or a signed hold/UNVERIFIED slip bearing
your audit notes.
Skill: Investigation DC 12 to collate; Persuasion DC
13 to sell it as a packet to Malvaar or Hommlet
agents.
Clean Success: You compile marks + ledger stub +
route chit. Constable Malvaar issues sealed papers;
Hommlet sends a quiet agent to reclaim crates.

=== page 116 ===
Boatman’s Warehouse “Marks in
the Dust, Knives in the Ledger”
Investigation → Infiltration • Levels 3–5 • Focus:
contraband stolen off Viscounty/Gnarley roads
A merchant from Hommlet swears their caravan was
hit north of town. Two days later, crate brands and boltstamps matching that caravan show up on the floor of
the Boatman’s Warehouse. If the party can prove
provenance and trace the handling chain (who took
what, when, and for whom), they can return goods, flip
factions, or choke a vein of Temple commerce.
Why Now
Fresh pull from the Low/Long Roads and Gnarley trails
is on the boards for same-night turnover—red-tagged
lots being hoisted to the second floor.
Short-staffed floor: Lodriss’s own thugs man the
crane and the stair, but Skole’s wider market crew is
thin and distracted.
Basement whispers: a caged voice begs for help; a
second swears they saw a patron’s crest on a crate.
Cast & Motives
Lodriss, smiling knife: keep flow steady, keep Skole
useful, keep Tolub paying.
Skole, proprietor: balance pirates, bandits, and
buyers; no raids on his floor.
Madame Selentis, tithe/audit: hates “private” sales;
arrives with ledgers and red ribbons. (Pairs with
Reapers in the basement.)
Captain Tolub, Water’s fist: clear floor space, unload
fast, get “the chest” upstairs. Belsornig wants proof
of control.
Approaches (pick 1–2 to spotlight)
1. Paper & Nerve (Social Heist) Pass as tally-hands;
freeze a line with “UNVERIFIED” to stall 1 hour
(copy weights, lift route chits, plant a counterfeit
seal).
2. Quiet Hands (Stealth) Shadow a push-team from the
pier; chalk tiny sigils on suspect crates; slip a band to
reveal hidden wax-marks.
3. Loud-but-Legal (Weaponize the Audit) Tip Selentis:
“private sales” here tonight. Ride her seizure to
legally cordon a rival stack; extract stubs while
everyone argues.
4. Smash & Scatter (Force) Drop the crane pallet
(hazard!), kick doors to the market, and race the
Reapers to the basement cages. (Signal the pier
watch or you’ll get boxed.)
The Floor, Fast
Pier Doors to wagons and barges; interior doors to
tavern/market; rickety stair to a gallery and locked
cache (trapped); stone stair to the contraband vault and
secret prisoner room.
Evidence PCs Can Pull (choose 3+)
Provenance: wax seals/brands
(Dyvers/Verbobonc/Hommlet), counterfeit guild
marks, “Tolub’s Mark” on grain alcohol; “Crone’s
Tooth” pirate bark tag.
Chain Link: intake weights, handler initials (S / L),
route chits (Hall→Wharf / back-wagon at dawn).
Disposition: red-ring/Temple-bound crate list
upstairs; basement cages tagged for “Vesrek”
transfer.
Escalation Tracks
(tick when PCs blunder, stall, or make noise)
Noise (0–3)
0: Side-eye and mutters.
1: “Drifting” toughs fill aisles; coded knocks.
2: Crane lookout posts; pier doors half-barred.
3: All doors barred; only “ledger names” move;
basement guard doubles.
Tithe/Audit (0–2)
0: “Where’s the clerk?” grumbling.
1: Selentis arrives with ledgers & seals—“audit.”
2: Red ribbons hit anything untagged; seized stacks
become a wall you must talk or cut through.
Pirates (0–2)
0: Tolub’s crew demands floor space—“make a lane.”
1: A runner: “Belsornig wants his chest now.”
2: Pirates shoulder through; a Water agent claims
cargo—no delays, no witnesses.
Complications (pick 1–2)
Skole Walks the Aisle. Cold smile, warm cudgel.
Hold your nerve or he locks the doors and “counts
heads.”
Audit Cross-Fire. If PCs utter “private sale,” Selentis
seizes a stack that the party needs—great cover, new
obstacle.
Reaper Shadow. A basement enforcer tails anyone
fixated on ledgers; if made, he runs to the Waterside
with a warning.
Outcomes & Fallout
Clean Proof, Clean Exit: Deliver provenance + chain
link to Hommlet/Constable allies; earn coin,
bridge/dock papers, and future favors. (Temple
attention rises.)
Rescue & Reveal: Free captives; expose a noble’s
letters from the upstairs cache; gain leverage over a
Viscounty house.
Choke the Vein: Blow the audit wide open or torch
seized stacks; Lodriss retaliates, Water blames
Earth, and Nulb tilts toward open turf war.
